1935.03.27

Unfinished River Works to be Handed Over to Kong and Li; Hu Yuanhui Departs Work Site; Qi Shou'an Oversees Reinforcement of Taihang Dike; Shouzhang County Seat Surrounded by Water

(Tianjin) Hu Yuanhui telegraphed Tianjin stating he has departed the Yellow River construction site and arrived in Handan on the 25th. He is expected to return to Tianjin by the 28th. All unfinished work matters will be handed over to Li Yizhi and Kong Xianrong. The Yellow River Disaster Relief Committee telegraphed nine counties in southern Hebei, including Changyuan, Puyang, Qingfeng, Nanle, and Daming, to assist the Central Yellow River Engineering Bureau in diligently repairing the Jin Dike and completing it before the flood season to ensure the safety of southern Hebei. A separate telegram was sent to the Changyuan County Magistrate, instructing him to inform the public that the Guantai breach closure project and the construction of the Jin Dike will continue to be handled by the Central Government to satisfy public expectations. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

(Tianjin) Changyuan County Magistrate Zhang Qinglu telegraphed the province stating that the Yellow River's water level remains unchanged, but the wind remains strong, with whitecaps rising several feet high, impacting the bank and eroding the revetments increasingly. The Taihang Dike is currently being overseen by River Bureau Director Qi Shou'an, who is stationed there to supervise the emergency repairs. The Ying Shui dam outside Changyuan's east gate is awaiting materials before construction can begin immediately. The water depth outside the city remains above eight feet. The Hebei Yellow River Disaster Relief Association telegraphed the Changyuan County Magistrate on the 26th stating that 10,000 sandbags have been purchased and handed over to the railway bureau for transport to Daokou. Personnel should be dispatched immediately to receive and use them. Another telegram was sent to the Changyuan County Magistrate stating that the disaster relief porridge kitchens will be closed starting April 1st, and millet will be distributed instead, for a period of two months, with a total budget of 13,000 yuan. 6,000 yuan was wired in advance by the Bank of China on the 26th for immediate use. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

(Kaifeng) Has accompanied by Wu Xiufeng, Zhang Junqi, and others, arrived in Bian at around 11 PM on the 25th and stayed at the Jintai Hotel. On the 26th, they visited local authorities and heads of various water conservancy organizations, and it was decided that they would depart for Han on the 27th. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

(Jinan) River Bureau Director Zhang Lianjia is scheduled to depart for Yu early on the 27th to discuss repairing the Jin Dike. Currently, the Guantai breach is taking 60% of the main flow, and the Shouzhang County seat has already been surrounded by water. The provincial government has allocated 150,000 yuan for emergency repairs to the people's dikes in nine counties along the upstream south bank and midstream north bank, and to prepare stone materials for emergency repairs to the Jin Dike. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

(Jinan) The provincial government council today approved an order instructing the militia commander Zhao Mingyuan to supervise river affairs personnel in quickly blocking the Luanjingzi breach on the north bank of the lower Yellow River in Lijin County, and to repair 50 li of people's dikes on both banks near the estuary, channeling the water to scour the sand and facilitate drainage, thereby protecting the reclaimed area. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

(Kaifeng) The Yellow River Conference has drafted a work plan: 1. To construct a small new dike revetment project in Lanfeng to prevent the river from reverting to its old course; 2. To construct a revetment project from the Qin River estuary to the Jiubao Thirteen Dams to prevent the river from flowing towards the Zhang and Wei Rivers; 3. To repair the Zhukou to Shili South Dike; 4. To connect the Huayang Dike; 5. To construct a revetment project for the Zhongmou Dike. A total of one million yuan is needed. A special telegram was sent to summon the River Affairs Bureau Directors of Hebei, Shandong, and Henan provinces to a meeting in Bian on the 28th. The Economic Commission has dispatched Zheng Zhaojing, Deputy Director of the Water Conservancy Department, to attend and provide guidance. Li Yizhi returned to Bian from Shaanxi on the 26th to preside over the meeting. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 26th)

(Xi'an) Due to the urgency of the Yellow River breach closure project, Li Yizhi departed Tongguan for Bian on the evening of the 26th and will proceed to Puyang to supervise the work. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 26th)

The Economic Commission No Longer Participating in the Salachi Irrigation Project; Explanation of Reasons

(Nanjing) The National Economic Commission issued the following statement today: "The Commission's decision to cease participation in the Salachi irrigation project in Suiyuan Province has elicited external criticism. Therefore, we hereby state the reasons as follows: The Salachi irrigation project in Suiyuan began in the 17th year of the Republic [1928]. The following year, due to severe droughts in various provinces, the China International Famine Relief Commission urgently sought to provide work for disaster victims and consequently loaned funds to the Suiyuan Provincial Government and oversaw the project. By the 21st year [1932], the Relief Commission deemed its mission complete and transferred the responsibility of management to a mixed committee jointly formed by the Provincial Government and local groups affiliated with the Commission. The project cost a total of 860,000 yuan at the time. However, the actual results were quite disappointing, and it was understood that even more capital would be needed to achieve greater benefits. Therefore, in January of the 23rd year [1934], the Suiyuan Provincial Government requested assistance from this Commission. As the Commission's purpose is to assist economically sound enterprises, it immediately began studying the Salachi project's engineering status and the necessity of expanding it. However, due to a lack of reference materials, progress was difficult. It was subsequently learned that when the project began, the local topography had not been thoroughly surveyed, and the Yellow River's water volume as a source of irrigation had not been deeply studied. Therefore, in the summer and autumn of the 23rd year, this Commission specially sent personnel to Sa to conduct an investigation and sought the opinion of the League of Nations Technical Cooperation Engineering Committee. Committee members such as Walmodou were all hydraulic experts. Mr. Walmodou and construction engineering expert Sa Douli personally went to Sa from December 12th to 26th of last year to conduct an inspection. Upon returning to Beiping, they thoroughly discussed the matter with all related parties. By this time, the Commission's investigation had also been completed. After consulting with the League of Nations experts upon Mr. Walmodou's return to Beijing, they unanimously recommended ceasing participation. The Commission's decision was originally based on this detailed investigation and the advice of impartial experts. As for the technical report, it will be published when the League of Nations experts return to Geneva, sometime this summer." (Guomin News Agency Dispatch, 25th)

Sui-Mongol Tax Dispute; Opinions Gradually Converging; Fu Zuoyi Refutes Various Points Stated by Prince De

(Beiping) Regarding the Sui-Mongol tax dispute, Sui representatives Li Zhizheng and Shi Huayan visited He Yingqin twice yesterday to seek instructions on everything. They also visited Song Zheyuan multiple times yesterday and today for discussions. Opinions from all parties are gradually converging, and formal consultations are expected in the coming days. Fu Zuoyi also sent a telegram to He, refuting various points stated by Prince De. The original text was over 700 characters, and the gist is as follows: (1) The Mongol Political Council is responsible for handling local autonomous government affairs of various leagues and banners. That is, the autonomous system is subordinate to the Council, while the administrative system is subordinate to the Executive Yuan's Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, the Provincial Government, etc. (2) The seventh article of the principles of autonomy stipulates that a certain percentage of various local taxes collected by the province and counties in the leagues and banners must be allocated to the leagues and banners. It is clearly stipulated that the province and counties can collect local taxes in the Mongol territories. However, the Council mistakenly interprets this as meaning that the province and counties have no right to establish checkpoints in the Mongol territories and even claims that if counties have been established and local taxes are collected, a certain percentage must still be allocated to the Mongols, which is a misunderstanding of the facts. Moreover, the allocation is for the league and banner governments, not the Mongol Political Council. (3) The eighth article of the principles of autonomy states that no new counties or administrative bureaus will be established in the leagues and banners in the future. This is a principled regulation regarding the establishment of new counties and has nothing to do with the issue of tax allocation. Furthermore, the stationing of troops is for national defense and bandit suppression, and the Council has no right to interfere. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

(Beiping) He [Yingqin] is scheduled to host a banquet for Mongol and Sui representatives Li Zhizheng, Shi Huayan, and Bao Yueqing tomorrow evening, uniting the prestige of all parties. Song Zheyuan is scheduled to return to Cha tomorrow afternoon, accompanied by Qin Dechun and Xiao Zhenying. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

(Taiyuan) Prince De sent Mongol Political Council member and prince Guoer Zhuoerzhapu to Mount Wutai to pay respects to Zhangjia Buddha, report on the recent situation of Mongol politics, and urge him to return to Mongolia. Zhang is scheduled to leave Mount Wutai the day after tomorrow and first go to Ping. Various Mongol princes and important officials have been flocking to Mount Wutai to offer incense recently. Prince Suo visited the Bingyuan Northwest Company's various factories today. Zhu Jia and others all visited the hotel to meet with him. Prince Suo presented cabinet with twelve fine horses, which have already been transported to Bing yesterday. Yan [Xishan] reciprocated by giving Prince Suo many kinds of local products as gifts, and personnel have already been dispatched to transport them to Cha. Prince Suo has decided to go to Ping the day after tomorrow. The Zhengtai and Pinghan railway bureaus have both prepared special trains. Prince Suo dispatched personnel to Shizhuang today to prepare everything. Prince A is currently traveling from Sui to Ping and is scheduled to come to Bing within the next few days to visit Mount Wutai. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

(Beiping) Alatan Oqir, Deputy League Leader of Yike Zhao and member of the Mongol Political Council, arrived in Ping from Sui at 6 PM on the afternoon of the 26th with his family and over ten attendants. Fu Zuoyi's representative Ma Ren and Shi Huayan's representative Kang Guoping, as well as Zhang Zirong, section chief of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission's Beiping office, and over twenty others welcomed him at the station. Alatan Oqir told reporters at the station that he was here to visit Chairman He [Yingqin] and present his views on the Sui-Mongol tax issue. The Mongol Council has decided to obey the Central Government on this matter. He himself will stay in Beiping for two weeks before returning to Sui. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 26th)

(Beiping) The Mongol-Sui tax dispute has been discussed repeatedly in Ping, and the opinions of both sides have gradually converged. Both sides are currently seeking instructions from their superiors. Shi Huayan and Li Zhizheng visited Mo Zheyuan and Xiao Zhenying again on the morning of the 26th to discuss everything. After receiving replies and expressions of opinion from all parties, the two sides will formally consult again to discuss specific measures. It is expected that a resolution will be reached soon. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 26th)

General Budget for the 24th Year [1935] Begins Compilation and Review

(Nanjing) The plan for the general budget of the 24th year [1935] has begun compilation and review. For the expenditure portion of the 24th year, with the exception of the pension fees item, which is difficult to reduce, both the recurring expenses and the project expenses items will be reduced. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

Disobedient Militia in Yutian Defeated by Security Forces; Wang Chengzhu's Troops Forced to Withdraw; Zhou Yuying Increases Troop Deployment for Joint Defense; Yin Rugeng and Yi Wo Go to Handle the Matter

(Tianjin) The conflict between the Yutian security forces and the militia began early on the 25th. Zhou Yuying's troops, with a battalion of 600 soldiers, launched an attack on the illegal militia of Wang Jizong in three routes on the night of the 24th: one team taking Lin Nancang Town, one team surrounding Ya Hongqiao, and one team surrounding Zhushu Wu. The four city gates have been tightly closed since the night of the 24th, and pedestrians are being inspected during the day. The illegal militia occupied various locations, including Liujiaqiao, Ya Hongqiao, Lin Nancang Bo, Zhushu Wu, and Zhao Jiapu, and built solid trenches to resist. Gunfire erupted early on the 25th, and contact occurred simultaneously in various towns and villages. Residents fled one after another. Traffic between inside and outside the city and between Zunhua, Tangshan, Yutian, and Fengrun was cut off. Telegraph and telephone lines were all out of service. Wang Jizong led 1700 men to occupy Ya Hongqiao, engaging in fierce fighting with Zhou Yuying's main force. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

(Tianjin) Zhou Yuying's Security Third Regiment has increased the deployment of a battalion to Yutian for joint defense, which has been agreed to by the Japanese side. It arrived in Yutian from Funing on the 25th. Yin Rugeng negotiated with the Tianjin Japanese Army Headquarters to transport eight heavy machine guns to Yutian for use by Zhou Yuying's troops. They have already been transported. At 2:40 PM on the 25th, Yin Rugeng and Senior Staff Officer Obokura Yoshiyuki of the Tianjin Japanese Army arrived in Tangshan together. Yi Wo, Chief of the Shanhaiguan Japanese Special Service Agency, also arrived in Tangshan at 9:45 AM on the 25th. Tao Shangming hosted them at the Commissioner's Office on the evening of the 25th. On the morning of the 26th, they took a long-distance bus to Yutian to monitor Zhou Yuying's troops' resolution of Wang Jizong's illegal militia. They will then travel to Tong County on the 28th or so to investigate the current status of the reorganization of Li Yunshang's security forces. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

(Tianjin) The battles in Ya Hongqiao and Lin Nancang Bo have ceased. On the afternoon of the 25th, Wang Jizong's troops and Liu Guitang's bandits suffered heavy casualties under the fierce attack of the security forces. A large fire raged in Ya Hong Town. Wang could not resist and led his troops to break through the encirclement and retreat to Qianjiagou, on the border of Fengrun and Yutian counties, where they dug trenches to defend. Liu Guitang's bandits retreated towards Liujiaqiao and Zhao Jiapu. The security forces split up to pursue. Zhou Yuying's troops, newly arrived from Wenning and Xinkai, have dispatched a portion of their forces to pursue and suppress in all directions. Militias have been dispatched to garrison the borders of Fengrun, Yutian, Tangshan, and Zunhua to prevent Wang Jizong's troops from fleeing into them. The Yutian Post Office's statistics show that the Security Supplementary Force stationed in the county for the past year extorted a total of 1,267,000 yuan in property from wealthy households and remitted it abroad. Of these remittances, those made by Japanese and Korean drug trading firms totaled 100,000 yuan, the most. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

(Beiping) The War Zone Clearing Committee will convene a regular meeting tomorrow morning to discuss methods for reorganizing security forces and militias, as well as bandit suppression issues. Notices were issued today. With the exception of Yin Rugeng, who is not in Ping, all other commissioners will attend. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

(Beiping) After arriving in Tangshan from Tianjin yesterday, Yin Rugeng is scheduled to go to Yutian today. Staff Officer Obokura of the Tianjin-based Japanese Army and Yi Wo, chief of the Japanese Special Service Agency in Yushu, will also go with him. Yin and others will stay in Yutian for several days to be responsible for handling the reorganization of the militia. After inspecting places like Xiadian and Yanjiao, they will return to Ping. Related sources said that over a hundred bandits from Zunhua had fled into Qian'an County yesterday. Wang Chengzhu's troops from the Ya Hongqiao militia were disarmed by Zhou Yuying's security forces and were forced to withdraw the night before last. In this battle, four security force members were killed and thirteen were injured. They are currently being tracked and encircled. A portion of the rebel Ya Hongqiao militia, about two hundred men, have fled into the Jingyu area of Zunhua County and have been surrounded by security forces and militias, making them easy to deal with. A small portion of the rebel Ya Hongqiao militia has also been discovered in Fengrun County, and security forces and militias have been dispatched to intercept them. Tong County has temporarily declared martial law for the past two days to prevent bandits from fleeing into the area. Dozens of bandits were discovered in Wanggezhuang in Shunyi County yesterday and can be easily dealt with. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

Kailuan Miners' Conflict

(Tianjin) Five hundred workers at the Kailuan Zhaogezhuang Tianqiao, because they were prevented from working by the force of the contractor's hired gangsters, causing the miners underground to be unable to transport coal out, also declared a strike on the evening of the 24th. On the morning of the 25th, hundreds of Tianqiao workers, armed with weapons, clashed with the contractor's hired gangsters. As a result, seven or eight people were killed or injured on both sides. A police brigade arrived and used force to mediate before the crowd dispersed. The Tianqiao workers demanded that the system of workers contracting work for themselves not be abolished, and that the mining bureau compensate them for the wages of the days they were prevented from working. On the evening of the 25th, the crowd gathered and surrounded the mining area's Third Police Station. They dispersed only after the station made great efforts to persuade them. Yu Xifan of the Tangshan Public Security Bureau rushed to the scene on the morning of the 25th with Chief Inspector Li Jianzhang to handle the matter, and telegraphed the mining bureau to quickly dispatch important officials to assist. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

(Tianjin) The Zhaogezhuang miners' unrest has subsided. After Yu Xifan's persuasion, he took responsibility for accepting the workers' conditions on behalf of the mining bureau and absolutely guaranteed that the system of workers contracting work for themselves would not be abolished. The workers agreed to resume work at 6 AM on the 26th, but demanded that the conditions be fully implemented within three days, otherwise they would go on strike again. The Third Police Station of the Zhaogezhuang Mine Police arrested six counter-revolutionary elements who were inciting workers to strike for a long time. They were sent to the Tangshan Public Security Bureau on the 26th for interrogation. The Kailuan Mining Area Police Team, under the provincial order, will be reorganized on April 1st into the Kailuan Mining Industry Police Headquarters, with Yu Xifan as the Director and Wei Dong, recommended by the Kailuan Mining Bureau, as the Deputy Director. Each station will be renamed a branch, with each branch having four police squads of forty men per squad. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

Kong Xiangxi Discusses the Situation of Financial Relief

(Nanjing) Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi received British Ambassador Cadogan at 5 PM on the afternoon of the 26th and talked for about twenty minutes. Someone met with Kong and inquired about the situation of China's contact with international parties to borrow funds, and the issuance of 100 million yuan in financial public bonds by the central government. Kong Xiangxi replied that in recent years, due to the dumping policies adopted by various countries in China, the interior has experienced banditry and natural disasters, rural areas have gone bankrupt, finance has been depleted, and both export and import trade have declined. Recently, the financial situation has become even more dangerous due to the impact of the US silver policy. In order to stabilize finance and seek to restore foreign trade, the central government has contacted various countries to borrow funds in order to save the situation. The contact is still ongoing. The status of all the contact is not yet at the stage for release. As for yesterday's news from London, that the Chinese government is seeking to borrow ten million pounds in British gold from the British government, this matter is obviously true. Kong continued, "At a time when the central government's military, administrative, and political expenses are strained, the central government is issuing 100 million yuan in financial public bonds to stabilize society and revitalize industry and commerce. I have been in Shanghai for several days to contact the responsible persons of the Central Bank and other banks. All banks have expressed their agreement with the government's move. In the future, the financial issue will gradually move onto the right track." (Special Dispatch, 26th)

Ministry of Finance Orders Sichuan Transportation Commissioner to Reorganize Sichuan Province's Salt Affairs

(Nanjing) On the 26th, the Ministry of Finance ordered the Sichuan Salt Transportation Commissioner to reorganize salt affairs in Sichuan Province, to dredge the Sichuan salt sales routes during the communist suppression period, stabilize the workers, and avoid stockpiling the products. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance has rejected the request of Sichuan salt merchants to designate the Chu bank as the exclusive sales area for Sichuan salt, and has instructed the promotion of Sichuan salt sales in two areas: (1) expanding sales in southern Sichuan and western Kang; (2) abolishing the salt surcharges imposed in the previous defense areas by a certain date. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 26th)

Judicial Yuan Interprets Ambiguity in Sealed Property

(Nanjing) The Judicial Yuan now interprets the ambiguity of whether the national tax authority obtains priority of payment when sealing the property of a tax defaulter as follows: An administrative agency, based on the function of its administrative power, sealing the property of the people, and a court, based on the request of a party, implementing a provisional attachment on the property of a debtor, are two different things. If a court implements a provisional attachment on property that has already been sealed by an administrative agency, it is implementing it on property other than the purpose of the administrative agency's sealing. In the future, when this provisionally attached property is used for distribution, even if there are many creditors, they can only handle it within the scope of their attachment. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 26th)

Zhang Fakui Visits Mausoleum Yesterday

(Nanjing) Zhang Fakui led his entourage to visit the mausoleum on the morning of the 26th. He was guided by Ma Xiang to the auditorium, performed all the rites, and returned. Zhang said that he had traveled around Europe and the United States earlier this year, visiting 22 countries. He resided in London and Paris for a longer period of time. In all the countries he visited, he saw that they spared no effort in preparing for national defense. Germany's national defense equipment was especially advanced, and the entire country had become militarized. Recently, Germany's cancellation of the military clauses of the Treaty of Versailles and the implementation of compulsory military service have made the European situation particularly uneasy. However, since the Great War, all countries have felt the danger of war. The majority of Europeans psychologically desire peace. To say that a second world war is about to break out seems premature, because today's European powers are actively expanding their armies on the one hand and advocating disarmament on the other hand, a contradictory phenomenon. As for China's future path, the only way forward is to strive for unity from top to bottom and to work hard. Zhang will fly to Chongqing after receiving a reply telegram from Chairman Chiang. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

Ancient Boat Discovered in Huaiyin, Excavated by Huai River Workers on the Banks of the Abandoned Yellow River

Huaiyin: An ancient boat has recently been excavated by Huai River workers in the eastern section of the enemy embankment in Yangzhuang, Huaiyin County, on the banks of the abandoned Yellow River. Several pieces of ancient porcelain were found next to the boat's planks, but no human bones were found. According to archaeologists, the boat may have been submerged in the soil when the Yellow River diverted its course south to seize the Huai River during the early Yuan Dynasty, and it has only appeared now after more than 600 years. (Special Dispatch on the 26th)

Current Commentary

The Issue of Reducing the Transit and Export Taxes

— Liu

Recently, the Ministry of Finance has a plan to abolish transit taxes and reduce or exempt export taxes, which has been passed by the Central Political Council. (See the conversation between Minister Kong and the Central News Agency reporter.) This is indeed a measure that we have been longing for, and it is also the most essential and wisest. Without a solution to the trade deficit, the outflow of currency cannot be stopped. In the face of fierce international commercial competition, other countries are using managed trade, devalued currencies, and high tariffs to block imports and promote exports. Yet we still have transit taxes and export taxes, creating layers of obstacles to the development of export trade. How can we avoid a complete defeat and an increase in the trade deficit? At the annual meeting of the American Chamber of Commerce this year, Mr. Basha once said: "The Chinese government never considers exporters and often hinders the efforts of merchants to promote Chinese exports by increasing taxes and export duties. Although the development of export trade can provide jobs for tens of thousands of Chinese people and bring new capital into China, China does not make it its business to encourage this." Now that our government has paid attention to this, how can our industrialists and businessmen not be delighted?

Export taxes were originally levied for the sake of fiscal revenue. In earlier years, there were also two types of taxes: re-import tax and inland transit tax. These were abolished starting in January of the 20th year of the Republic. The current export tariff also grants tax-free exports to goods that were once important in exports but are now gradually declining, as well as emerging industrial products that need protection. Looking at the tariff schedule, there are about 38 categories listed below. The numbers listed in the table are the item numbers in the export tariff.

46 Broad beans, 48 Sorghum, 49 Maize, 50 Millet

51 Rice, 53 Wheat, 54 Unlisted miscellaneous grains, 23 Black tea

123 Brick tea, 124 Green tea, 125 Tea dust, 126 Raw tea

127 Scented tea, 128 Tea leaves, 129 Tea stalks, 130 Unlisted tea

180 Doupion silk, 181 White silk, 182 Gray silk, 183 Yellow silk

184 Waste silk, 186 Silk floss, 192 Cotton socks, 196 Drawn work, etc.

197 Lace, 199 Spun silk yarn, 204 Satin, 205 Tussah silk

222 Silk clothing, 217 Foreign currency, 250 Books, 251 Paintings

252 Various publications, 254 Straw hats, etc., 257 Packaging containers, 262 Hairnets

264 Umbrellas, 266 Lacquerware

According to recent news, the abolition of the transit tax seems inevitable, and a supplementary plan has been drafted and is under review. As for how to reduce or exempt export taxes, the details have not yet been revealed. In my opinion, the position of export taxes in the customs revenue has been gradually declining in recent years due to the decline in exports, from 47.831 million yuan in the 20th year of the Republic to 23.245 million yuan, and there has been no sign of recovery. In the past two years, it has not even reached 10% of the import tax amount. The following table shows the general situation. (Unit: thousands of national currency)

Import Tax, Export Tax, Transit Tax

20th Year of the Republic: 314,686 47,831 15,646

21st Year of the Republic: 236,291 26,777 20,552

22nd Year of the Republic: 265,611 23,245 18,003

23rd Year of the Republic: 261,021 24,700 16,900

Since export taxes are an obstacle to foreign exports, and their value is very small in the total tax revenue, even if they are completely abolished, although it will reduce a source of income for the treasury, who knows if it will not increase the national wealth? If it is difficult to completely abolish both taxes at once, then all goods that occupy an important position in current exports, except those that are necessary for the country or are special products of the country, should be granted tax exemption. If egg products have decreased significantly in exports in recent years, and soybeans and soybean cakes no longer have a position in export commodities, and tung oil and cotton have also declined, if no urgent remedy is sought, failure can be expected immediately. According to the International Trade Guide (Volume 7, Number 3), the percentage of the value of export commodities in the 23rd year of the Republic (as a percentage of the total export value of that year) is listed in the following order to see the general trend of export goods.

(1) Tea 6.74%, (2) Cotton yarn 5.85%, (3) Metals 5.74%

(4) Egg products 5.65%, (5) Hides 5.44%, (6) Raw silk 5.31%

(7) Tung oil 4.90%, (8) Silk fabrics 3.64%, (9) Cotton 2.84%

(10) Hog bristles 2.83%, (11) Wool 2.43%, (12) Peanuts 2.31%

(13) Medicinal materials 1.89%, (14) Tobacco 1.76%, (15) Cotton cloth 1.64%

(16) Other 41.03%

Except for items (1), (6), and (8) in the table, which are already tax-exempt, the rest, such as cotton yarn, cotton cloth, coarse and fine ramie cloth, eggs and their products, peanuts, tanned leather, hides, bristles, tung oil, tea oil, cotton, tobacco, dried and fresh vegetables, medicinal materials, spices, and various carpets and rugs, are still subject to taxation. There are certainly many other products that need to be reduced or exempted. Now that the financial authorities are in the process of deliberation, they will surely implement it as soon as possible to comfort the eager expectations of the industrial and commercial sectors. Import taxes should also be increased at the same time to compensate for the losses. (If the tax rate is increased by 10%, it can offset the losses from the complete exemption of export and transit taxes.) If export taxes are abolished, import taxes are increased, and the industrial and commercial sectors can work hard to improve and seek the development of their own businesses, there may be hope for economic recovery.

League of Nations Health Expert Dr. Stampar Arrives in Nanjing Yesterday

(Nanjing) Dr. Stampar, a health expert from the League of Nations and an advisor to the Economic Committee, was sent to Shaanxi, Gansu, Ningxia, and Qinghai to assist in the construction of health undertakings, with remarkable results. Jiangsu Province Improves Pawnbroking Industry; Design Council Decides to Discuss in Groups

The London Times Discusses the Mongolian Issue

(London) The Times published an editorial today titled "The Revival of Mongolian Nationalism," discussing the existing triangular competition in Mongolia, saying that the Russians have more experience in Mongolia and the climate is more suitable, which is not something the Japanese can match, so they can have an advantage. Japanese Response to Britain on the Oil Monopoly Issue

(Tokyo) According to semi-official sources, the Japanese government yesterday responded to the British government's protest of November 24 last year regarding the oil monopoly rights in Manchuria, stating, "From Japan's point of view, the establishment of the oil monopoly rights by 'Manchukuo' is not considered to violate any treaties or violate its declaration of the Open Door Policy. The United Kingdom completely disregards the reality of 'Manchukuo's' independence, but also cites the part of 'Manchukuo's' declaration that is beneficial to the United Kingdom's argument. In any case, the Japanese government cannot agree to any theory that makes Japan responsible for 'Manchukuo's' actions, nor can it accept any opinions based on non-recognition of 'Manchukuo.' Japan is prepared to mediate, but cannot interfere in 'Manchukuo's' internal affairs." (Reuters Telegram on the 26th)

Russian Students Plot to Set Fire to and Destroy Harbin Institute of Technology

Anglo-German Continued Talks: Hitler Clarifies Stance, Opposes Eastern and Central European Pacts, Conditions Attached to Returning to the League of Nations, Yesterday's Talks Focused on Armaments

(Berlin) France has appealed to the League of Nations regarding Germany's rearmament. If dealt with satisfactorily, Germany may return to the League. Germany views its army and navy size as still negotiable under certain circumstances. This is reportedly Hitler's direct response today to British Foreign Secretary Simon and Minister Eden's inquiries. According to well-informed sources, Hitler today extensively explained certain points of German foreign policy, particularly opposition to Eastern European and Danube River pacts. He also emphatically stated Germany's commitment to peace and willingness to cooperate in easing tensions in Europe. However, he did not elaborate much on the issue of German rearmament and its compulsory military service plans. Talks will continue tomorrow morning at 10:00 AM, when Germany's army and navy size and the possibility of Germany returning to the League of Nations will be discussed in detail. There will be no sensational announcements before Simon departs. People in Berlin believe that other countries now need to work hard before any final resolution of major issues can be announced. (Reuters, 25th)

Yesterday Morning's Meeting

(Berlin) The British and German authorities continued their meeting at 10:30 this morning, with the issue of armaments as the main point of discussion. The British side was still represented by Foreign Secretary Simon and Lord Privy Seal Eden. British Ambassador to Berlin, Phipps, also attended. Simon looked well after yesterday's efforts. The German side was still represented by Hitler, assisted by Foreign Minister Neurath and Special Envoy for Disarmament, General Ribbentrop.

Armaments as Main Topic

(Berlin) Anglo-German talks temporarily stopped at 1:20 PM. The British and German cabinet members all attended a luncheon at the British Embassy. Chancellor Hitler also personally participated. After the lunch, talks continued. According to information obtained by our correspondent, today's talks involved various issues related to the army, navy, and air force. British sources have summarized Chancellor Hitler's proposals, stating that if all countries completely disarm uniformly, Germany will do the same. If one country refuses to disarm, Germany must expand its armaments as much as possible. The size of the German army is set at 36 divisions, which is a common basis for distribution among countries, but the number of officers is not.

Germany Adopts a Two-Pronged Approach

Regarding the armaments issue, Germany will decide on any restrictions to its own plans based on the actions of other countries. Germany suggested to the British representatives that the main points of German foreign policy and its constructive proposals should be compiled by Hitler into a written memorandum. It is widely believed that Hitler's position on the armaments issue is that if all countries implement disarmament, Germany is willing to follow suit. If a country begins to expand its armaments, Germany will do the same. Regarding naval issues, it is reported that Hitler stated that the extent of Germany's naval rearmament, no matter what, requires several years of effort. The British side anticipates that Germany intends to shift the responsibility for the arms race onto the British negotiators. Therefore, they adopted a two-pronged approach in today's talks, consisting of three steps. The scale is very large, namely: (1) Hitler does not insist on the naval rearmament request, and the so-called 400,000 tons of navy is not a definite figure. (2) Hitler firmly supports the Air Pact, thereby proving that the German air force has the reason to be equal to the largest air force country. (3) Since the air force can be equal, the army and navy should be handled accordingly. As for Germany's proposed guarantee pact, senior British officials believe that it contains significant dangers, as this type of guarantee system could protect some of Germany's neighbors from aggression, while others may suffer as a result. (Havas, 26th)

No Concessions on Russian Armaments

It is reported that after discussing the situation of Soviet Russian armaments this morning, Hitler stated that unless Russia promises (1) to transfer the main part of its western border military force to the Far East and (2) to reduce its troop numbers, Germany cannot make major concessions on armaments.

Talks Not Proceeding Smoothly

Talks will continue at 4:00 PM this afternoon. It is reported that this morning's talks were far less smooth than yesterday's. Hitler did not seem to offer any special suggestions on the armaments issue.

Today's discussions will proceed according to the following guidelines:

(1) Eastern European Pact: Germany is unwilling to join the current form of the pact or is willing to conclude several regional pacts in accordance with the Polish-German agreement.

(2) Memel: Germany can conclude a non-aggression pact with Lithuania, provided that Lithuania adheres to the Memel Statute regarding the German minority.

(3) League of Nations: If France's lawsuit against Germany's rearmament to the League of Nations can be resolved satisfactorily, Germany is willing to return to the League of Nations.

(4) Armaments: The size of the German army, navy, and air force can be negotiated in London. (Reuters, 26th)

Counterproposal to Eastern European Pact

(Berlin) During this morning's talks between British and German representatives, the German side refused to conclude the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact and proposed a counterproposal, advocating that countries bordering each other conclude non-aggression pacts, and that other countries conclude guarantee pacts. British cabinet members were quite surprised by Germany's counterproposal, which they found self-contradictory and ambiguous, and reportedly requested Head of State Hitler to explain its outline in writing. (Havas, 26th)

Britain Strictly Prevents Information Leaks

It is reported that this morning's meeting focused on armaments and disarmament issues. Simon and Eden looked stern when they left the meeting. After lunch, the two stayed at the embassy for some time to talk deeply with Ambassador Phipps. The British representatives are now strictly on guard to prevent the leakage of information from the talks. German police officers are also on strict alert to protect the British guests. During the gathering, a police squad was prepared to take orders, and plainclothes detectives were mixed among the crowd.

Eden Prepares to Go to Moscow

Simon said that after the meeting ends, he plans to meet with foreign press representatives. At the same time, Eden has packed his bags and is preparing to depart for Moscow at midnight. (Reuters, 26th)

Memel Court Verdict Strengthens Hitler's Hand

Not long after the talks began, a telegram arrived from Kaunas, the capital of Lithuania, stating that 126 National Socialist Party members accused of plotting to overthrow the government and return Memel to Germany were severely punished by the Lithuanian authorities after interrogation. Four people were sentenced to death, two were sentenced to life imprisonment with hard labor, and the rest were sentenced to imprisonment ranging from eight to twelve years. All their property was confiscated. The news conveyed in this telegram may affect the resolution of the Memel issue. The Memel court's verdict is widely regarded as sufficient to strengthen Hitler's hand on the Memel issue. It is widely expected that the Memel trial will cause public outrage in Berlin and lead to strict demands on the Lithuanian authorities to reduce the sentences. After receiving this news at the meeting, Hitler stopped the discussion and presented the Memel issue to the British representatives for a considerable period of time. (Reuters, 26th)

Crowds Gather on Wilhelmstrasse, Wildly Cheering "Long Live German Head of State"

At 1:20 PM, British Foreign Secretary Simon hosted a banquet for National Socialist Party leaders at the British Embassy. At that time, more than a thousand people gathered on Wilhelmstrasse, waiting for Simon and Eden to arrive. General Goering, wearing a sky-blue, gold-trimmed air force general's uniform, arrived first. Everyone waved and wildly shouted "Long Live" to greet him. Soon after, Hitler also arrived, and the crowd cheered even more enthusiastically. Hitler responded with the National Socialist Party salute. Simon arrived immediately after and also received a warm welcome. A total of 50 people attended the banquet, including General Fritsch, a leader of the defense forces. Only Mrs. Phipps was a woman at the table. The gathering place was in the embassy's magnificent ballroom. Hitler looked particularly tired when he entered. (Reuters)

Germany Desires Peaceful Cooperation

(Berlin) Regarding the Anglo-German talks, it is reported that Chancellor Hitler explained to the British cabinet members that Germany is very willing to immediately conclude a pact to limit armaments on the basis of equal rights and a collective security system.

Considers the Soviet Union a Great Enemy

It is also prepared to sign the proposed Western European Air Pact. However, Germany opposes any security system that includes the Soviet Union.

Austria Should Have the Right to Self-Determination

As for the Danube River Pact plan (a pact of non-interference in the internal affairs among Central European countries), Germany opposes any system that maintains the status quo between Germany and Austria (i.e., the issue of German-Austrian merger). Germany will insist that the Austrian people have the right to self-determination in political affairs.

Conditions for Returning to the League of Nations

It is also reported that Chancellor Hitler supports Germany's return to the League of Nations, but only on the conditions that the League of Nations is reorganized, that the covenant is separated from the Treaty of Versailles, and that Germany's equal rights are fully recognized at the same time.

Does Not Forget the Memel Region

Regarding the issue of the Memel region, it is reported that Chancellor Hitler denied that Germany intends to take violent action in the area but stated that as long as the Memel system is not changed, the Memel issue will continue to be a point of contention. (Havas, 25th)

(Berlin) According to the Associated Press today, Germany may demand the autonomous region of Memel, which currently belongs to Lithuania. It is generally believed that although European countries may not immediately agree to this demand, the fate of Memel may be decided by a popular vote similar to that of the Saar. It is also reported that Germany may propose a popular vote in Memel as a condition for Hitler to make concessions on the issues of rearmament and security. (National Telegram, 25th)

(Berlin) Regarding the visit of British Ministers Simon and Eden to Berlin, the German government issued the following simple press release today:

Issued a Brief Communiqué: Head of State Hitler received British Foreign Secretary Simon and Lord Privy Seal Eden this morning. Foreign Minister Neurath and British Ambassador Phipps also participated in the talks. Meetings were held immediately in the morning and afternoon. All the points mentioned in the London Declaration were raised and discussed, and the talks will continue tomorrow. (National Telegram, 25th)

Both Sides Meet with Sincerity

(Berlin) In yesterday's meeting between Britain and Germany, both sides were able to meet with sincerity. Therefore, the exchange of opinions was quite friendly. However, what Head of State Hitler and British Foreign Secretary Simon discussed yesterday mainly focused on eliminating misunderstandings and laying the groundwork for today's discussion of details. As of now, the situation of the negotiations can be said to be mostly optimistic. There is also one point, namely that a pending issue has been involved in the outline of yesterday's general discussion, namely the Eastern European Pact. Hitler expressed lengthy opinions on this. (National Telegram, 25th)

Resolved Many Difficulties

According to newspaper reports, during today's talks, both sides clearly showed enthusiasm for fully stating their positions and seeking understanding. According to general impressions from the outside world, the Anglo-German exchange of opinions has actually resolved many difficulties with all the issues, and there is no doubt that the UK is willing to explore the German viewpoints with impartial expectations. Simon Refuses to See Guests

(Berlin) Many journalists gathered at the British Embassy, waiting to meet Simon, but their wish was not fulfilled. Eden announced that the British Foreign Secretary could not see guests due to overwork. (Reuters, 25th)

Banquet by German Foreign Minister

(Berlin) Tonight, Foreign Minister Neurath hosted a banquet to welcome British Foreign Secretary Simon and Lord Privy Seal Eden. About 90 people were invited to accompany them. Chancellor Hitler also came to participate. (Havas, 25th)

German Newspapers Summarize Opinions on Current Issues

(Berlin) Tonight, the Deutsche Tageszeitung summarized Germany's attitude towards the issues currently being discussed as follows:

(1) Armaments: Germany must not be discriminated against. If other countries are willing to implement disarmament or restrictions, Germany is also willing to do so.

(2) Eastern European Pact: This is the source of disaster. Germany does not want to risk joining the struggles of other people. Germany feels that countries which should not be involved in regional agreements are those countries geographically located in a way inappropriate to hear about it.

(3) Danube River Pact: This pact must not prevent the development of natural relations between Germany and Austria or cause other countries to interfere in Austria's internal affairs.

(4) Air Pact: Germany has long declared its agreement to the League of Nations. Before the fundamental issues regarding security and equality are resolved, no decision can be made on this matter. This 'pact must not become a tool for one-sided debate. (Reuters, 25th)

Britain Clearly Opposes Germany's Breach of Treaty: Prime Minister's Words Relieve Doubts

(London) The rumor that Britain has peacefully acquiesced to Germany's restoration of armaments was completely dispelled today by Prime Minister MacDonald in the House of Commons. In response to questioning, MacDonald declared that Germany has no right to abandon the treaty and said that there are no provisions in the treaty for repeal. "To say that Germany or any country's unilateral action can cause the treaty to be abandoned is a mistake." It is generally believed that the Prime Minister's words have swept away any doubts about the consensus of opinion among Britain, France, and Italy. (National Telegram, 25th)

French Premier Publishes an Article Calling for National Unity, Citing Soviet Russia's Military Expansion as an Example

Feeling threatened, Soviet Russia is now actively expanding the Red Army, and the number of its people serving national defense has greatly increased. It is no wonder that Soviet Russia is proud of it. Soviet Russia is indeed giving us a better patriotic lesson. (Reuters, 25th)

France Vigorously Implements Air Defense, Expansion of Air Force Bill Passed by the Chamber of Deputies

(Paris) Today, the Chamber of Deputies passed a bill with 453 votes to 11, according to which the whole country will vigorously implement defenses against aerial attacks. A special revenue defensive committee will be set up to manage the affairs of civilians and volunteers who cannot be mobilized. The case stipulates that in the event of enemy air raids, the population in densely populated areas must be scattered in nearby villages, and orders will be issued at any time to conduct air defense exercises to train the people so as to avoid being caught off guard at the last minute. The case also stipulates that those who hear the alarm and do not immediately comply shall be subject to imprisonment of six days to one month. (Reuters, 25th)

(Paris) The Chamber of Deputies has passed a bill to expand the air force with 451 votes to 11. The bill stipulates that 99 percent of the expenses for constructing bomb shelters will be borne by the state, and the rest will be recognized by various agencies. According to estimates by socialist members of parliament, the total amount of this burden will be about 4 million francs. (National Telegram, 25th)

France Prohibits the Export of Military Raw Materials

(Paris) The cabinet decided today to prohibit the export of a military raw material to maintain national defense. It is reported that this move was caused by Germany's purchase of large quantities of raw materials such as magnesium. Cotton and wood are also subject to the ban. (National Telegram, 25th)

The Second Meeting Place for Britain, France and Italy is Selected as Isola Bella in Northern Italy; Italian Vice-Minister Reports on Paris Talks, Seeks Comprehensive Solution to Armaments Issues, No Other Option than Agreement Guarantees

(Paris) Italian Undersecretary for Foreign Affairs Suvich returned to Rome today from Paris and immediately reported to Prime Minister Mussolini on the results of his talks with French Foreign Minister Laval and British Foreign Secretary Simon. It is learned that Isola Bella in Lake Maggiore has been selected as the future meeting place for the three countries. According to Italian observers, a real decision on the issue of German rearmament must be made at that meeting. Today, the Italian newspaper Il Giornale d'Italia reiterated in its editorial that there is no other good solution to the comprehensive solution to the arms issue in the future except for the necessary safeguards generated by common agreement. These safeguards are already outlined in the proposed Mutual Assistance Pact and the Danube River Non-Intervention Pact. The solution to the arms issue will not exceed this range in the future either. (National Telegram, 25th)

Austria-Hungary Follows Germany's Lead, Demands Equal Rights, Italy Sympathizes, Little Entente Opposes, League of Nations Meets New Difficulties

(Geneva) The League of Nations began action today on France's lawsuit against Germany for violating the Treaty of Versailles so that the matter could be dealt with by the highest international peace organization. Countries belonging to the Council of the League of Nations have received a notification today from Secretary-General Avenol to convene a special meeting on April 15. Senior League of Nations officials expect that if the issue is formally voted on, the Council will rebuke Germany, but they are now making every effort to avoid this. At the same time, the League of Nations has another difficult problem because, according to the Associated Press from reliable sources, Austria has also launched a request to restore conscription and establish a standing army of 100,000 people. It is reported that Austria has expressed to Britain, France and Italy that unless the military clauses of the Treaty of Saint-Germain are amended, Austria will no longer be able to maintain its position. Italy, of course, agrees with this, because this move can increase the strength to resist Germany's expansion in Southern Europe. The Little Entente opposes the proposal, fearing that this move will cause Hungary and Bulgaria to demand equal treatment. Well-informed sources say that Austria's request to increase its troops is closely related to the Habsburg restoration movement. It has been learned here that the Austrian Home Guard is currently brewing a coup, with its young leader, Prince Starhemberg, as the Austrian ruler. However, this plan will probably take a peaceful approach, starting with amending the constitution. After Prince Starhemberg takes power, Archduke Otto's accession to the throne will be even closer. (National Telegram, 26th)

Budapest - Hungarian Deputy Prime Minister Gömbös said at a rally in his constituency yesterday that Germany had been demanding the issue of rearmament for many years, but because other countries did not comment on it, it took a path of self-determination to achieve its goal of equality. Hungary, as a member of the League of Nations, plans to demand equal rights, and Italy and other friendly countries are willing to help, so what it seeks can certainly be achieved. In addition to political issues, Hungary also plans to raise financial and economic issues. Countries that assume the heavy responsibility of European security should also be promoted. (National Telegram, 25th)

Italy Increases Troops on Austrian Border, Does Not Want to Oppose Austria's Rearmament, Considers It a Bulwark Against German Southern Advance

(Rome) The conflict between Italy and Abyssinia has temporarily subsided due to the tense situation in Europe. Italy has turned its attention to the north. The Associated Press learned today that Italy's mobilization plan against Germany intends to deploy a large number of troops on the Italian-Austrian border. There are currently nine regiments of troops in that area. Rome is maintaining silence on the rumors circulating in Geneva that Austria plans to triple its military strength, but it has not denied it either. Some senior officials said that Italy does not want to oppose Austria's rearmament, believing that it will create a bulwark against the development of German National Socialism in Southern Europe. (National Telegram, 26th)

U.S. Senator Borah Observes that European War Can Be Avoided, Germany Does What It Wants by Violating the Treaty, Expects Allies to Eventually Succumb

(Washington) Republican Senator Borah recently declared that the United States is not at risk of being drawn into a European conflict. Germany's rearmament is the prelude to the abolition of the Treaty of Versailles, which will help ease the European situation. (Havas, 25th)

(Washington) Republican Senator Borah, chairman of the Foreign Relations Committee during President Hoover's era, declared today in his characteristically brief and straightforward tone, "I do not believe there is a risk of war. Germany will be able to do what it wants, and the Allies will succumb. Although the Treaty of Versailles will become a piece of waste paper, that is a good thing." As soon as these words came out, the war clouds in Europe immediately dissipated. (National Telegram, 25th)

(Washington) During the European War, the British mail ship "Lusitania" was sunk by a German submarine, causing the deaths of many American passengers. President Wilson then declared war on Germany because of this. Recently, in view of the fact that if European countries were to start a war, this kind of thing could easily happen again, which could cause the United States to be drawn into the vortex again, the United States government is considering suspending the issuance of passports to travelers going abroad in wartime to prevent this from happening. It is also studying measures to prohibit the export of military supplies, but the general public is skeptical as to whether the prohibition of the export of military supplies can be implemented. It is believed that cotton and wheat can indeed be regarded as military supplies in modern warfare. If exports are prohibited, American farmers will inevitably strongly oppose it. (Havas, 25th)

Former Chinese Inspector General of Customs Elected Chairman of Opium Committee

(Geneva) Former Chinese Inspector General of Customs L.A. Lyall was elected today as Chairman of the Permanent Opium Committee. (Reuters, 26th)

Pacific Situation is Urgent, Canada's Position, Safety Depends on Compromise between Britain and the United States

(New York) Today, the New York Times editorial column published an article commenting on Canada's position in the Far East incident, saying, "The British Imperial Conference in 1921 decided not to renew the Anglo-Japanese alliance, which was due to Canada's proposal and was supported by Newfoundland and Australia. Because, from the geographical location of Canada, if a war occurs between the United States and Japan, Canada will be the only way for both sides to fight. If British policy is linked with Japan, the danger of Canada's position is unimaginable, and Canada's security depends on the compromise between Britain and the United States. Now that the United States has not joined the League of Nations, a regional collective security system should be established, that is, to continue or expand the Nine-Power Treaty, which is enough to prevent problems before they occur. As for Canada, as a British Dominion and a country along the Pacific Ocean, it should, based on the ideal of international collective action, seek to solve various problems in the Pacific Ocean by various methods. If this kind of attempt fails, Canada will also do its best to ensure that the friendly relationship between Britain and the United States is not harmed in the slightest." (Havas, 26th)

Avenol's Statement: Japan's Withdrawal from the League of Nations Takes Effect Today; League of Nations Secretary-General Expresses Regret; Matsuoka States Japan Cannot Be Isolated

(Geneva) Japan's formal notice of withdrawal from the League of Nations, issued on March 27, 1935, takes effect tomorrow. From tomorrow onwards, all legal relations between Japan and the League of Nations will be severed. (Reuters, 26th)

(Geneva) League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol issued a statement here today regarding Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations, stating that it is regrettable that Japan, an original member of the League, has severed its ties after fifteen years of cooperation. Now that the withdrawal is a fact, all legal relations between Japan and the League of Nations no longer exist. Japan no longer enjoys any rights or bears any obligations to the League. It is unfortunate that Japan no longer maintains its former position with regard to the League. However, we are gratified to hear that the Japanese government intends to pursue a policy of international cooperation in the spirt of the Imperial Rescript issued two years ago. We cannot say what form Japan will adopt, but personally, I have decided not to take any action that could hinder relations between Japan and the League. We cannot predict the future. I do not believe we should abandon hope for the universality of the League. (Reuters, 26th)

(Tokyo) The period of advance notice for Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations concludes today. From tomorrow onwards, Japan will sever relations with the League. According to the Tokyo Newspaper, Japan's policies and attitudes after withdrawing from the League are as follows: (1) The League of Nations still refuses to recognize "Manchukuo," so Japan has decided never to return to the League. (2) Japan will not return the South Pacific Islands under mandate, because the administering country does not necessarily have to be a member of the League, but will only submit annual reports on governance. (3) Japan will participate in disarmament conferences, as their purpose is to promote world peace and reduce the burden on the people, and the US and Russia are also participating. (4) Japan will continue to participate and cooperate with the World Court and the International Labour Bureau, as their nature is independent of the League of Nations. (5) Japan will not participate in the Opium Advisory Committee, the Committee on the Traffic of Women and Children, the General Conference on Communications and Transit, the Economic Consultative Committee, the Finance Committee, the Health Committee, the Fiscal Committee, and other agencies in an official government capacity, because the League's appointment of commissioners is unfair. (China United Press, 26th)

(Tokyo) Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota declined to comment on Japan's formal withdrawal from the League of Nations today, saying that Japan wishes this day to pass quietly, without much ado. Other officials from the Foreign Ministry also declined to express their opinions, but stated that Japan will abide by the policies stipulated in the Imperial Rescript of March 1933. Observers now believe that Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations is a very legitimate move, as it allows Japan to break free from the internationalism embraced by Britain and the United States. They also believe that the dangerous situation has now passed, and the political situation in the Far East is now more tranquil than last year. Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations, Foreign Minister Hirota's criticism of the Washington Naval Treaty, and his conciliatory policy towards Russia have greatly increased Japan's prestige in the Far East. According to observers, the events of the past two years have made the Japanese government aware of the dangers of multilateral treaties, and it is expected that Japan will advocate bilateral agreements in the future. (Reuters, 26th)

(Tokyo) Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations will take effect at midnight on the 27th, both in name and in reality. Mr. Yosuke Matsuoka, who had been fully empowered as the chairman of the Japanese delegation to the League of Nations Council during the Sino-Japanese conflict, and who had declared Japan's withdrawal from the League on February 24, 1933, is deeply moved by this. His statement is as follows: The notice of withdrawal from the League of Nations taking effect today is merely completing the formality of withdrawing from the League. The world has known for two years that Japan was withdrawing from the League, and when the notice was issued, the Emperor granted an Imperial Rescript. The spirit of this Rescript can be said to be the aspiration of the entire Japanese nation. However, even though we are formally withdrawing, we must still cooperate with all nations for the sake of world peace, and there is no change in this. Inside or outside the League, it is all the same. Japan must not be isolated in the world, and the nations of the world will not allow Japan to be isolated, for such a move is impossible in this small world. I believe that after Japan's withdrawal, the League of Nations will only be a peace organization for Europe, and I hope that it can fulfill its function. The nations of the world, at least as of today, cannot regard the League of Nations as a global peace organization, because it has failed to fulfill its mission, and they are all aware of this. The way to safeguard world peace is to divide the world into regions and practice division of labor and cooperation. We should first safeguard peace in each region, study this path, and hold regional conferences to facilitate the exchange of views. There is no better solution than this. In short, Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations may be related to fate, and in the end, it is up to the countries concerned to seek the best way forward. (Japan United Press, 26th)

(Tokyo) The Japanese government will completely sever relations with the League of Nations at midnight on the 27th. According to a report from Consul-General Yokoyama in Geneva on the 25th to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Japanese government's contribution to the League of Nations, amounting to 483,294.85 Swiss francs, was paid to the League of Nations Secretariat on the 9th. (Japan United Press, 26th)

Important Bills Remain Unresolved; Japanese Diet Adjourns; Minister of Agriculture Expresses Indignation, Economic Circles Disappointed; Seiyukai Criticizes Cabinet's Inability, Trouble Ahead

(Tokyo) The turbulent 67th Diet session has finally come to an end. The closing ceremony was held in the House of Peers at 11:00 a.m. on the 26th. Prime Minister Okada and other cabinet members, Prince Konoe, Speaker Hamada, Vice-Speaker Matsudaira, and all members of both houses attended. The Emperor did not attend in person. The Prime Minister, on Imperial command, read out the Imperial Rescript for the closing ceremony. After bowing deeply towards the Imperial Throne, he received the Imperial Rescript from the secretary and stated, "I, the Minister, have the honor of reading the Imperial Rescript for the closing ceremony on Imperial command." Amidst the deepest respects of all members, he read the gracious Imperial Rescript. Upon completion, Speaker Konoe received the Imperial Rescript, and the ceremony concluded. All members left the chamber. (Dentsu News Agency, 26th)

(Tokyo) The eventful 67th Diet session concluded last night. The closing ceremony was held in the House of Peers today. Secretary-General Wakamiya of the Seiyukai, recalling the political battles of the past three months, expressed his impressions: "Looking back on the Diet session, I feel even more keenly the incompetence of the current cabinet. The reason why the important bills proposed by the government were not passed is because the cabinet's foundation is not based on political parties. Not extending the session to pass the Rice Control Law further demonstrates its incompetence. Therefore, the future of the cabinet is predictable." Chief Secretary Raimu of the Minseito stated that half of his time was spent dealing with the aftermath of the bomb incident, which resulted in the adjournment without completing deliberations on important rural issues, which is regrettable for the nation. We express our dissatisfaction with the achievements of this Diet session. Chief Secretary Noda of the Kokumin Domei told reporters that the current cabinet's poor performance in the Diet is due to the fact that the cabinet members are not suited to a time when the entire nation should be united, so it is no surprise that they have not achieved good results. Even if they continue to shamelessly remain in power, they will inevitably collapse soon. However, political parties should also fundamentally reform at this time to prepare for the future of the Diet. Member of the Research Society, Oka Buchikageko, told reporters that the fact that all important bills were shelved is evidence of the weakness of the cabinet, which is due to the government's lack of firm beliefs and its failure to engage in compromise with political parties. Unless the current cabinet undergoes major reform, it will be difficult for it to continue until the next Diet session. (Dentsu News Agency, 26th)

(Tokyo) With the Diet adjourning without completing deliberations on important bills related to the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry, the question of Minister of Agriculture Yamazaki's resignation and Prime Minister Okada's political responsibility has become the focus of attention. The government will now devote its full efforts to realizing the Cabinet Deliberation Council and recruiting influential figures from various sectors to compensate for the authority lost in the Diet. Whether it can be established and its capabilities will not only affect the current cabinet, but also have a significant impact on Japan's political structure. Another difficult issue for the government in this Diet session was the aftermath of the so-called Emperor Organ Theory. Although discussions in the Diet have been completed, the external opposition movement is becoming increasingly fierce. If the method of resolution is not appropriate, unexpected waves will occur in the political world, which is predictable. In short, optimism is not warranted for the future of the government, which revealed its weaknesses in the Diet, and the Seiyukai. (Japan United Press, 26th)

(Tokyo) With the Diet session not extended and the bills related to rice control shelved, Minister of Agriculture Yamazaki expressed considerable indignation. Last night, he told reporters that the reason why the session was not extended was because the government did not consider it necessary, but the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry is in great difficulty. Rural policies cannot be implemented as a result, and even if we are criticized by the world, it cannot be helped. The aftermath cannot be easily discussed, but this is only the Minister of Agriculture's responsibility and should be borne by the entire cabinet. (Dentsu News Agency, 26th)

(Tokyo) Although the economic circles generally expected that the economic-related bills would be completely defeated, the fact that the Diet adjourned in this way has caused a great shock, leaving them disappointed. (Japan United Press, 26th)

New Belgian Cabinet Formed; Prime Minister Theunis Concurrently Serves as Foreign Minister; Currency Policy to Implement Devaluation; Advocate Restoring Diplomatic Relations with Russia

Brussels: The Vice-Governor of the National Bank of Belgium, Theunis, announced last night that the formation of the cabinet was completed. It is reported that the new cabinet will be composed of the Catholic, Liberal, and Socialist parties. Theunis will concurrently serve as Foreign Minister. The previous cabinet of Prime Minister de Broqueville was overthrown due to strong opposition to its fiscal policies. Therefore, the public is eagerly awaiting the new cabinet's formal announcement of its position on maintaining the gold standard. It is likely that Theunis will oppose reducing the value of the Belgian franc. However, as the Socialist party, which supports devaluation, is participating in the cabinet, it is difficult to predict what will happen. Business leaders generally support devaluation, while the banking sector and the government generally oppose it. (National News Agency, 26th)

Brussels: The new cabinet has now been formed with the following personnel: "Prime Minister and Foreign Minister" Theunis (Catholic Party, new appointment), "Minister without Portfolio" Vandervelde (Socialist Party, incumbent), Hymans (Liberal Party, former Foreign Minister), de Broqueville (Catholic Party, former Minister of Interior), "Minister of National Defense" Devèze (Catholic Party, incumbent), "Minister of Finance" Max-Leo Gérard (Liberal Party, new appointment), "Minister of Colonies" Rubbens (Catholic Party, former Minister of Labor and Social Affairs), "Minister of Education" Bovesse (Liberal Party, former Minister of Justice), "Minister of Economic Affairs" Isaac (Catholic Party, incumbent), "Minister of Interior" Ziwa Nave (Catholic Party, former Minister of Transportation), "Minister of Justice" Soudan (Socialist Party, new appointment), "Minister of Transportation" Spaak (Socialist Party, new appointment), "Minister of Public Works" de Man (Socialist Party, new appointment), "Minister of Labor" Troclet (Socialist Party, new appointment). (Havas, 26th)

Brussels: Among the fifteen members of the new cabinet formed today, there are six from the Catholic Party, four from the Liberal Party, and five from the Socialist Party. Among the Socialist Party members, there are Vandervelde, a leader of the Second International, and de Man, an economist famous for creating a rationalization plan. The new Prime Minister, Theunis, made a cautious statement regarding currency policy, refraining from making any definitive statements. Therefore, it is possible that the new cabinet will implement currency devaluation. The new cabinet's domestic policy aims to control banking operations, implement the conversion of public debt interest, and reduce working hours for laborers. In foreign policy, it will restore diplomatic relations with Soviet Russia. Theunis will also strive to stabilize the international situation, realize an international monetary standard system, and reduce barriers to relations. As for restricting import quotas, it will oppose them. (Havas, 26th)

International Commercial Telegram - Special Commercial News from Reuters on March 26th -

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: Today's price is 145 shillings and 7 pence, half a penny lower than yesterday.

London Silver Bars: Today, the silver market rose sharply due to purchases by speculators and few sellers. Spot is 28 pence and 875, futures is 29 pence, both up 1 penny.

Bombay Silver Bars: The Bombay silver market opened firm, rising more than 1 rupee due to the overnight rise in London silver prices. The market closed stable. Spot price is 67 rupees and 9 annas, up 1 rupee and 6 annas.

Exchange Rates

British-American: In the London foreign exchange market today, the market was generally calm except for the Belgian franc, which fell sharply due to heavy selling. At noon, the US-Belgian exchange rate was 23.25, a drop of 1.95 compared to yesterday's closing price (21.30). The British-American exchange rate opened at $4.78125, lower than yesterday's US-British closing price by 375. The price trended lower after opening, and only returned to the opening price at 2:00 p.m., which was $4.78125.

British-French: The French exchange rate opened at 72.53 francs, fell to 73.40 francs, but later returned to 72.50 francs, which is the most recent price.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The New York cotton market opened slightly higher. Although there were not many transactions, the rising trend continued. The spot situation remained strong, and there was still talk of inflation in the market. The Northeast weather report indicated that preparations for cotton fields are currently suspended. Indian and Bombay cotton markets fell slightly today due to selling by Japanese merchants and poor Liverpool telegrams. The market closed weaker, with the price for April-May at 220.25 rupees, down 25.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was calm today, and sentiment was somewhat weaker. At 1:00 p.m., the price for the May contract was 6.24, down 4 pounds.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market rose slightly today. At 1:00 p.m., the price for the May contract rose 375 to 5 shillings and 2.25 pence.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened stable, with prices rising slightly, expressing sympathy for overseas market conditions. The market sentiment became firmer after the rubber price increased, and the price continued to rise. Eastern demand was good, and it was reported that the drought in the southwestern wheat region had not been significantly reduced.

Rubber

London: This morning, the London rubber market adopted a wait-and-see attitude, awaiting the resolution of the International Rubber Regulation Committee. The opening was quiet, and prices did not move, but later became slightly more stable. At noon, the price for the July-September contract was 5.4375 pence, up 0.0625.

New York: Today, the rubber market was the focus of attention for general merchants. Before the opening, the news was received that the Rubber Regulation Committee stipulated that the quotas for April, May, June and July were set at 70%, and the other months were at 65%. This news was favorable to the bulls. At the opening, merchants competed to buy, and the momentum was frantic, causing prices to rise by 100 pounds higher than yesterday. After a slight pause, the price rose again half an hour after the opening, and the market situation was quite firm. With the rubber market showing signs of improvement, other commodities also became firm and stable.

Securities

New York: There was very little news of interest on Wall Street today. Securities opened quietly and unevenly, with prices mostly unchanged. The Dow Jones 30 Stock Average opened at 99.56, up 6 pounds. Copper mining stocks are expected to rise in price today due to the prospect of copper production restrictions. The remaining stock prices hardly changed today. The New York securities market prices are listed on the left.
