Major Dust Bowl Disaster in Western US; Tens of Thousands of Acres of Farmland Affected; Many Farmers Abandon Their Homes and Relocate

Kansas: The plains of the western United States are suffering from a dust bowl disaster, and this year's harvest is feared to be unusually poor, which is rare in the past. The number of acres of farmland affected in Colorado, Wyoming, Kansas, Nebraska, Texas, and Oklahoma is unknown, but farmers have abandoned their homes and relocated, and many livestock have also died. According to statisticians from the Department of Labor, the losses are in the millions, and tens of millions of acres in southeastern Colorado may not be suitable for farmland or pasture for the next hundred years. (Reuters, 26th)

Irish Hospitals' Sweepstake; Tianjin Has Hope of Winning First Prize

Dublin: According to today's news, the Irish Hospitals' Sweepstake for the Champagne Stakes has sold a total of £2,824,926, with £1,680,979 set aside as prize money, divided into sixteen first prizes of £100,000 each. Tianjin has hope of winning one first prize, as the ticket purchased by a gentleman in Tianjin has drawn a horse that will participate in the race. (Reuters, 26th)

Northwestern Inspection Report

— Special Correspondent Ya

Gold and Silver Mines of Ejin and Alxa

The plains of Andunyu are vast and boundless. The verse from Meng Haoran's poem, "The wilderness vast, the sky low, the trees," is truly a depiction of this place. However, upon entering Jialue Pass, the scenery is completely different.

The southern mountains of Jiuquan are the highest peak of the Qilian Mountains. Snow accumulates year-round and does not melt, commonly referred to as the Heavenly Mountains. In summer, the red sun shines brightly, and the melting snow irrigates the fields, as beneficial as a water channel. Hence, there is a saying that even without rain throughout the year, a bountiful harvest can be achieved. However, according to my friend Liu Xiaoquan, "During the great drought in Gansu and Shaanxi in the seventeenth and eighteenth years of the Republic of China, starving people dug up grass roots and peeled tree bark, cooking them together with leather to barely sustain themselves. The wealthy bought steamed buns, fearing they would be snatched by the starving, and would spit on them without concern for cleanliness. Starving corpses were left unburied, and beggars would carry corpses to merchants' shops, refusing to leave unless given food. Selling daughters was common, but initially there were buyers, but later no one cared. Those who initially bought daughters later sought to sell themselves but could not. The various tragic scenes are too unbearable to fully describe. Jiuquan, being in the same disaster area, was no exception." Therefore, the saying of a bountiful harvest without rain is an exaggeration. In recent years, rainfall has been slightly better, but when asking the farmers, the answer is still unanimously "drought." One farmer even said, "During the great famine, we swore that if we were lucky enough to survive, even if we had to beg for food, we would eat one less mouthful each day to save some food in preparation for another disaster. Who knew that in recent years, Heaven has not blessed us with much rain, and it is still difficult to even have thin millet porridge. Not to mention anything else, just look at this cold weather, and we are still wearing these clothes. Besides, there is also..." At this point, the conversation abruptly stopped. It seems they are suffering not only from "drought" but also from "taxes." Therefore, to alleviate the suffering of the farmers, it is essential to actively repair water conservancy and passively abolish exorbitant taxes. Both are extremely crucial, and this is not limited to just one county.

Wei Yunzhi, the magistrate of Jiuquan County, said that the Northwest is rich in treasures and the people are honest and simple. Although it is said that the culture is backward, it is not without solutions. The most concerning issue is the increasingly serious border crisis. In areas north of Jiuquan, such as Weiyuan City and Pingshu Camp in the Ejin Torghut banner, foreigners often disguised as Mongols, speaking the Mongolian language, travel back and forth to scout and inquire. They also present gifts such as tea bricks and silk to the princes to curry favor, which seems suspicious. Yu Dianfen, the director of the Jiuquan station of the Xin Sui Automobile Company, who was present, also said that on the company's routes through the Mongolian grasslands, similar situations are indeed often seen. Regarding the border situation and mineral resources of Ejin, according to those familiar with the matter, the following is said:

From the northwest of Ejin to the Malimenzhade Mountain, it borders the Hooqin Torghut. This mountain rises steeply for twenty li and has a Bodhisattva temple, called Darik by the Mongols, which is the name of the Bodhisattva. The mountain is about three hundred li from the Ejin Wangfu (Prince's Residence). Several dozen li past this mountain is the Beizi (minor prince) residence of the Hooqin Torghut. From Hooqin to Altai, it is about one thousand and several hundred li. Passing Ejin, there is an endless plain with many springs, fertile land, and a mild climate, similar to Ningxia and Gansu. The locals grow highland barley and there are abundant mineral resources, especially gold. In the Juyanhai Lake in the northwest of Ejin, several rivers flow in, and the Weak River of Gansu (i.e., the Shandan River) also flows into it. The lake is one hundred and several tens of li in circumference, and the water does not overflow, but flows underground for thousands of li until it reaches the Altai border northwest of Hooqin Torghut, where it flows out and becomes a huge river, flowing northwest. There is a large silver mine in Alxa, about a thousand li northwest of Dingyuan, which takes eleven days to reach. It is called the Kala Zeng Huzha Mountain. The mine is about fifty li from east to west and thirty li from north to south. The quality of the silver ore produced is excellent. During the Tongzhi era of the Qing Dynasty, a Mr. Su from Gulang, Gansu, mined it once with a capital of over ten thousand, but using old methods for two years only covered the capital. In the twenty-eighth year of Guangxu, his son Su Chao gathered shares again, but both times, due to the distance of the required water and firewood, making transportation inconvenient, the operation was stopped. Now, with automobile transportation of water and firewood, it is more convenient than before, and using Western mining methods will surely yield substantial profits. Forty li away from this mountain, there is a kind of firewood called Zhagechai by the Mongols, which can burn even when wet and is specially used for smelting silver. The territory of the Zhasaktu Khan of Outer Mongolia was originally not large, but now it is mistakenly marked as part of that banner on maps in many places. Currently, wealthy Mongols from the Zhasaktu Khan who are avoiding communism have fled to Alxa and Ejin, each with several hundred households.

About a hundred li from Jiuquan City, there are stones produced in the mountains, some as large as a dou (unit of volume) and some as small as a fist, with fine texture and beautiful colors. They are called Suzhou stones. Stone craftsmen carve them into utensils such as wine cups, bracelets, and pen holders. Their colors include yellow-red, black-green, milky white, and various mixed colors. The luster is beautiful and jade-like. Local people use them as gifts for distant guests, and those who receive them are all delighted. There is a large Buddhist temple in the county, with two notable items: one is a large pot for cooking porridge for a thousand people, and the other is a stone vase that can hold a hundred flowers, which are renowned far and wide.

Traveling to Zhangye (Ganzhou), the car broke down at Twenty Li Fort and stopped for repairs for a day. The next day, wanting to reach Wuwei (Liangzhou), they got up in the middle of the night to pack. Outside the inn, ox carts rumbled one after another, attracted by the electric light of the car, forming groups of three or five to watch. The reporter went up to talk to them. At first, they hesitated to speak, but later they spoke freely without restraint. According to them, "In the villages of this county, rainfall and snowfall are timely, and on average, one shi (unit of volume) of millet sown can yield six shi. The price of grain is usually five or six yuan per shi, but when the new grain is harvested, taxes are pressing, and everyone rushes to sell in the city, selling only two yuan per shi. Those from villages farther from the city who come to sell grain either travel overnight to return on the same day or stay overnight in the suburbs because they cannot return, enduring hunger and cold, all to save a little money. Unfortunately, they often encounter gamblers who drag them away to gamble, losing everything. Alas, these days farmers shouldn't have any money anyway." When asked why the magistrate doesn't ban gambling, they replied that gambling is not banned during the Lunar New Year and the donkey and horse fairs. The donkey and horse fair is during the autumn harvest and is supposed to be for people to buy and sell donkeys and horses, but in reality, everyone openly gambles for dozens of days. If they lose and don't pay, they can report to the Public Security Bureau. People from distant villages also go to set up gambling stalls, but if no one enters, the village chief and headman have to maintain order or offer travel expenses to invite them to other villages. The magistrate of a certain county once issued a ban on gambling after the fair, but the gamblers moved the gambling stalls in front of the county government, so rampant was their power, naturally relying on the army," and so on. Later, in Wuwei, it was indeed heard that Ma Buqing's division had banned gambling, which shows that what the farmers said was not false.

Sichuan Province Vigorously Implements New Policies; Chengdu, Chongqing, and Wanxian Three Cities Strive for Reform; All Inland Tax Bureaus Completely Abolished

Chongqing dispatch: This time when Chairman Chiang Kai-shek visited Chongqing, he was very serious about the various reform movements in Sichuan. Liu Xiang, Chairman of the Sichuan Provincial Government, and general administrative personnel have been especially diligent in promoting them. Currently, the three major cities of Chongqing, Chengdu, and Wanxian have been completely transformed, presenting a new and rising atmosphere. The recent reforms in these three major cities are recorded separately below:

Strictly Prohibiting Smoking

Since March, all opium dens in Chongqing City have been eliminated, and the number of opium pipes confiscated has reached five or six thousand. Opium addicts in the two cities of Jiangbei and Bachi are required to completely quit within this month. Those who do not comply with the regulations or have not quit by the deadline will be punished for disobeying orders. All stores selling opium quitting pills are experiencing a tenfold increase in sales. In order to prevent opportunistic merchants from profiting, the authorities have specially organized chemical tests by the Health Committee to prevent them from mixing in toxic substances and harming society. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek was also requested to send a telegram to Liu Ruiheng, the Director of the National Health Administration and Chairman of the Opium Prohibition Committee, urgently requesting him to send trustworthy and reliable personnel to Sichuan to handle the opium quitting work in Sichuan Province. It is heard that after receiving the telegram, Liu is in the process of selecting personnel, and they are expected to arrive in Sichuan around the end of the month. The cities of Chengdu and Wanxian are also working hard on the opium prohibition movement, and it is expected to be completed in the shortest possible time. According to news from important officials of the Provincial Government, the chairman deeply hates the people's opium smoking and has made a firm determination to require all addicts in Sichuan Province to quit opium this year, otherwise the responsible officials in each locality will be punished without leniency.

Reorganizing Police Administration

The Provincial Government believes that the three cities of Rong (Chengdu), Yu (Chongqing), and Wanxian are located at important land and water transportation hubs, with a mix of Chinese and foreigners, and are the focus of attention both at home and abroad. Therefore, public security matters should be specially reorganized in order to correct perceptions and establish a good reputation. It has specially presented five key points to the three cities of Rong, Yu, and Wanxian, urging them to intensify their efforts. The key points are as follows: (1) Cleanliness of clothing. Whether or not the clothing is clean is the best indication of the diligence or laziness of the police officers and is related to the entire police administration. Therefore, the clothing worn by the police must be neat and clean, and no negligence is allowed, so as not to affect appearances. (2) Eliminating the old and weak. Since the police are responsible for serving society and leading the general public, they must be energetic and serious in attitude in order to be competent in their duties. All those who are old and weak, lack energy, or are addicted to bad habits should be immediately eliminated and replaced with strong and well-trained personnel. (3) Maintaining traffic. Maintaining traffic is one of the basic tasks of the police and is very important as it relates to social order and safety. Therefore, various methods must be used to guide the traffic of various vegetable carriers, sedan chairs, and vehicles, so that they travel according to the prescribed routes, so as not to hinder traffic. Police booths must also be set up at wider intersections to facilitate police officers in directing traffic. (4) Cleaning the streets. Health is the mother of career success, and cleanliness is essential for health. Upon investigation, the main roads in various cities are generally clean, but the streets and alleys are often filled with garbage and are extremely dirty. This is due to the lack of cleanliness among the people, but also due to the dereliction of duty by the police. In the future, regardless of sunny or rainy weather, heat or cold, all levels of officials must personally inspect the streets, wells, ponds, ditches, toilets, food, and items. If any uncleanliness is found, it must be immediately prohibited or guided for correction. (5) Improving toilets. It is found that the cleanliness of toilets is of great importance to the public health of citizens. In the past, due to poor construction and the people's non-compliance with the law, people would defecate and urinate at will outside the toilets, and the foul odor spread everywhere, causing pedestrians to cover their noses. Now that summer is approaching, there are especially many diseases. Ways should be found to improve the toilets and conduct serious inspections to curb the source of disease. Yesterday, a special order was issued to change the Public Security Office of the Chongqing Garrison Command to the Public Security Bureau, appointing Fan Chongshi as the director and urging him to immediately take office, strictly enforce the regulations, and correct perceptions. Fan has already taken office that day and is implementing reforms.

Abolishing Tax Bureaus

After the establishment of the Provincial Government, all old taxes and levies in Sichuan Province have been abolished, and a single tax system is implemented. The Sichuan Provincial Local Tax Bureau is established in Chongqing, the Local Tax Sub-bureau is established in Wanxian, and Local Tax Collection Offices are established in counties bordering other provinces, such as Yibin, Jiangjin, Hejiang, Gongjiang, and Nanchuan. All other inland tax bureaus are abolished. The Chenghua, Hechuan, and Fuling County Tax Bureaus, the Fuhe Merchant Protection Office, and the Jiangna Collection Office are immediately stopped from collecting taxes and are required to close down within a time limit. The original telegram stated, "Upon investigation, all old taxes and levies in Sichuan Province have been abolished, and a Provincial Local Tax Bureau is established in Chongqing, a Local Tax Sub-bureau is established in Wanxian, and Local Tax Collection Offices are established in counties bordering other provinces, such as Jiangjin, Yibin, Hejiang, Gongnan, Fengwu, Youxiu, Peng, etc., and a single tax system is implemented, which have been ordered separately and telegraphed to the county bureaus for compliance. It is now found that the Chenghua, Hechuan, Fuling, Luxian, and Jiading Tax Bureaus, the Fuhe Merchant Protection Office, the Jiangna Collection Office, as well as the Neijiang Sugar Tax, the concurrent handling of merchant prohibition of opium, and the merchant protection and opium suppression investigation office in Fushun, the merchant protection part, are all located in the inland of Sichuan Province and there is no need to establish them. They should be abolished immediately and stopped collecting taxes by the afternoon of March 20th of this year. The matter of knowing how to levy taxes on goods and packages transported to neighboring provinces shall be taken over by the county tax collection bureau, except for Chengdu, and one or two staff members for handling neighboring transportation shall be retained and sent to the tax bureau for supervision. In addition to paying the salaries of the officials and staff of the office at all levels who have left their posts this time, a one-month gratuity will also be given to show concern. You are required to comply with the instructions and forward them to your subordinates for compliance, and report the compliance situation for verification." In addition, the Sichuan Provincial Government has recently determined that during the period of bandit suppression, the intelligence of public officials should be improved urgently in order to achieve maximum efficiency in a short period of time. It is planning to establish a training class for public officials, gathering administrative personnel from various counties for training. This method is currently being discussed by the Department of Civil Affairs, using the public official training regulations promulgated by the Central Government as a guideline.

Shandong Telephone Network Completed

Jinan Dispatch: The province's long-distance telephone network, which has been actively constructed by the Department of Construction for the past three years, has largely completed the connection of all provincial and county long-distance telephones. Only the counties of Yanpu, Wendeng, and Rongcheng are still in progress, and construction will begin recently, scheduled to be completed by the end of April. The entire provincial telephone network can be connected. In the future, the Department of Construction will seek to improve and reorganize the province-owned telephones, and make the county-owned telephones more widespread in rural areas. The Long-Distance Telephone Management Office is now ordered to edit a three-year work report statistics and the Long-Distance Telephone Chronicle. The general situation of long-distance telephones and the subsequent reorganization plan are recorded below separately.

Province-Owned Telephones

The province-owned telephones in the province are divided into seven major trunk lines, namely Jinan-Qingdao, Jinan-Tai'an-Tengzhou, Jinan-Dong'a-Jinan, Jinan-Liaocheng, Jinan-Dezhou, Jinan-Hui, and Jinan-Yi. Its administrative area is divided into five districts: Jinan-Dong'a, Jinan-Wu, Lai, Jinan-Yi, and Jinan-Cao. There are 116 telephone bureaus and 19 agency offices. The total length of the lines is 14,612 li, of which 4,676 li are copper wires and 9,945 li are iron wires. The total length of the wires is 17,892 li. There are 288 telephones, 110 switchboards, and 120 long-distance machines. In addition, there are three submarine cables from Putai to Boxing, Luokou, and Dong'a, as well as a Hojia Liu water line.

County-Owned Telephones

County-owned telephones belong to each county and are managed by the Department of Construction. Each county has a long-distance telephone office. The total length of the county-owned telephone network in the province is 5,691 li. Together with the existing lines, the total length is 30,378 li, with 39,837 li of overhead wires. There are a total of 2,963 telephones. All villages and towns can directly communicate with the county, and can also be connected to the province-owned telephones.

Business Situation

Since the telephones in the province are divided into province-owned and county-owned, the revenue is also divided into province-owned and county-owned. The payment is made once a month, which is a zero-payment method. The monthly revenue is around 40,000 yuan. During the peak business season, it can reach more than 50,000 yuan, while in the off-season, it ranges from 30,000 to 40,000 yuan. Of this, accounting takes up two-thirds. It is estimated that after the establishment of the Wendeng County Telephone Bureau, its revenue can be more than doubled, because the coastal areas will be connected to various counties in the future, and its telecommunications business will naturally be busy.

Reorganization Plan

Now that the entire provincial telephone network has been completed, the Department of Construction and the Long-Distance Telephone Management Office are focusing on reorganizing the province-owned and county-owned telephones. The reorganization plan is as follows: (1) Reorganizing the telephone poles on each line, starting with the counties in southern Shandong. All existing telephone poles that are too short or rotten will be replaced with Sha wood poles with a diameter of 5 inches at the top and 7 inches at the bottom. (2) Each county's county government will supervise the people's corps and the united village associations to be responsible for protecting the line poles. The village near the province-owned telephones will be responsible by the county government. If there is any loss, the village will be responsible. The county government's Fourth Section will order each village to be responsible for the county-owned telephones. This method has been implemented in all counties.

Hua County, Henan Province, Appeals for Relief for Disaster Victims; Providing Disaster-Stricken Children and Women with Work as a Long-Term Relief Measure

Kaifeng Dispatch: The flood in Hua County, Henan Province, has caused widespread disaster to the people. Xie Suian, the magistrate of the county, and others have recently sent a telegram to the Shanghai Drought Relief Association, appealing for relief. The telegram stated: "Unfortunately, Hua County has suffered repeatedly from war and famine, leaving ten houses empty of nine. Refugees are everywhere. The Relief Institute was established in the 22nd year of the Republic of China. The poor and helpless gathered at the news, but due to the small amount of funds, it was difficult to accommodate many people. Therefore, we divided the areas and strictly admitted people. Within a day, the old, weak, and disabled who were admitted to the hospital numbered over eighty. They had no clothes or food, and the tragic situation was indescribable. We were planning to raise funds from various sources and勉强勉强(mian qiang): barely/forcefully sustain them with amaranth and糟糠糟糠 (zao kang): chaff and bran to prolong their remaining lives. The fields are completely gone, regardless of whether they are poor or rich households, and the water fills the entire area. We only hear the sound of crying and the sound of water, and there is no time to count those who have become wave fodder and buried in the belly of fish. And those who were lying in collapsed houses, rescued by boat boards, perched on tall trees, jumped into the water and swam, and thus escaped, are estimated to be more than 100,000 people. They eat in the wind and sleep in the dew, only stretching their necks to cry. They break their hearts and pierce their eyes, only gazing at the ocean and sighing. When they see people asking for help, they only shed tears and bow their heads. They beg along the villages, but who can take off their clothes and share their food? They are lucky to have saved a life and avoided becoming drowning ghosts, but who knows that a moment later they will become starving corpses. It is painful to speak of, and those who hear it are heartbroken. Alas, how much ancestral misfortune has our Hua people suffered, that they have suffered such a heavy and tragic calamity? At the end of the lunar year, we were fortunate to have your association come to Henan to provide relief and allocate 20,000 yuan to Hua for relief, which was distributed in full. The surviving remnants were able to prolong their remaining lives. However, because the number of disaster victims is large, the distribution is difficult to cover. The remainder are still displaced and wandering, with the ditches and ravines in sight. And the most painful of these is that the young and strong have drowned, leaving only frail old men and women. Suian and others racked their brains and made a concrete plan to have the disaster-stricken children reclaim the wasteland in the fourth district of Hua County and learn carpentry and mud work. The disaster-stricken women learn weaving and straw hat braiding. We raise funds for the construction of thatched houses, the purchase of agricultural tools and livestock, and industrial equipment. It is estimated that we need 5,000 yuan. So that the old and weak can engage in profitable work. With this 5,000 yuan as a fund, we use the interest they generate to save their remaining lives. Jiangsu Merchants Association Requests Suspension of New Regulations on House Tax

The Jiangsu Provincial General Chamber of Commerce, regarding the new regulations on house tax in Jiangsu Province, telegraphed the National and Provincial governments on the 23rd based on the opinions of the chambers of commerce in various counties, requesting a suspension of implementation and a return to the old regulations. The original telegram is as follows: "To Wang, President of the Executive Yuan of Nanjing; Kong, Minister of Finance; Chen, Chairman of the Jiangsu Provincial Government in Zhenjiang; Yu, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs; Zhao, Director of the Department of Finance; and the Jiangsu Provincial Donation and Tax Supervision Committee: We have repeatedly received letters and telegrams from the chambers of commerce of Yixing, Zhenjiang, Wujin, Wuxi, Qingpu, Gaoyou, Fengxian, Taicang, and Wujiang, stating that the Provincial Government meeting passed a new chapter on the collection of house tax in various counties on February 26 of this year, arbitrarily changing the donation rate and increasing the burden on the local government, and requesting to strive for its abolition in order to alleviate the people's suffering. At the meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees of the affiliated association on the 21st of this month, the opinions were collected and it was unanimously agreed that since the house tax in Jiangsu Province is the funding for each county, and the province and counties are both local governments, each has its own system. Even if there is a change in history or an increase is necessary, it should be discussed publicly by the county in accordance with the provisions of Article 4 of the Provisional Law on Central Supervision of Local Finance before being presented to the province for a decision, which is in accordance with legal procedures and also shows solemnity. Jiangsu Province is close to the capital and guards the central government. How should it show special respect for the regulations of the central government and set an example for other provinces and become a local model? How can the Jiangsu authorities, who have always been known for their virtuousness, disregard the central government's clear regulations and summarily pass them through a provincial government meeting? Previously, it was reported that at a meeting of the Jiangsu Provincial Donation and Tax Supervision Committee, the Director of the Department of Finance attended and reported that the house tax donation rate was the highest standard, and the actual collection in the future would be determined based on the needs of each county. In accordance with Article 7 of the Provisional Law on Central Supervision of Local Finance, local governments at all levels shall not implement any changes in tax items, increases or decreases in tax rates, or raising of public debts without approval in accordance with the provisions of Articles 3 and 4 of this law, and shall not be included in the budget. According to Article 2 of the Provincial Government Organization Law, the provincial government may issue provincial orders and formulate provincial single-line regulations and rules for provincial administrative matters within the scope of not conflicting with central laws and regulations, but regarding restricting people's freedom and increasing people's burden, it shall not be implemented without the approval of the National Government. Inspection of Various Counties Along the Huai River: Desolate Scenery North of Qingjiang and Stagnant Customs; Bandits Rampant in Huai'an, Lian'shui, Yancheng and Other Counties

Zhenjiang News: Zhao Dihua, Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance, and Shen Baixian, Director of the Department of Construction, along with Zhu Ping, Director of the Provincial Land Bureau, and Li Jixin, a member of the Reclamation Design Committee, and a dozen others, departed for northern Jiangsu on the 13th of this month to inspect the Huai River guiding project and the supervised reclamation area. This reporter went to Qingjiangpu on business and traveled together with them. What I saw and heard is recorded below:

Jiangsu is known as the wealthy region of Southeast China. People living along the Yangtze River, traveling between Beijing and Shanghai, see fields and forests as dense as tents, and bustling towns and cities with merchants. They believe Jiangsu deserves its reputation. However, once one steps into the northern Jiangsu area, the impression fades. South of Gaobao still retains some of the Jiangnan atmosphere, but north of Huai'an is completely different. North of Qingjiangpu, the scenery is utterly desolate, like heaven and earth compared to Jiangnan. The old course of the Huai River, after the Yellow River moved south, was silted up and shifted northward, burying the Huai River's flow path. Yellow sand stretches for miles, the north wind roars furiously, and one cannot distinguish objects a few steps away. We inspected the land and found that the people along the Huai River guiding area struggled for drinking water, let alone irrigation. The car bumped along on the levee. Trees are scarce south of the Huai River, and north of the Huai River, there is barren white land (alkalinity not removed) everywhere. The further northeast the journey, the more difficult the lives of the people become. The car stopped at the boundary between Funing and Lianshui counties. We saw that in the countryside, five or six out of ten children had trachoma or scabies. When the wind blew their hair, nineteen out of ten had lice eggs in rows. Girls seven years old and above had already bound feet. The backwardness can be imagined. The chief engineer of the Huai River guiding project, Mr. Ge Hanlou, said that the success of guiding the Huai River would not only eliminate the water volume of Hongze Lake, but also introduce fresh water for irrigation. The desolate scene of today can be transformed into a fertile area like Jiangnan in the future.

Funing is the largest county in northern Jiangsu. According to recent surveys, it has about ten million mu of land. The area of ten counties such as Chuansha in Jiangnan is not comparable to its size. Yancheng County also has six million mu of land, but less than one-third of it has been reclaimed. For this Huai River guiding project, Funing should provide 25,000 laborers. According to County Magistrate Zhang, 21,000 laborers have already arrived and are still being recruited. It is expected that the quota will be exceeded by the end of the month. Yancheng's quota is 15,000, and 11,000 have already arrived. Looking at all the counties, from the county government to the township chiefs, all their energy and financial resources are concentrated on the Huai River guiding project. For counties with smaller populations, such as Jiangyan, Taixing, Gaoyou, etc., funds have been provided, or labor or machinery are used, and the engineering office can handle it themselves, which saves even more time. Last year, the counties had different methods, but after a meeting in the province this spring, they have been changed and standardized. In addition to conducting on-site inspections of the construction sites, Zhao and Shen also went to Funing, Jiancheng, Dongtai, and other counties to discuss implementation with the county government and local figures, and to solve specific problems such as bank loans, food regulation, public security, and hygiene. In order to explore other aspects, the reporter asked local people in each place, in addition to talking with the county magistrate, to inquire about everything from an objective perspective. The main points are as follows: (1) The most serious problem in Funing is bandits. Its northern district borders Xiangshui County, with land like a belt, penetrating into the coast, too far from the county seat, appearing and disappearing unpredictably. It can be said to be a "three no-care" zone. If the police brigade is slightly weak, it will be threatened by bandits. People are wary of bandits, not only travelers are cautious, but also merchants in the counter also need to have inserted guns in the waist when trading with people. The day after the reporter passed Gangshang Town in Jiancheng, there was news that bandits resisted arrest and were shot dead. (2) In Jianyin, Lianshui, Funing, and other counties, there are tens of thousands of guns scattered among the people in each county, but they still feel insufficient to defend against bandits, and the bandit problem is worrying. (3) There are more than ten million mu of wasteland in the counties. Funing Huacheng Reclamation Company has 600,000 mu of land, which can become a county, but less than one-third of it has been reclaimed. There are 6 million mu of saline land, but only about 3 million mu are taxed. Land east of Fantai and low-lying land in the lake are not subject to taxation. (4) The sea is shifting eastward, and the salinity of the land is decreasing, but the central government still requires the old salt producers to produce salt at the same amount as before. Those who produced ten catties a year can now only produce three catties, which is not enough for food and clothing. On the one hand, private salt is promoted, and on the other hand, salt producers are forced to survive. There are still more than a thousand households in Yancheng County who are homeless.

The Progress of the Zhejiang Provincial Aquatic Products Experiment Station - Work Plan Has Been Drafted -

Zeng Yangfu, Director of the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Construction, in order to develop the province's aquatic resources and save the decline of the fishing industry, has planned to establish an aquatic products experiment station to conduct basic research and experiments in fisheries, as a foundation for the national aquatic products construction in the province. At the same time, he plans to organize a new type of fishing industry to guide the people. Chen Tongbai, former technical officer of the Guangdong Provincial Department of Construction and director of the Department of Aquatic Products, has been appointed as the director of the station. It is reported that the station has been officially established in Dinghai, and Chen Zhuanshou, Lin Shuyan, and Wu Zhongyuan have been appointed as technicians, Chen Qiongzhang, Lin Maochun, and Zhang Naigao as technicians, Lü Xianying as the general affairs director, and Wang Xi, Li Fangqi, and others as clerks and accountants.

The work plan proposes to conduct a detailed survey and statistics of the province's fishing conditions, fishery administration, fishing methods, and economic aspects within one or two years. At the same time, it will study important fisheries in Zhejiang Province, such as cuttlefish, yellow croaker, and ribbonfish, in order to improve them. The problem of fish fry, which is related to the national aquaculture industry, is also planned to be included in the work. In terms of manufacturing, it will focus on the cold storage and drying experiments of cuttlefish and yellow croaker. In addition, Zhejiang raises clams, with an annual output of hundreds of thousands of yuan. The station has already started research and experiments to increase production. The seaweed business is currently extremely declining, and the station also plans to have a revival plan.

Nanhui's Gentry Enthusiastically Support Education

Yang Shunquan, a native gentry living in Shanghai, believes that education is the foundation of a country, and rural education is the foundation of education. He has witnessed a sharp increase in the number of school-age children in the Sanjieqiao area of Beicai Town in the county. The county schools are far away. It has only been open for half a year, and the number of students has reached more than 300, with remarkable results. This semester, the school's affairs have been further improved, and the number of students has increased sharply. The original classrooms are not enough to allocate, so he has invested more money to build two more classrooms and opened a farm to implement life education. He has also submitted an application to the Education Bureau for registration. Such efforts to promote education are enough to improve the morality of the world.

Recently, Afu felt that he was approaching seventy years old and still had no children, so he planned to adopt his nephew. Cremating Funeral Items Causes a Fire

Yu Xiangzhou, a resident of Dongguanshe Mountain in front of Mei Garden, has opened an iron shop in Shen Town and has some savings. Recently, Yu died of illness, and his son, Jiasheng, hired monks to chant scriptures to fulfill his filial piety and burned a large number of ghost money and funeral items outside the door. Unexpectedly, the embers flew into the firewood in front of the mountain, causing carelessness. For a time, the wind helped the fire's power, and it was extremely fierce, spreading to the three neighboring families of Yu Jurong, Yu Zhirong, and Yu Xianglin, burning down a total of twelve houses, causing significant losses. Also, in Chenxiang Shanghoubei in the fourth district, yesterday morning, a child playing with fire burned down the houses of Yang Zhirong and Gu Er.

Pessimism About Mulberry Buds Suffering From Frost and Snow

This county is a silkworm and mulberry area. In addition to cultivating rice fields, farmers generally cultivate mulberry fields. During the three seasons of silkworm farming in spring, summer, and autumn, they make considerable profits. In recent years, silkworm and mulberry farming has failed, and farmers have declared bankruptcy. They have all turned mulberry fields into rice fields. Although the provincial government is making every effort to promote it and rehabilitate them, it is not as prosperous as in the past. Since the sudden snowfall on the 21st of this month, the weather has been severe, followed by heavy frost, so that the newly sprouted mulberry buds have been hit and have become withered. According to old farmers, this year's mulberry buds will be difficult to develop, and the price of leaves will definitely be expensive in the future. There is also the wheat crop, which has been crushed by the snow, and the future harvest is expected to be unfavorable.

The Problem of Fine Salt Sales

The Salt Affairs Audit Office of the Ministry of Finance issued instructions to the audit offices in Changlu, Shandong, Huaibei, Liangzhe, and Songjiang, as well as the Yangzi Patrol Bureau and the five tax police bureaus in Su, saying, "Since the promulgation of the fine salt sales method, all fine salt within the jurisdiction of the audit offices in Yangzi and the five districts of Su, within the prescribed sales quota in each port, can be sold smoothly without obstruction. However, if lightly taxed fine salt is transported to areas with higher tax rates, the difference in tax rates should be paid in full and officially released and collected from the place of departure; otherwise, it will be regarded as illicit salt in accordance with Article 5 of the method. Furthermore, since the promulgation of the fine salt sales method, this office has repeatedly warned against tax police interfering with fine salt. Now, we reiterate the previous order that all fine salt sold within this area, within the prescribed sales quota, regardless of the location, if it is not lightly taxed fine salt, the tax police shall not interfere. In addition to separate orders, you should comply with and handle accordingly." It is reported that the tax police authorities stationed in Xi have also received this instruction.

Local News

Polish School Ship Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday; Polish Envoy Weidenthal Led Polish Nationals Aboard to Welcome; Tonight Going to Beijing to Meet Officials from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Navy, etc., Staying in Shanghai for Five Days, Setting Sail for Hong Kong on April 1st

The Polish government's large Dar Pomorze commercial training school ship, carrying 107 crew, professors, and students, departed from the port of Danzig, Poland, on September 16th last year, relying entirely on wind power to sail the ocean around the world, for practical exercises in maritime transport. It arrived in Honolulu on January 18th of this year, Yokohama, Japan, on March 1st, and departed from Nagasaki for Shanghai on the 23rd. It arrived safely in the Huangpu River yesterday afternoon at 5:00 PM, docking at buoy numbers 3 and 4 on the Bund. The Polish Ambassador to China, Weidenthal, personally led representatives of the Polish community to board the ship to welcome them and inquire about various matters, as follows:

Historically Interesting

The Dar Pomorze is not a warship but a school ship used by the Polish government to train merchant marine personnel. The ship is 78.5 meters long, 13.5 meters wide, has a draft of 6.85 meters, and a displacement of 1,566 tons. It is a steel-hulled ship with three masts, resembling the large sailing ships that navigate the oceans in our country in its upper part, but the hull is made entirely of steel, making it similar to a modern transport ship. The design is very artistic. Navigation relies entirely on full sails and wind power. Although it is equipped with a 560-horsepower engine, it is agreed that it will not be used unless it is extremely difficult. The ship's history is even more interesting. The ship was originally manufactured in Germany in 1909 as a commercial training ship for the German government. After the European War, the ship became the property of France. It was not until 1930 that the people of the Pomeranian Province of Poland donated funds to purchase it from France and presented it to the government, hence the name Dar Pomorze, as a permanent memorial.

Staying in Japan for Two Weeks

The ship departed from the port of Danzig, Poland, on September 16th last year, along the Baltic Sea, the islands of Santo Domingo, Cologne, and others, passing through the Panama Canal, and arriving in Honolulu on January 18th of this year, where it was warmly welcomed by the United States. It then crossed the Pacific Ocean and sailed directly to the Far East, arriving in Yokohama on March 1st. After staying for a week, it sailed to Osaka, where it docked for four days. It then stopped in Nagasaki for three days, departing from Nagasaki for Shanghai on the 23rd. The journey was smooth and calm, and it arrived at the Huangpu River at 5:00 PM yesterday afternoon, docking at buoys 3 and 4 on the Bund.

Envoy Personally Welcomed

When the ship sailed into the Huangpu River, its beautiful design and the fact that it was a ship rarely seen in the Far East attracted a large crowd of onlookers on the shore. The ship's hull is painted white, with a pointed bow and three masts. Full of rope ladders, the sails were all unloaded, and it would have been even more beautiful with the sails fully deployed. After docking in the center of the river, Polish Ambassador Weidenthal, accompanied by embassy counselor Wasser, embassy official Morozi, and Mr. and Mrs. Baierzi, chairman of the Polish community in Shanghai, Mr. and Mrs. Grozeski, chairman of the Polish Chamber of Commerce, and dozens of leading Polish nationals in Shanghai, held flowers and boarded the ship to welcome them. Miss Putis Jiaski, representing the Polish community in Shanghai, presented flowers to the ship's captain, Mr. Masic Zhijiyeji, to welcome them. The entire ship has a total of 107 people, including 66 naval students, a captain, training officers, German and English teachers, radio operators, a pastor, and a doctor, totaling 41 people.

Talks with the Captain

A reporter from this newspaper boarded the ship yesterday to visit and met with the captain. According to him, the ship departed from the port of Danzig, Poland, on September 16th last year, along the Baltic Sea, through the Panama Canal, and arrived in Honolulu on January 18th of this year. It then crossed the Pacific Ocean, traveling for 40 days, and arrived in Yokohama, Japan, on March 1st. When approaching the Sea of Japan, it encountered a storm, and the weather was extremely bad. It had no choice but to use the engine to arrive safely at the port. After staying in Yokohama for seven days, it toured famous scenic spots in Tokyo and Nikko. Then, it sailed to Osaka, docked for four days, and then stopped in Nagasaki for three days. It departed from Nagasaki for Shanghai on the 23rd. When sailing the ocean, it relied entirely on wind power and only used the engine near the waters of Yokohama and when entering the port. This is the first time a Polish ship has come to the Far East. He feels very happy to meet people from your country. It is scheduled to stay in Shanghai for five days and sail south to Hong Kong on April 1st, passing through Singapore, Batavia, Saint Helena, Ascension Island in South Africa, and finally, Dover, England, returning to Poland. The voyage is scheduled for one year, as anything longer would be winter, and the weather would be colder, making it inconvenient. Therefore, it cannot stay in each port for too long. As for the purpose of this round-the-world tour, it is to enable students to acquire more practical knowledge and skills. The students' studies focus on the driving skills of commercial liners. The graduation period is 48 months, including two years of classroom instruction and two years of external practice to cultivate specialized personnel for commercial liners. In China, they will visit various Chinese shipping agencies and shipping facilities.

Itinerary

The Polish Consul General in Shanghai, Golesinski, will accompany the ship's captain to the Municipal Government this morning to meet with Mayor Wu and Chen Xunyong, the Deputy Minister of the Navy who is staying in Shanghai. That night at 11:00 PM, the Polish Ambassador, accompanied by the ship's captain and commander, will go to Beijing. Tomorrow morning, they will meet with officials from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Navy, and Communications in Beijing. At noon, they will attend a banquet hosted by the Ministry of the Navy. At 2:00 PM in the afternoon, they will pay respects at the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum. At 5:00 PM, the China-Poland Cultural Association will host a tea party. They will return to Shanghai by night train that evening. On the 29th, at 6:00 PM in the afternoon, the Polish community in Shanghai will host a banquet at the Richard Hotel to welcome them. On the 30th, Mayor Wu, the Deputy Minister of the Navy, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, and the Wusong Merchant Marine School will host banquets and tea parties separately. The ship will invite teachers and students from the Wusong Merchant Marine School to board the ship for a visit. In the afternoon, they will host a reception for newspaper reporters and the Polish community in Shanghai on the ship. On the evening of the 31st, at 8:00 PM, the Polish Ambassador and his wife will host a banquet at the embassy. At 10:30 PM, they will invite people from all walks of life to a tea party at the embassy. On April 1st, the ship will set sail for Hong Kong.

Afterwards, every Tuesday, it will fly from Chongqing to Kunming, and on Thursdays, it will fly from Kunming back to Chongqing. It will only carry mail and will not carry passengers for the time being. The date when passenger service will begin will be announced in the newspaper. To commemorate the opening of the route, commemorative envelopes are available for sale at the Shanghai Postal Administration and the Hankou and Chongqing post offices, or at the Hankou and Chongqing offices of this company. Each envelope sells for 5 cents. There are few remaining, so buyers should purchase them as soon as possible. Also, these envelopes must be mailed from Shanghai before the 27th of this month. This is hereby announced.

Cai Sheng Bai Discusses the Benefits of Acceptance Bills; China Communications Bank and Other Banks Also Agree to Discount Them as Much as Possible; It is Hoped That Both Local and Outlying Areas Will Promote and Implement Them Together

According to the Central News Agency, in order to improve the credit sales system, increase commercial capital, and alleviate the stagnation of transactions, the Shanghai Silk and Satin Industry Association and the Shanghai Electric Silk Weaving Factory Industry Association have established commercial acceptance bills this spring, and several companies have already implemented them. The Central Bank has also agreed to rediscount them. It is learned that the China National Products Production and Sales Cooperative Association is also promoting them. However, some business circles have not fully understood the benefits of promoting commercial acceptance bills. Yesterday, a reporter visited Mr. Cai Sheng Bai, General Manager of Mei Ya Silk Weaving Factory, who was the first to implement commercial acceptance bills. He explained the motives and processes of the promotion in great detail. The record of his talk is as follows:

Beneficial Without Harm

Mr. Cai said that commercial acceptance bills have become very common negotiable instruments in the markets of Europe and the United States. The amount on the bill ranges from tens of thousands of yuan to as low as tens of yuan. Because the credit of the acceptor is reliable and can be redeemed in full when due, banks everywhere can discount them. The discounting location is not limited to the local area. However, in our country, due to commercial habits, the credit sales system is generally valued. Therefore, very few commercial acceptance bills have been implemented in the past. However, Mei Ya Silk Weaving Factory has been implementing them for three years and deeply feels that they are beneficial without harm. When the factory was first established, due to the bankruptcy of the rural economy after the September 18th Incident and the January 28th Incident, the commercial markets in various parts of the country were unusually depressed. If the old-fashioned credit sales system were still used, not only would the danger be worrying, but the stagnation of transactions would be even worse. Therefore, he resolutely took the lead in establishing them. At that time, some silk merchants in various places did not understand the benefits of this type of negotiable instrument, so they inevitably had various concerns and difficulties. However, after making efforts to promote them and explaining them in detail, there are now no difficulties. During these three years, the value of goods traded by the factory using commercial acceptance bills has reached more than 800,000 yuan, and after each bill is cashed at the bank, not only

Dar Pomorze Polish Ship

Page 10

Has there never been an unexpected event, but there has never been a refusal to accept, etc. However, the general merchants value credit sales and it is difficult to change their habits. For this type of acceptance bill, there may be misunderstandings at first. In fact, those who can accept it when it is due show that this merchant

Has Excellent Credit and is Unquestionably Reliable. Old merchants who firmly believe in the credit sales system, when asked to sign and accept a commercial acceptance bill when purchasing goods, may even think that it damages their reputation and affects their dignity. The habit of Chinese commerce is to value verbal credit. Not only must all accounts be settled at the end of the year, but even the sending and receiving of goods at ordinary times do not have receipts. In the past, when the commercial situation was simple, there was no problem, but modern commerce has become increasingly complex, not just personal transactions, but the transactions of companies and groups, and the financial situation is unusually complicated and dense. Therefore, the need to use negotiable instruments is becoming more and more urgent. Therefore, purchasing goods for a certain amount and agreeing on a date of payment is a very common commercial credit. If the payment can be made when it is due, it not only does not damage one's dignity, but also has an excellent reputation. For example, 30 or 40 years ago, businesses and industries regarded it as a shame to pledge their own goods to others for money, which damaged their reputation, so they did it very secretly. But now, with the understanding of the principles of commercial economics, those who pledge their own goods to others for money are actually creditworthy. Therefore, pledging has become a common behavior in commercial and economic operations. Therefore, I believe that after the promotion of commercial acceptance bills, it will gradually become a habit without a doubt. These commercial acceptance bills can also be

Rediscounted in a Circular Manner. For example, A sells goods to B, and issues a bill that B signs and accepts. A can take the bill to Bank A for discounting. Bank A can also rediscount it to Bank B. And B receives A's goods and resells them to C. B can also issue a bill, which C signs and accepts. B can take the bill to the bank for discounting, so that the amount owed for the goods it accepts can be paid correctly when due. With such circular discounting, the stagnant goods can immediately be turned into capital with just one transaction. At the same time, the accounts receivable of all parties can also be turned into promissory notes with just one transaction. How much more lively is the application of this in economics? Therefore, customers who trade with our factory using commercial acceptance bills have known the convenience and are happy to promote it and do not want to continue using the old-fashioned credit sales system, which is clear evidence. Some say that acceptance bills seem to be suitable for promotion in the local area, but not in outlying areas. However, our factory has not only promoted acceptance bills in both local and outlying areas, but customers in outlying areas who trade using acceptance bills have never made any mistakes. Now, the Shanghai Silk and Satin Industry Association and the Shanghai Electric Silk Weaving Factory Industry Association are vigorously promoting them, and the National Products Production and Sales Cooperative Association is also advising all producers and sellers to implement them. Also, China, Transportation, National Products, Shanghai, Silk Industry, and Xinhua Banks have also indicated that they can accept and discount these acceptance bills. With increasing momentum, it is easier to promote them. Therefore, it is hoped that all industries

Will Promote Together. First, break the old concept of a one-year settlement of the credit sales system, and understand that after promoting acceptance bills, financial capital can be increased (that is, the stagnant accounts receivable can be used as current funds at the same time), and the accounts receivable can be turned into promissory notes, which have more precise guarantees in the bill law. Then, everyone will be happy to promote them. However, in the early stages of establishment, there will inevitably be various difficulties. But with the result of hard work and progress, it can definitely be implemented nationwide. However, this matter is a new beginning, and it is difficult for one industry and one company to implement it. In particular, it is necessary for the trade associations of various ports and industries to convene meetings to resolve and implement it together, which will be easier to do. Now, the Shanghai Silk Industry Association and the Electric Silk Weaving Factory Industry Association have resolved to implement it from April 1st. Therefore, it is hoped that the major companies and stores in this city and outlying areas will work together to promote and implement it together, so that no problems will occur in acceptance. Then, not only can Shanghai promote it to various ports without obstacles, but other ports can also continue to promote it to other ports. Then, the goods of national industry and commerce can be cashed at any time in the form of negotiable instruments, and the financial flow is not hindered, and the business progresses indefinitely. It is certain that the negotiable instrument can be manipulated.

Representatives of Cotton Merchants from Three Provinces Request Increased Taxes on Foreign Cotton to Maintain the Domestic Cotton Industry

A telegram from representatives of Shaanxi, Shanxi, and Henan cotton merchants in Shanghai to the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing states: Your Excellency, Ministry of Finance, our country is an agricultural country, and most farmers rely on cotton production for their livelihoods. In recent years, the government has spared no effort in developing the Northwest to improve cotton quality and increase production. Therefore, last year's output increased greatly, which is sufficient to meet the country's annual consumption. Now, foreign cotton is imported and sold at low prices, and various yarn factories are purchasing it in large quantities, resulting in a surplus of Chinese cotton and a daily decline in prices. If this is not stopped quickly, money will flow out, the countryside will go bankrupt, and the impact on the national economy and the people's livelihood will be profound and significant. Moreover, the number of cotton merchants in Shanxi, Shaanxi, Henan, Shandong, Shanghai, and Wuhan is no less than a thousand, with capital of no less than tens of millions, accounting for a large part of Shanghai's commerce. Now, they are being oppressed by foreign cotton and cannot sustain themselves. If they go bankrupt, not only will Shanghai be greatly affected, but commerce in various places will also decline, and there will be no hope for the revival of the rural economy. All countries in the East and West levy heavy taxes on imported foreign goods to resist them. Our country's tariffs are now autonomous. We should ask the Ministry to follow this example and quickly impose heavy taxes on foreign cotton to plug the leak and maintain the cotton industry. We are anxiously awaiting orders. Yang Yizhai, Guo Lizhai, Jie Qingxuan, Geng Zhijing, Zhang Yuwen, Mao Tingfang, Sun Ruitang, and Xiong Zhipu, representatives of cotton merchants from Shaanxi, Shanxi, and Henan in Shanghai, kowtow together. Sent on the 23rd.

Qian Chengxu Returns to Shanghai from Shandong; Suggests a Raw Material Loan Plan

According to the Ta Kung Pao, Dr. Qian Chengxu, an official of the China Industrial Federation, was invited by Han Fuju, Chairman of the Shandong Provincial Government, to go to Shandong on the 4th of this month to discuss the rescue of Shandong's rural economy and to plan the dredging of local products and the revitalization of commerce. After about two decades, he left Shandong on the 23rd and returned to Shanghai. Yesterday, reporters from the Ta Kung Pao visited the federation and Mr. Qian told them about his visit to Shandong and expressed his opinions on the raw material loan and the procedures for implementing it. The details are recorded as follows:

Raw Material Loan According to Mr. Qian, he was invited by Chairman Han of the Shandong Provincial Government to go to Shandong to discuss the rural economy and to ask for planning. In the current situation where Shandong's industrial capital is affected by the sluggish market, how should local products be dredged for sale in order to remedy the situation? After meeting with Han, I suggested unifying the industry, appropriately drawing a part of the property from farmers and businessmen, organizing a joint warehouse, issuing securities, selling them at low prices in the market, and absorbing cash. When the cash flowed back, the securities would be redeemed with cash to activate local product trade. After a long period of discussion, it was believed that Shandong's industry has not yet reached the stage of unification, and the proposed plan seems difficult to implement in practice. I was asked to come up with a second plan. Then I proposed estimating Shandong's raw materials and asking the financial community in the outlying markets to add accounting capital to facilitate turnover. While the issue was being discussed, the Shanghai China Industrial Federation published the Industrial and Commercial Finance Research Report written by financial experts Zhang Naiqi, Yang Yinpu, and Zhang Xiaomei. The principles for creating a modern capital market set forth in the report are relatively close. Therefore, in the end, I also suggested to Chairman Han that Shandong should issue a raw material credit loan of 25 million yuan, entrusting financial institutions with the existing cotton, tobacco, raw coal, peanuts, silk, and various important raw materials to make credit loans in the market to activate commerce. After six months, the original handling agency is responsible for repaying the loan. Chairman Han expressed great approval for this and contacted local merchants privately many times. The result was very satisfactory. I have telegraphed Mr. Han again, asking him to formally acknowledge and express his opinions on the suggestion in writing to complete the formalities. Once the reply arrives, I will collect all the documents and send them to the Shanghai Banking Association to ask for a special discussion on the matter. In short, Shanghai is short of cash, and industry and commerce are feeling the pinch. If Shandong can issue 25 million yuan of goods as credit, then Shanghai will have 25 million yuan more capital for turnover, which will be of great benefit to both production and sales.

Implementation Procedures As for the implementation procedures of the plan, they are tentatively set as follows: (1) From the private side, the intentions are orally explained to Chairman Han. After he agrees, contact the Jinan financial community to solicit their consent. (2) If the Jinan financial community thinks it is feasible, start consulting private opinions from the industrial and financial circles in Shanghai. (3) After the private contacts between Shanghai's financial and industrial circles are roughly on track, the private opinion is sent to Chairman Han in writing, asking him to express his approval. (4) After Chairman Han receives the private letter, he replies to the sender with his approval. (5) After the private person receives the written reply from Chairman Han, he/she visits the financial and industrial circles to make a general decision. (6) To make the opinions of all parties consistent, the industrial and commercial circles or the Industrial Federation officially issue an opinion, declaring their position, and at the same time, the points of the proposal are officially sent to Chairman Han of Shandong for consideration. (7) After receiving this official document, Chairman Han submits it to the Provincial Affairs Meeting for discussion of the principles, or convenes a meeting of local financial industry representatives to decide on a preliminary plan at any time without going through the Provincial Affairs Meeting. The plan is then officially sent to the person in charge of Shanghai's industrial circles in writing. (8) After receiving the plan set by Chairman Han, the person in charge in Shanghai officially convenes the relevant industrial leaders to jointly study and decide on detailed measures. At the same time, a joint meeting is held with financial leaders to negotiate on various conditions such as guaranteeing the loan. (9) After the conditions are decided, both parties begin to negotiate the organization. (10) When the organization of the institution is completed, the private task is over.

Treasury Ministry's Telegram Reply to the Chamber of Commerce: Request to Abolish the Saltpeter and Sulfur Contractor System, and Order the Saltpeter and Sulfur Bureau to Comply with Established Regulations

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, along with the Porcelain Industry Trade Association, the National Goods Products Trade Association, and the Industrial Joint Stock Company, jointly sent a letter and telegram to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, concerning the collection of fees from saltpeter and sulfur contractors. Yesterday, a telegram reply was received from the Ministry of Finance, the original text of which is as follows: "Regarding the telegrams previously received by this Ministry from Shanghai Tianli Company, Kaicheng Acid Manufacturing Company, Jiangsu Pharmaceutical Factory, and the Shanghai Chemical Raw Materials Trade Association, requesting the revocation of the Jiangsu Province Saltpeter and Sulfuric Acid Exclusive Sales Office, this Ministry has already instructed the Salt Affairs Department to order the Jiangsu Saltpeter and Sulfur Bureau to state that sulfur and nitric acid are types of saltpeter and sulfur products, for which the Jiangsu Saltpeter and Sulfur Transportation and Sales Office has been collecting residual profits. Upon the expiration of the current contractor term, the area covered by the Saltpeter and Sulfur Transportation and Sales Office will be demarcated, and a separate office will be established to solicit merchants to handle the business, originally for the sake of convenient management and the elimination of monopolies. The previous regulation of one yuan per box for residual profits has not been increased. We immediately instructed the merchants to take note and ordered that the name of the Jiangsu Province Saltpeter and Sulfuric Acid Exclusive Sales Office be changed to the Jiangsu Province Saltpeter and Sulfuric Acid Transportation and Sales Office to avoid misunderstandings. Furthermore, the selling price of Chilean saltpeter is clearly stipulated in the contract undertaken by the Xinli Company, stating that in addition to the cost of remaining warehouse rent, insurance, and consumption, it shall not exceed 15% of the purchase price. The telegrams state that the price at which Xinli Company sells Chilean saltpeter is twice the price on the foreign market per ton, and that sulfur and nitric acid should not be used as an excuse to force manufacturers to pay double the price. After reviewing the original case, it is found to be inconsistent. In addition to ordering the Jiangsu Saltpeter and Sulfur Bureau to investigate whether excessive residual profits are being collected and prices are being raised, and strictly instructing all transportation and sales offices to comply with established regulations, please take note. (Official seal of the Ministry of Finance)"

Red Swastika Society Burial Team Reports on Recent Work in Jiangxi: Piles of Skulls, Tombs Built of White Bones, Such Heartbreaking and Tragic Sights

Jiangxi Province is suffering from both banditry and drought, and the situation is dire. The World Red Swastika Society elected a president to lead three relief teams, carrying clothing, rice, and medicine, to various disaster areas to provide assistance. This has already been reported in various newspapers. It is also reported that the society found corpses and skeletons scattered everywhere in the disaster areas, and rudimentary graves that urgently needed to be taken care of. Previously, a burial team was organized and sent to the Guangchang and Ningdu areas to specialize in burial work. The team members were all selected for their perseverance, hard work, and experience in burial. Now, we have obtained a recent work report from the team, which is published below:

Our team departed from Nanchang on January 28th, and assigned team members to Ningdu and Guangchang counties to specialize in burial work. In Guangchang, many exposed corpses were buried in the Toupo Town area under the county's jurisdiction, and countless scattered remains and bones were collected along the way. In addition, graves buried in the riverbank area were scattered by flash floods. As spring approaches, there is a risk of epidemics. Team members have been dispatched to handle this matter. On January 30th, we arrived in Ningdu and stayed at the Liao Clan Ancestral Hall in Xuechi Lane, sharing the premises with the Second Relief Team. On February 3rd, we began work. For more than twenty days since then, we have been traveling to the mountains near the city every day to carry out burials. Except for days when we were unable to work due to rain, we have buried a total of 531 exposed corpses in places such as the mountains to the east, the Dongxue Ridge and Dapo to the south, the Weibei Ridge, Macao Ridge, Beauty Hair Dispersing Ridge (i.e., the execution ground), Fengyu Pavilion, Yinduo Mountain, Battery Mountain, Elephant Skin Beach, and Songpi Cheng to the west, and the Beitang Ridge to the north. There are also countless rudimentary graves that have been reinforced with soil. In addition, more than 400 skulls and thousands of dry bones have been collected and piled up at Beauty Hair Dispersing Ridge (it is said that thousands of people were killed here, making it the most tragic place in Ningdu), forming a bone mountain. All organizations passing by cannot help but sigh and pay their respects. Because General Chen Cheng of the 18th Army wants to build a White Bone Pagoda on the spot to leave a permanent memorial, we have not yet started construction. There are still many other mountains where we are continuing to work. Furthermore, more than ten li northeast of the city is Cuifeng Peak, a famous scenic spot in Ningdu. The solitary peak stands independently and soars into the clouds, with cliffs thousands of feet on all sides. However, there is a crack, only a foot wide, that leads directly to the top of the peak. It is only wide enough for one person to climb. There are no stone steps, and one must rely entirely on the strength of one's hands and feet, supporting oneself on the left and right. If one were to lose one's footing halfway, one would fall thousands of feet and one's bones would be crushed. The danger is enough to make one shiver. Curious people often try to climb to the top, but give up halfway due to exhaustion. It is said that there were more than 300 households on the top of the mountain, who were surrounded by bandits for more than two years. Due to lack of food, they either starved to death or were slaughtered, leaving many corpses. Our team, inspired by a spirit of charity, led all the team members to bravely go straight up, fortunately without stopping. The area at the top of the peak is two or three li, surrounded by trees, with hundreds of acres of fertile land and hundreds of houses, most of which have been burned down, with broken tiles and crumbling walls, a desolate sight. Bones are scattered everywhere. Our team collected more than twenty piles of large and small bones and buried them on the spot. Furthermore, seventy li northeast of the city, in the Changsheng Town Huangcun area of the Third District, it is said that more than a thousand people were killed and buried along the riverbank. Many of them were washed away by mountain floods, but several hundred remained unwashed. On February 21st, team members were sent to collect and bury them, building two large white bone tombs, and it is planned to mark them with stone tablets to make them permanent. Further details will be reported later.

International Trade Bureau Introduces Domestic Products: White Wax, Soybeans, Hair Nets, Bedspreads, Carpets, and Embroidered Goods

According to the International Trade Bureau, the bureau is a government agency that aims to promote direct foreign trade and is responsible for providing guidance and introductions, without any profit motive. Manufacturers should not misunderstand this. The domestic products recently requested by foreign merchants are listed below: Insect wax, also known as white wax, is a secretion of insects that live on trees and is a special product of Sichuan Province. The areas where the insects and the trees are produced are different. The insects are produced in Jianwei, Ya'an, and Huili, on the border of Sichuan and Yunnan, spanning hundreds of miles. Tens of thousands of people make a living by raising insect wax. The trees grow in Jiading, Sichuan, and the insect species must be transferred to Jiading every year to produce wax. China's candle-making industry must use white wax on the surface of candles to prevent them from melting easily. In addition, it is used in pharmacies to make wax shells to protect valuable medicines. In Europe and America, it is often used to manufacture cosmetics, decorations, and toys. A certain company in Mexico has sent a letter requesting 1,000 kilograms of white wax. Exporters can send a letter to the bureau for guidance and introduction. Furthermore, the Belgian Société Anonyme d'Importation et d'Exportation Quatre Soeurs needs shimmering large clam shells. The Cairo Brothers Company of Liverpool, England, needs soybeans. A certain company in Finland needs bamboo poles, coconut coir, and Manila hemp rope. A New York Italian Bedding Import and Export Company is seeking hair nets, bedspreads, carpets, bedding, and embroidered goods. Domestic manufacturers engaged in the above-mentioned goods can send a letter to the bureau for introduction. The address is the fourth floor of the Bank of China Building, New Rubbish Bridge.

Gaoqiao Rural Improvement Society Organizes Mutual Aid Loans for Farmers and Improves Cotton Planting and Promotes Women's Production; General Meeting of All Members to Be Held on the Sixth of Next Month

Since the Gaoqiao Rural Improvement Society established an experimental zone in Xingang last year, it has spared no effort in improving rural education and other aspects. Now, in order to develop the rural economy, the society plans to organize mutual aid loans for farmers, improve rice planting, and promote women's production. A general meeting of all members will be held on a scheduled date. The details are as follows:

Organizing Mutual Aid Loans

In order to develop the rural economy, the society plans to organize small mutual aid loans for farmers. The society has already negotiated with the Shanghai Bank. The society will investigate farmers who actually need loans. If farmers need to purchase seeds, plowing cattle, and fertilizer, they can borrow mutual aid loans from the society, which will be underwritten by the Shanghai Bank. All interest rates will be extremely low, and it will be officially launched soon.

Improving Cotton Seeds

The society believes that the cotton seeds planted near Gaoqiao are not of good quality, which greatly affects farmers' income. In view of this, the society is improving cotton seeds and has purchased Jiangyin Baizi seeds, encouraging farmers to switch to planting them. If the harvest from planting this improved seed is less than that of ordinary cotton seeds, the society will be responsible for compensation. Therefore, the local people are willing to switch to planting Jiangyin cotton seeds.

Promoting Women's Production

The society also believes that it is necessary to reform the situation where women do not engage in production. It has formulated a plan to promote women's production, which will be gradually implemented. The women's supplementary school attached to the society will be the center for promoting this matter. The students in the class will encourage women to join. It has been decided to first organize embroidery and craftwork, which is currently being trained. It has been specially contracted with major embroidery factories. If this matter is implemented, women can earn six or seven yuan per month.

Scheduled General Meeting

The society has also scheduled a general meeting of all members for the sixth of next month. In addition to reporting on the society's affairs over the past year, the society's affairs will be discussed after the meeting. Mr. Wang Kuizheng, the general manager of the society, is currently drafting a plan to promote the society's affairs for discussion at the general meeting.
