Judge Xiong Huiping interrogated him repeatedly and brought Zhao and Zhang to court to question Wang. Later, Judge Xiong was transferred to the High Court's Third Branch, and Judge Sun Pengxian took over the case, announcing a new trial and rescheduling it pending further study of the case. This was reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday, Judge Sun continued the trial in Criminal Court No. 2. Attorney Gu Shouxi appeared in court on behalf of the Police Department. The defendant's defense attorneys, Shen Xingxia and Zhang Qikai, arrived in court on time. Zhao and Zhang were again brought to the stand for questioning. The defendant, Wang Xinggao, still vehemently claimed innocence, denying any involvement in the instigation and stating that he had been falsely accused. The official questioned Zhao and Zhang, who testified as before. The court then summoned West Constable Lang Bole, Detective Qian Yumin, and Informant Guo Shaorong, who handled the case for the police. The court found that the investigation and evidence were complete and ordered the start of the closing arguments. After arguments between the police attorney and the defendant's attorneys, the court announced the end of the closing arguments and scheduled a judgment for April 1st. The defendant was returned to the detention center, and Zhao and Zhang were sent back to prison.

Hengyuan Shenji Fishmonger Shop's Closure Dispute: Shareholders' Opinions Differ; Lawyer Accused of Sealing the Business

Hengyuan Shenji Pickled Fish Shop, located at No. 25, 16th Embankment, Nanshi, was established as a joint venture. Shareholder Wang Tingsheng was elected as manager. On the night of March 7th of this year, Wang Tingsheng entrusted lawyer Li Ming to send people with dozens of the lawyer's seals to seal the business. All goods and equipment were sealed. The shareholders considered this action by lawyer Li and Wang Tingsheng to be an obstruction of their rights. Therefore, they hired lawyer Lu Congzu to file a private prosecution with the Criminal Court of the District Court, stating that Hengyuan Shenji Pickled Fish Shop is

a joint venture,

with each share costing 1,500 yuan, for a total of ten shares, with a total capital of 15,000 yuan. The first defendant, Wang Tingsheng, owns three shares, worth 4,500 yuan. The plaintiff, Hu Shaotang, owns two shares, worth 3,000 yuan. There are five other people: Zhu Jicai, Lu Wenping, Xu Yisheng, Lu Wenqin, and Mrs. Liu Hu (wife of Liu Huafeng), each owning one share. Now, the first defendant, in collusion with the second defendant, lawyer Li Ming, has sealed the business without authorization, suspending operations, which obstructs the exercise of rights. Therefore, they are filing a lawsuit according to law. The defendant, Wang Tingsheng, submitted a response, stating that the Hengyuan Shenji Pickled Fish Shop was founded by his late father and has been in operation for more than 40 years. After his father's death, Tingsheng took over as manager, also for nearly ten years. Later, some old shareholders withdrew and

new shares were recruited,

for a total of ten shares, with a capital of 15,000 yuan. Tingsheng owns three shares and is still elected as manager. Since the January 28th Incident, business has declined. For several years, he has been struggling to manage without loss. However, recently, affected by the sluggish market, by February 3rd of this year (the end of the lunar year), the losses were very large and he could not make ends meet. On February 7th, the fourth day of the first lunar month, known as the day to welcome the God of Wealth, the plaintiff, Xu Yisheng (associate), notified the rice cook and warehouse staff not to buy the festive items used to welcome the God of Wealth, saying that the shareholders had no intention of doing business. As a result, the God of Wealth was not welcomed according to custom, and the staff were alarmed. Tingsheng believed that

the store was founded by his father

and he could not bear to see the hard work of decades collapse in one day. That night, he invited the shareholders to a meeting to discuss ways to maintain the business. However, the plaintiffs, holding seven shares, unanimously stated that they had no intention of doing business. Tingsheng, for the sake of the shareholders' interests and the livelihoods of the staff, repeatedly pleaded, but the plaintiffs were resolute and nothing came of it. Tingsheng, in order to protect the interests of creditors and reduce the losses of shareholders, had no choice but to legally entrust lawyer Li Ming to liquidate the business, and his conscience

is clear.

As for the second defendant, lawyer Li Ming, responded according to the law and filed a counterclaim, alleging that the plaintiffs, Zhu Yicai and others, falsely accused him of colluding to obstruct the exercise of rights. In his response, he stated that Wang Tingsheng, as a shareholder and manager, is the legal representative of the shop and his appointment for liquidation is a legitimate act that he should perform in his capacity. How can it be considered illegal? The counterclaimant advertised the liquidation and implemented the sealing. This sealing is a necessary stage in the custody process and cannot be compared with the seizure enforced by a court or other official agency. Seizure is accompanied by legal coercion, while sealing is the same as the party's own

closing of the door

to stop trading, or the liquidator sending someone to guard it and stop entry and exit. It does not involve any coercion. The plaintiffs falsely accuse him of seizure, which is a deliberate attempt to frame him. When a liquidator seals and inventories assets, his authority originates from the appointment of the parties and is an act of custody. It is very different from the seizure of other people's property by a court or official agency, which involves detention. Parties are free to operate normally, but when they close their doors to stop business or seal their own property in their possession, there is no need to cooperate with police officers. The liquidator's

execution of the sealing

or guarding, and even the removal procedures, is no different in nature from what the parties themselves do, and there is no reason to cooperate with the police. The plaintiffs are distorting the law and deliberately fabricating facts of collusion, violence, and coercion in a civil dispute in order to subject the respondent to criminal penalties. The plaintiffs have clearly committed a crime under Article 180, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code. After receiving the complaint, Judge Chen Kangsun summoned the plaintiffs and the defendant (the counterclaimant) Wang Tingsheng and Li Ming to court for questioning yesterday afternoon. The plaintiff Xu Yisheng, accompanied by a lawyer, and the defendants Wang Tingsheng and Li Ming, also hired three lawyers, Shen Junru, Ge Zhitan, and Li Shirui, to appear in court

to defend them.

The plaintiff Xu Yisheng, 28 years old, from Ningbo, testified that lawyer Li Ming sealed the business and demanded compensation for losses. Wang Tingsheng refused to hand over all the accounting books. Although the capital of 15,000 yuan has been reduced by more than 12,000 yuan, there are still more than 20,000 yuan in savings, which can still be maintained. Wang Tingsheng did not consult with the shareholders and closed the business rashly. The judge asked and obtained the testimony, saying, "Is it not that your shareholders did not intend to operate, and therefore closed down?" Xu replied, "That's not right. Wang Tingsheng did not consult with us. We posted a notice on the 9th, and he did not come to negotiate." Next, Li Ming testified that he was entrusted by Wang Tingsheng and acted entirely according to the wishes of the parties. Finally, Wang Tingsheng testified that he convened a meeting of the shareholders and they unanimously did not intend to continue the business. The judge asked, "If they agreed, why are they making things difficult for you?" He replied, "I don't know." The judge then said to the two lawyers, "Today, only one plaintiff, Xu Yisheng, is present, but Li Ming and others have already filed a counterclaim. The plaintiffs must appear in person at the next hearing." The hearing was adjourned.

Can Smoke Ash Cure Tuberculosis? Unscrupulous Doctor Accused; Case Transferred to the District Court for Investigation

Cai Wanjie (the deceased) was 31 years old, a native of Yancheng, and resided at No. 25, Qiu'an Lane, Changan Road, under the jurisdiction of the Hengfeng Road Police Station in Zhabei. He worked as a rickshaw puller and had some savings. Unfortunately, Cai suffered from pulmonary tuberculosis in the second half of last year. Later, through an introduction, he was examined by Feng Xiaofu, a doctor from Taizhou (who did not have a license or a health bureau certificate), who lived at No. 134 Jinling Road. Feng instructed Cai to take pills. From last year until Cai's death, Feng charged him 40 to 50 yuan for pills. Until the morning before his death, the deceased's wife asked about her husband's condition, and Feng replied that he had passed the danger period. However, at around 9:00 PM that night, Cai passed away. After the remaining pills taken by the deceased were tested, it was discovered that the pills were made by Feng using opium smoke ash mixed with other harmless ingredients. They were heated over a lamp and had the smell of opium smoke. Therefore, it was known that Feng Xiaofu was using deceptive means to swindle money. The deceased's brother, Cai Shiduan, reported Feng Xiaofu's medical malpractice to the Hengfeng Road Police Station. After receiving the report, Director Lu Pei immediately summoned Feng for questioning, reported to the Inspectorate of the Public Security Bureau, and ordered Lu Abao, the local representative of the twelfth district, to file a report with the Shanghai District Court for an autopsy. At around 2:00 PM, Coroner Du Jiasheng, together with Recorder Jiang Shaojie, arrived at the scene and confirmed that the deceased, Cai Wanjie, had died of illness. The corpse was returned to the family for preparation of the coffin and burial. Feng Xiaofu and the plaintiff Cai Shiduan were questioned by Director Lu. Because the case involved allegations of medical malpractice causing death, the plaintiff and defendant were immediately sent to the Zhabei Branch of the Third Section of the Public Security Bureau and were transferred to the Shanghai District Court yesterday afternoon for investigation and handling.

Suicide of Upper-Class Traveler at the Fair Hotel; No Possessions or Suicide Note; True Identity Uncertain

At 11:30 p.m. on the 24th, a middle-aged man with a local accent and neatly dressed checked into the Fair Hotel at No. 291, next door to Baoyu Lane on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession. He claimed to be Liu Jihua, 32 years old, from Shanghai, and engaged in the foreign goods business. A receptionist led him upstairs and booked room 30 for him. After paying the room fee, he went out again and did not return to the hotel until 1:30 a.m., when he entered the room, closed the door, and went to sleep. It is unknown what caused him to take poison and commit suicide that night. After swallowing the poison, he lay on the bed fully clothed, waiting for death to arrive. At noon the next day, Han Yingguan (32 years old), a tea boy from Songjiang, noticed that he was still sleeping soundly and had not gotten up. Following routine, he knocked on the door and asked if the room was to be extended. After calling out for a long time, there was no response from inside the room. Realizing something was wrong, he managed to pry open the door, which was bolted from the inside. Upon entering, he found Liu lying supine on the bed, fully clothed. Upon touching him, he found that he had already died and his body was cold. He immediately informed the front desk and reported it to the French police, who sent detectives to investigate. An empty box of prepared opium was found next to the pillow. There were no other possessions or a suicide note left behind, so the reason for his suicide is unknown. There is also no way to contact his family. The body was transported to the Tongren Fuyuan sub-hall for preservation. Yesterday, a report was submitted to the Special No. 2 Court, and Prosecutor Wang Ren, along with forensic doctors Wei and Jiang, and Clerk Zhao, etc., were dispatched to the hall at noon to examine the body. It was confirmed that the deceased had died by taking poison before death. The court convened a hearing. After the detective reported the case, the witness, tea boy Han Yingguan, was questioned about the circumstances of the discovery. It was ordered that the body be handed over to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall for photographing, encoffining, and burial, pending identification by relatives. However, whether the deceased's name is genuine is still difficult to determine. The body was wearing a gray lined spring jacket, a melon-cap, coffee-colored woolen socks, and gray Walter's呢shoes. He had delicate features, a medium build, and appeared to be an upper-class person.

Brief Biography

Shi Qingyang was from Chongqing, Sichuan Province, and a licentiate. He studied at Chongqing Middle School and later studied sericulture in Japan. He joined the Tongmenghui (Revolutionary Alliance) in Tokyo, Japan, and followed Sun Yat-sen in the revolution. At the end of the Qing Dynasty, he returned to Sichuan under Sun's orders and served as a director of the Tongmenghui in Chongqing. During the Chongqing Restoration in 1911, he led the suicide squad and later served as the commander of the Volunteer Army. He was reorganized as the commander of the 20th Regiment of the 5th Division of the Sichuan Army. During the anti-Yuan Shikai campaign in 1913, he served as the commander of the Guerrilla Forces in northern Sichuan. After the failure of the campaign, he fled to Japan and joined the Chinese Revolutionary Party. In 1915, during the so-called National Protection War against Yuan Shikai, our party first organized the Chinese Revolutionary Army. Despite the difficulties, the banner of the Chinese Revolutionary Army was still raised. Only Qingyang in Xiyang, Xiushan, and Pengshui in Sichuan, Zhu Zhixin in Xiangshan, Guangdong, and Ju Zheng in Ju County, Shandong, rose up. In 1917, during the National Pacification War, he was appointed by Sun Yat-sen as the Pacification Commissioner of northern Sichuan and fought bitterly against the enemy on the south bank of Chongqing with the Guizhou Army. He also served as the commander-in-chief of the guerrilla army and subsequently captured Shunqing, Guang'an, and other counties. In 1918, the Guangzhou Military Government specially awarded Qingyang the rank of Lieutenant General in the Army to commend his contributions. He then served as the Commander-in-Chief of the First Route Army of the Yunnan-Sichuan National Pacification Army in aid of Shaanxi, the Commander of the 6th Division of the Sichuan Army, and the concurrently as the Jialing Dao尹. In 1921, he followed Sun Yat-sen on the Northern Expedition and was stationed in Guilin, serving as a counselor in the General Headquarters. In 1922, he was ordered to return to Sichuan to comfort the troops, and then ordered to lead his old troops to suppress bandits, serving as the Commander-in-Chief of the First Route Army of the Sichuan Bandit Suppression Army and the concurrently as the Commander-in-Chief of the Eastern Sichuan Border Defense. In 1923, at the First National Congress of our party, he was appointed by Sun Yat-sen and elected as a member of the Central Executive Committee. At that time, Qingyang, with his two divisions and one mixed brigade, had been fighting in Sichuan for two years and was defeated and stationed on the border. He deeply felt the necessity of uniting the Southwest and suggested to Sun Yat-sen that Tang Jiyao be appointed as the Deputy Marshal, which was approved. He then left his troops and traveled to Guangdong and Guangxi. Just as things were about to succeed, Sun Yat-sen passed away shortly after going north, so he stayed in Beiping and formed the Zhongshe. Later, the youth in the North who adhered to the party's principles and resisted the Communist bandits actually had the Zhongshe as their core. In 1925, he returned to Sichuan and was arrested by Wu Peifu in Hankou because his bandit suppression army had intercepted the ships carrying arms and ammunition that Wu was transporting to Sichuan. People from all sides, both North and South, came to his aid, and he was spared from disaster. In 1927 and 1928, he traveled to the three provinces of Sichuan, Yunnan, and Guizhou, making various arrangements for the party's forces and mediating their disputes from time to time. In 1929, he came to Nanjing and was appointed as the Special Commissioner for the Development of Yunnan and Kangding, but he did not go. He was appointed as a member of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission. In 1932, he was appointed as the Chairman of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission. In March of this year, he resigned due to illness and sought medical treatment. At 5:05 p.m. on March 25th, he passed away at the Maierong Hospital in Shanghai at the age of 57.

"Stop Spitting" Campaign to be Mobilized Tomorrow; Spitting is a Major Cause of Tuberculosis Transmission; 1.6 Million People Die from Tuberculosis Every Year

The Shanghai Anti-Tuberculosis Association's "Stop Spitting" campaign rally is scheduled to be mobilized starting tomorrow. Details are as follows:

Declaration of the Rally: The Declaration of the "Stop Spitting" Campaign Rally states, "The harm of tuberculosis is well known to everyone. Because we lack common sense and are ignorant of prevention, the number of people sacrificed each year is about one million six hundred thousand, and there are even more patients. Why is there so much tuberculosis in China? There are many reasons, but we believe that spitting everywhere is the biggest reason. We can often see people spitting casually on buses, trams, roads, movie theaters, and public places. It must be known that spitting casually is the biggest cause of spreading tuberculosis bacteria, because the patient's bacteria can be spread on the ground or fly in the air, leading to the transmission of tuberculosis. If we want to prevent tuberculosis from spreading, we should try our best to eliminate the bad habit of spitting everywhere. Spitting should be done in a spittoon, gutter, handkerchief, or paper, because the sputum in the spittoon and gutter will not spread, and the handkerchief can be boiled in boiling water, disinfected, and then washed clean with soap, and the paper can be burned. The above words are our sincere advice to everyone in the "Stop Spitting Everywhere Campaign", and at the same time, we sincerely ask everyone to implement them conscientiously. Finally, please pay special attention: (1) Persuade against spitting everywhere on roads, buses, and public places. (2) Spitting everywhere is spreading tuberculosis. (3) Spitting everywhere is tantamount to murder. (4) Spitting should be done in a spittoon, gutter, handkerchief, or paper."

Chamber of Commerce Notice: The first day is Student Day, the second day is Workers' Day, the third day is Merchants' Day, and the fourth day is Various Groups' Day. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday issued a notice to various trade associations, which stated, "Regarding the notification of the Shanghai Anti-Tuberculosis Association's initiation of the Shanghai 'Stop Spitting' campaign and the organization of the Shanghai 'Stop Spitting' Campaign Rally Preparatory Committee, multiple joint meetings have been convened with various agencies, and it has been decided that March 30th will be Merchants' Day, during which the Chamber of Commerce will lead merchants in a widespread 'Stop Spitting' campaign. In addition to the declaration to be issued by the Chamber of Commerce on that day, the slogans and circulars issued by the Preparatory Committee are hereby forwarded. We hope that you will check and forward them to your affiliated factories or shops, and post them in conspicuous places to raise awareness and maintain public health. We sincerely hope for your cooperation."

An Old Thief with Gray Hair Commits Theft; Has Been Imprisoned Repeatedly but Remains Unrepentant; Deceives Women and Robs Them of Their Jewelry; Pretends to Be Senile and Answers Questions Irrelevantly During Trial

Chen Fuqing from Nanjing, now sixty years old, has gray hair and a long beard. Since his youth, he has been idle and engaged in burglary, robbery, and fraud. He has been arrested by the police multiple times, but because his sentences were short, he was soon released after being imprisoned. It was not until 1931 that he was sentenced to five years in prison for a major fraud case, but he was soon granted amnesty, so he never remained a prisoner for long. Even after being released from prison, his bad habits persisted into old age, and he has become even more daring. Relying on his elderly appearance, he pretends to be a rustic peasant and loiters in various entertainment venues all day long. When he sees someone who can be deceived, whether male or female, he uses different tricks depending on the person, and most fall into his trap. Such a person is truly an old and useless man. Now, this scourge of society has been arrested again for committing a crime. The incident involves a woman named Zhong Yuan, who is thirty-four years old. Although she is middle-aged, she has not lost her alluring nature. Her husband, Zhong Jiaxin, is working in Zhenjiang, and the woman, unable to bear being alone, often goes to various entertainment venues in the evening, ostensibly for amusement, but her real intention is not for pleasure. On the afternoon of the 15th of this month, the woman went to the Tianyun Building of Wing On Company as usual. While visiting the Civilization Theater, she happened to meet Chen Fuqing. Chen, being an experienced con artist, naturally knew at first sight what to do. He immediately put on various displays in front of the woman, making sure that she saw the ring on his finger and the watch hanging from his chest, and then he took out a huge wad of banknotes and pretended to be counting them. He spared no effort in showing off his wealth. The woman was indeed lured by the glittering gold and colorful banknotes, and sweet words soon made her follow Chen's lead. They went together to the Unity Hotel on Avenue Edward VII. Chen, using the alias Gu Liufa, booked room 22. After the waiter left the room, Chen immediately offered the woman a cup of fragrant tea. She took the cup and drank with him. As soon as the woman drank the tea, she became dazed and speechless, and Chen could do whatever he wanted with her. Chen did not bother to become intimate with her, but immediately took the only objects he was after - a gold ring and a ring with three small diamonds - from the woman's fingers and left. Half an hour later, the woman woke up and realized that Chen was gone and her jewelry was also missing. She realized that she had been conned and quietly left the hotel to report to the Old Zha Police Station, falsely claiming that she had been robbed by two bandits at No. 542 Lane on Avenue Edward VII and lost two rings worth a total of sixty-one yuan. She described in detail the appearance of one of the bandits. The woman also went to the Tianyun Building and told the receptionist Huang Apin what had happened, asking him to pay attention. Chen returned to the entertainment venue the day before yesterday and was arrested by the police and taken to the police station. After an investigation by Detective Zhang Yi, he was taken to the First Special District Local Court yesterday morning for trial by Judge Qian. Wang Yaotang, the lawyer for the police station, explained the incident, stating that similar cases had occurred several times recently in the Old Zha area, and Zhong Yuan was not the only victim. He charged the defendant with Article 340 of the Criminal Code, but said that further investigation was needed and requested an adjournment. Detective Zhang then reported the circumstances of the arrest, stating that a ruby was found on his person, which Zhong Yuan recognized as the stolen item. In addition, the ring and watch chain worn by the defendant were all made of copper, and he had twenty-four yuan in banknotes, which he used to make the surface of each stack of banknotes, as he inserted waste paper in the middle of each stack. Zhong Yuan (named A Gui) also gave a detailed account of what had happened. However, the defendant, Chen Fuqing, pretended to be deaf and dumb, deliberately giving irrelevant answers to the questions asked by the court, revealing the cunning of an old fox. Judge Qian then ordered him to be detained for another hearing at a later date.

Page 13

Continued Trial of the Jiande Bank Case; Plaintiff's Lawyer Requests Another Auditor to Review the Points Raised by the Plaintiff to Clarify the Facts

Following the collapse of Jiande Bank, all directors and General Manager Chai Chuangui et al. were sued by creditors for fraud and embezzlement. The First Special District Local Court has repeatedly held hearings and summoned the defendants for questioning, as reported in this newspaper on several occasions. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu continued the trial. Six of the defendants appeared in court: Li Jingwei, Tu Kaizheng, Chai Yousheng, Yan Ziyu, Xie Keming, and Ma Suizhi. The remaining defendants, Chai Chuangui, Chen Xifu, Ou Jiancheng, and Zheng Huaigu, did not appear. The court first questioned Chai Yousheng, who testified that there were eleven directors in the bank, and no executive directors were appointed. Chai Chuangui was responsible for the bank's affairs. Wei Haijiang's investment was voluntary, and he said that the bank's collapse was caused by Wei's lawsuit. The court, noting that he was distorting the facts, then asked him about the reasons for the collapse, but his answers were even more ambiguous. Judge Liu then instructed the defendants, saying, "Wei Haijiang's lawsuit is slightly different from ordinary cases. In addition to subscribing for shares, he also used real estate as collateral to support the bank, but now there is nothing he can do, causing him to suffer a major loss. It is not only unreasonable, but also legally speaking, you are all directors and should be responsible." The plaintiff's representative lawyer, Gao Junxiang, then stated, "The defendant Yan Ziyu claims that he never attended board meetings and denies being a director. In fact, attendance is irrelevant. If Yan had resigned as a director, there should be written proof. It has been found that the board of directors resolved that the directors should advance funds, and Yan also raised 4,500 yuan. If he was not a director, why would he advance funds?" The court then questioned the representative of accountant Pan Xiren about the bank's liquidation process. The representative stated that they only audited the accounts as of December 7th and found that the paid-up share capital was 500,000 yuan, and the losses were only slightly more than 130,000 yuan. However, the accounts before December 7th were never audited, so everything in detail cannot be clearly understood. The plaintiff's lawyer, Chen Tingrui, then stated that the case had been heard many times, but the accounts had not been clarified, leading to an indefinite conclusion. Therefore, he requested that the court appoint another accountant to audit the accounts, saying that the accountant who appeared in court today did not provide detailed reports and his words were ambiguous. As far as the plaintiff knows, the bank's share capital was only 200,000 yuan. In order to be fair and accurate, another accountant should be appointed to review the points raised by the plaintiff, which would be easier to understand and would not delay the matter any further. Lawyer Gao also raised several points of doubt regarding the account books, such as the alterations in the capital book and the discrepancy in the account names, and requested that they be investigated together. Judge Liu then ordered an adjournment for another hearing.

New Rules of the British Gas Company - Employees Will Fight for Their Rights

The British Gas Company, under the pretext of sluggish business, has frequently reduced the number of workers in various departments in large numbers. Yesterday, it issued new rules, denied the Shanghai Municipal Gas Industry Workers' Union organized by the workers, and canceled the coffin fee of fifty yuan paid by the company in case of the death of a worker. These harsh and oppressive clauses have aroused the anger of all five hundred employees, who have requested the union to fight for their rights, appeal to party and government organs for assistance, and expedite the handling of the matter. A general membership meeting will be convened soon to unite and discuss countermeasures, and if necessary, take the most effective measures. The new rules issued by the company are recorded below: Rules and regulations of the Shanghai British Gas Company. The company does not recognize any labor unions. Chapter 1: Rules for employee illness and leave. A. Chinese employees who are absent without the permission of their supervisor will not be paid. B. Chinese employees who are frequently absent without the permission of their supervisor will be suspended. C. If an employee needs to be absent, they must first ask their supervisor for leave. D. If an employee requests leave due to illness, they must have a doctor's certificate, otherwise, it will be considered absence without permission. E. If a Chinese employee is sick, and it is determined that the illness was not contracted before joining the company, nor was it caused by their own improper behavior, they may be sent to Renji Hospital for treatment. However, this matter is at the discretion of the Chief Engineer. F. Employees who are ill will be paid their full salary for one month, two-thirds of their salary for the second month, and one-third of their salary for the third and fourth months. However, this salary must be certified by a doctor and approved by the Chief Engineer. G. Employees who are frequently sick may be suspended at the discretion of the Chief Engineer. Chapter 2: Rules for holidays and overtime work. A. Chinese employees who work on the following holidays will be paid double wages, and those who do not work will be paid single wages: three days off for the Gregorian New Year, two days off for the Lunar New Year, one day off for the Dragon Boat Festival, one day off for the Mid-Autumn Festival, and half a day off for the Double Ten National Day on October 10th. B. Fitters and road pipe workers who work on Saturdays past 5 pm and on Sundays will receive overtime pay. Chapter 3: Rules for bonuses and suspension. A. Chinese employees will receive a bonus of half a month's salary at the end of the Lunar New Year. B. Any employee who is suspended for theft or other reasons will only be paid up to the day of suspension, and will be denied bonuses and other fees. C. Any Chinese employee who is suspended due to lack of work within the company or unsatisfactory work performance will be paid compensation based on their years of service in the company, with one week's salary for each full year. If the service is less than one year, it will be calculated as one year. This matter is at the discretion of the Chief Engineer. Chapter 4: Rules for compensation. A. Any Chinese employee who is certified by a doctor as unable to work again, and whose illness did not exist before joining the company, nor was it caused by improper behavior, will be paid compensation based on their salary at the time of retirement, with half a month's salary for each full year. However, service of less than one year is not included. B. In the event of an employee's death, compensation will be paid to the closest family member based on their salary at the time of death, with half a month's salary for each year. C. Any Chinese employee who has worked continuously in the company for more than ten years and retires will be handled in accordance with Articles A and B to receive compensation. However, for those with less than ten years of service, only one week's salary will be given for each year. The company will not re-employ retired or suspended employees. D. The coffin fee of fifty yuan paid by the company in the event of an employee's death is now canceled. E. Employees who die or are disabled due to work will be given appropriate compensation, depending on their position and years of service. Five. In the event of any questions regarding the above articles, the decision of the Chief Engineer shall prevail.

The Commodity Inspection Bureau Notifies Tea Merchants - Thick Paper Should Be Used to Line Tea-Packed Lead Casings to Prevent Lead from Mixing into Tea Due to Friction - The US Government Has Recently Issued an Order to Ban This

When tea is packed for export, thick paper must be used between the tea and the lead casing (commonly known as tin cans) to prevent lead from mixing into the tea due to friction, which would affect hygiene. The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau recently discovered that many tea boxes did not have lining paper in the lead casings, and lead was often mixed in, which is a major concern for hygiene. The US government has recently issued an order to ban this. According to the chemical analysis of the US Department of Agriculture, if the lead content in each pound of tea exceeds 0.019 grams cold, it will not be allowed to be imported (one gram cold is equal to 0.0648 grams gramme, and the above limit is equal to 2.7 pounds per million). This will have a significant impact on our foreign trade. A letter has been sent to the Tea Industry Association to inform all tea merchants that thick paper must be used between the tea and the lead casing when packing tea in the future to ensure hygiene.

The Stamp Tax Bureau Replies to the Chamber of Commerce - Notification Letters Are Exempt from Stamp Tax

The Jiangsu Stamp Tax Bureau for Tobacco and Alcohol replied to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating: "Regarding your Chamber's letter No. 351, stating that the Sheng Sheng Ranch charges customers for accounts receivable and uses a triplicate receipt book. Since the official receipt copy has been stamped with the stamp tax, the notification and stub copies are for advance notice and verification purposes only and are absolutely not used for collecting money, therefore, they should not be stamped. A sample receipt book was enclosed for your inspection, etc. After reviewing the submitted receipt book, the receipt copy has been stamped as required. The notification copy, if it is absolutely not used for collecting money, can be exempted from stamp tax. The letter is approved. In addition to keeping the original sample for reference, this is a corresponding reply. Please investigate and inform accordingly."

Jin Xingjian Invents Vacuum Fountain Pen

Chinese people with sufficient financial resources usually purchase expensive products from the United States and other countries for fountain pens. The general public usually buys cheap and inferior goods from a certain country, resulting in a huge outflow of profits. Jin Xingjian, a Chinese man, foresaw this and traveled overseas many years ago to specialize in researching this manufacturing technology. In 1931, he returned to China and founded the Jin Xing Fountain Pen Factory in Shanghai to manufacture various domestic Jin Xing brand fountain pens, which are sold throughout the country. The quality and low price have long been recognized by the general public. However, Mr. Jin still felt that this was not enough and continued to delve into the technology. Now he has succeeded in inventing a vacuum fountain pen. The pen barrel is completely vacuumed, the color is transparent, the writing is smooth, and it never leaks. It holds four times more ink than ordinary products, and the quality is no less than that of Parker, but the price is several times lower. The raw materials are also purely domestic. A few months ago, he submitted it to the Industrial Technology Promotion Committee of the Ministry of Industry for examination and requested a patent. The committee has now completed the examination and recognized that it is a valuable invention of the Chinese people and officially announced that it will be granted a patent for five years. After receiving the patent, Mr. Jin ordered the factory to step up production of the first batch of new products (the factory is currently located at No. 390 Kang Nao Road). It is expected that they will be available to the public in one or two months.

Special Publication

Jin Cheng Bank's Business Report for 1934 (13)

Within this year, the exchange rate market fluctuated extremely drastically. In the past, due to trade relations, the prices of silver dollars in various places were higher than Shanghai dollars. The Shanghai Tianjin exchange rate in 1930 was 1006.9 yuan, the Qingdao exchange rate was 1004.4 yuan, and the Hankou exchange rate was 1007.6 yuan. After 1931, the rural areas declined, the export of agricultural products decreased, and the domestic trade deficit had to be paid with silver. The Shanghai dollar price rose. Therefore, the annual average of Shanghai's domestic exchange rate in 1933 dropped to 1001.4 yuan for Tianjin, 1001.3 yuan for Hankou, and 1000 yuan for Qingdao. From January to September of this year, this trend did not change, and more silver flowed into Shanghai, causing the exchange rate to fall sharply. The average Tianjin exchange rate fell to 998 yuan in July, the Qingdao exchange rate also fell to 999 yuan, and the Hankou exchange rate was still able to maintain around 1000 yuan. However, after October, the exchange rates of coastal ports soared. For example, the Tianjin exchange rate rose to 1017 yuan on November 26th, and Qingdao and Yantai also rose to 1014 yuan on November 28th, while the Hankou exchange rate remained around 1002 yuan. The exchange rates of inland areas such as Bengbu and Changsha also changed little. Due to the convenience of transportation along the coast, there was a lot of smuggling after the silver tax was levied, resulting in a shortage of silver and an increase in demand for remittances to and from Shanghai, so the exchange rate continued to rise.

This year's foreign exchange was affected by the US silver policy and the exchange rate dumping of various countries, and the prices all rose sharply. After the export tax on silver was levied, the prices were slightly restricted. The beginning of the year was still mediocre, but the prices rose sharply in February, especially for the US dollar and the Japanese yen. After June, the price of silver gradually increased, and the exchange rates of various currencies also increased uniformly, reaching a peak on October 13th. One hundred national currency could be exchanged for 7.5 pounds of British gold, 13 Japanese yen, and 37 US dollars. Compared with the exchange rate in September 1931, the US dollar exchange rate increased by 43%, the British exchange rate increased by 67%, and the Japanese exchange rate increased by 210%. After the export tax on silver was levied, China's silver price lost contact with the world silver price and was lower than the world silver price, so the exchange rates of various currencies all contracted uniformly. The US dollar exchange rate fell to 32 yuan, the British exchange rate fell to one shilling and three pence, and the Japanese exchange rate fell to 110 yen. However, the trend still felt weak after November.

As for the financial industry itself, there has also been progress in the current situation, and there are many new directions for business operations. However, the changes in the market are also quite drastic. In the past year, 16 new silver firms were established, 3 were restored, and 49 new branches were established. In Shanghai, 12 firms closed down. Bank closures were also frequently reported in Ningbo, Nanjing, Tianjin, Suzhou, Anqing, Yangzhou, and other places. In this period of economic decline, a slight carelessness could lead to failure. The government's financial measures include cracking down on speculation in foreign exchange, implementing the Savings Bank Law, changing the margin to be calculated based on customs gold units, levying export taxes on silver, and establishing a foreign exchange stabilization committee. These are all important plans. However, the world economy and the domestic economy are closely related. In today's position of being dominated by international economic forces, how should we observe the global economic situation externally and examine our own situation internally, and deal with it properly without suffering losses? This is what we hope for. (2) Prices In China, prices in all regions fell sharply this year. Compared with the average wholesale price this year and the average price last year, Shanghai fell by 7%, North China fell by 9%, and Nanjing fell by 12%. Classified by industry, Shanghai's prices are as follows:

Spring and Autumn

Anecdotes

— (Wang Xiaolin)

Westerners use knives and forks to eat, while Chinese people use round chopsticks. Knives and forks symbolize aggression, while chopsticks can symbolize smoothness. The difference in the personalities of Chinese and foreigners can be seen in this small "eating" posture.

Using words like flowers and birds to describe women is said to be male chauvinism. But generally, emerging female writers have used and continue to use such words to describe women. What should this be considered? Is it female chauvinism? !

The world rains, the ground is wet; he loves her, she falls. The mystery in this, as long as you turn your mind, you can understand.

At present, the life of prostitutes has plummeted, and the comedy of marrying into a good family as a concubine has "not been heard for a long time." On the other hand, cases of female students' adultery are emerging one after another, and the tricks of new women degrading themselves into disguised concubines are unfolding before our eyes. Ha! A humorous contrast.

Visiting the Tomb of an Unknown Hero

— Yixin

From a winter that never snowed, we slipped away, and soon, the world was arranged into a lovely picture of lush green again.

The sun shines so warmly, and the wind blows so refreshingly; indeed, spring is too mysterious, like a beautiful maiden, constantly exuding an enticing magic.

We could no longer bear it, so we skipped class, hastily brushed the chalk dust off our collars and sleeves, pulled Lao Hu, and walked out of the school gate with a brisk pace.

Walking, walking, passing through green fields, listening to the gurgling of water, we finally stopped at a barren mound arranged like a trench; from a wooden board washed by rainwater, with only a few ink marks remaining, we discovered that this was the burial place of our loyal and brave soldiers.

"Four years," I thought to myself, "Alas, the hot blood shed by the brave warriors for the country has become a glass of red wine in people's minds."

We wandered around this forgotten, ownerless barren mound, sent the sunset home, and the smoke from the chimneys everywhere wove a wartime smokescreen, reminding us of this day four years ago. It was our loyal and brave soldiers who, taking advantage of this natural cover, charged and killed the enemy. We couldn't help but feel a little desolate.

Returning in the twilight, the spring-like, maiden-like temptation in my mind had been replaced by a scene of war memories.

Young Master Ming

— Zhu Ying

Young Master Ming is my old neighbor and was my classmate when I was in elementary school.

His father was very rich, and he was an only son, so in his childhood, his life was not only something all the children in our neighborhood envied, but also something none of the classmates didn't envy. Indeed, he was always wearing beautiful clothes, eating delicious candies, and playing with expensive toys.

He married at the age of eighteen. And his wife was so beautiful.

After he got married, he stopped studying and doing business, spending his days listening to operas and playing cards. When he got tired of that, he went out to play with women.

When he was twenty, his father died. Less than a year later, his mother also died. So he was even more comfortable, spending money as he pleased, with no one to interfere with him.

In one year, he squandered all his Shanghai stocks on gambling and whoring. From the second year, he began to sell the fields and properties in his hometown. In the third year, he lived by borrowing from relatives and friends. In the fourth year, he could no longer maintain himself and sold off his furniture and clothes. His wife, in that year, divorced him.

From then on, Young Master Ming was left all alone. He couldn't borrow any more money. His former close friends no longer greeted him. In the summer, he would go shirtless, and in the winter, he would wear a tattered cotton-padded jacket he had begged for. Sometimes he would even sit on the steps, catching lice in the sun.

I didn't see him all of last year, and I thought he was no longer among the living. But unexpectedly, this time, on the Old Zha Gate Bridge, I saw him pulling a rickshaw for me.

Looking at his demeanor, I fear he has also picked up the habit of using narcotics.

Metropolis Monster Appears

— Jiang Mi

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Eleven: A Sad Night's Conversation Reveals Life as a Dream; Random Footprints, Wind and Rain are Too Oppressive

Huanhua said, "Don't even mention it! That's why I think it's terrifying when women in society can't stand on their own two feet. This young lady's father came to Xi'an before the Qing Dynasty, and it's said he was an old bureaucrat. This young lady was the youngest, so of course she was loved very much, and they let her study. But he hasn't been an official for many years, and in Xi'an, they experienced the great hardship of an eight-month siege, followed by two years of severe drought, so the family became very poor. They originally planned to return to their old home in Anhui, but they hadn't heard any news in many years, so they didn't know what had become of it. Besides, they still had a dilapidated house to live in here, so they could save on rent. The cost of living here is different; living like Easterners is even more expensive than in the East, because goods come from outside Tongguan. Living like the local people, they eat some Guokui (hard flatbread) every day, drink a little rice soup, and can even save on oil and salt; a family can get by on a few dollars a month. That's why they hesitated to leave. Later, they couldn't even leave if they wanted to, because they couldn't raise the travel expenses. This girl, though, continued to study. But modern fashion harmed her. In the past two years, transportation has become more convenient, and people from the East have been coming here one after another. Women in fashionable clothes can often be seen on the streets. Which young girl doesn't like to look good, so they follow the women from the East and learn to dress like them. But that's not easy. A pair of leather shoes, shipped from Shanghai to Zhengzhou, from Zhengzhou to Tongguan, and from Tongguan to Xi'an, would probably cost seven or eight dollars a pair. Ordinary families can live for a month on seven or eight dollars; who would be willing to buy such expensive things for the young girls to wear? They fell in love with modern fashion and always wanted to learn it. If they couldn't get money from home, they would go outside to find it, and Little Western Paradise was the first place they looked for money." Jia Duocai said, "So that's how it is. But this isn't a matter of applying and taking an exam. How do they get in?" Huanhua said, "This is the bad part of making bad friends. For example, they're all poor girls, and none of them can afford silk skirts or leather shoes. But one or two of them suddenly become fashionable, with watches, silk clothes, and silk stockings." (167)

Royal Incense Vaguely Recorded

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

There was only one thing that could be considered both a game and practical. That was when the silkworms were about to spin silk, picking one or two of them and putting them on a thin piece of paper pasted over the mouth of a teacup, letting them spin the silk they were going to use to make cocoons onto the paper. Then, the paper filled with silk would be cut into round or oval shapes, with velvet as a pad, and used as a powder puff or to apply fragrant oil, which was indeed the softest and smoothest. I still think of it every time I put on powder.

Although the Empress Dowager herself only treated silkworms as a toy, the girls she hired to take care of the silkworms were still very serious about their work due to the influence of so many traditional superstitious ideas. They seemed like a group of devout nuns, and the silkworms were their sacred objects.

Chapter Twenty-Five: Artisans of Various Trades

In the palace, it could be said to be a self-contained society. There were not only girls in charge of raising silkworms, but also artisans of various other trades! The skills of these artisans were naturally excellent, far superior to ordinary workers outside. The Empress Dowager also firmly believed that they were rare masters and often took pride in them. Moreover, she herself was very interested in these delicate crafts and would often go to see them. Coincidentally, I was also someone who loved to watch people do fine work—although I couldn't do any of it myself—so the Empress Dowager would always take me with her, and after going there, she would linger as if she were watching some novel opera and be reluctant to leave. (278)

Two-Legged Shen Bao

— Xian Weisheng

There are dozens of newspapers published in the city. Regardless of the content, what is particularly commendable is that no matter what the name of the newspaper is, people lump them all together and call them Shen Bao, as if Shen Bao were a generic term for all newspapers. If it weren't for its senior status, how could it have penetrated people's minds so deeply? I often hear people say, "Have you read the Shen Bao today?" "Is there any news in today's Shen Bao?" "Thank you, give me a few copies of Shen Bao to wrap things with," and so on.

The "two-legged Shen Bao" I'm talking about is a special term in my hometown. It's not easy to qualify for this title. Most of them are idle brothers who have nothing to do and wander around all day long. Therefore, what they hear and see is more than others. If they don't get any news, that's it, but if they happen to get some news, they like to tell everyone, spreading even the smallest details, or even a dog fight on West Street or a overturned wonton stall on East Street, are part of their information. In practical terms, those people can be said to have no value at all, but they deserve the title of "well-informed." Furthermore, why don't people say "two-legged XX Bao" and insist on saying "two-legged Shen Bao"? If Shen Bao's news isn't particularly quick and superior to others, how could it be so?

Bowl Clay Powder

— (Ning Ziqiang)

Jingdezhen porcelain is the most famous. Although it cannot surpass Europe and the United States, it is considered the best in the country!

For any object, half of its successful creation depends on skill, and half on raw materials. If there is skill but no material, then there is no way to apply the skill. If there is material but no skill, then there is no way to use the material. They complement each other and are mutually indispensable. This is true for humans, and why shouldn't it be true for objects!

For example, the raw material for Jingdezhen porcelain comes from Qimen, Anhui, which is commonly called "bowl clay powder." Only with this fine raw material can exquisite pottery be created. When drinking water, remember the source; how can we forget the reason for its existence?

Miscellaneous Words

Calligraphy and Painting and Mounting (Part 1)

— Yin Qiu

Chinese calligraphy and painting are where the spirit of talented scholars resides, relying on paper and silk to be passed down through the ages. However, paper and silk are inherently delicate and must be mounted to facilitate display and preservation. Why? When calligraphers and painters are inspired, they pick up a brush and ink and wield them freely. Once a painting is completed, it is entrusted to a mounter, and its spirit and ink subtleties leap to life, inevitably appearing more outstanding than when it was unmounted. Therefore, whether it is a small piece of paper or a large piece of silk, mounting must be carefully considered, just like Western paintings must be fitted with an easel.

Mounters from Jiangsu and Zhejiang have long enjoyed a reputation for excellence. In the past, the Tang and Qiang families were highly respected. Although there are still skilled mounters today, few of them can follow ancient methods. Collectors and connoisseurs treat them with great respect! Because the same calligraphy and painting, when beautifully mounted, is icing on the cake; conversely, it is like putting dung on the Buddha's head. Or if there are masterpieces and treasures from previous generations that have been passed down for a long time and have become damaged and fallen apart, requiring re-mounting, then ordinary mounters cannot do the job. In the past, people compared re-mounting calligraphy and painting to seeking medical treatment for an illness; it is indeed not a false analogy!

When re-mounting calligraphy and painting, one must first examine the color and condition of the paper and silk. If the color is dull and the condition is poor, it must be rinsed and soaked. If the paper and silk are intact, they must be carefully peeled off and then slowly washed to remove dust and dirt. If they are moldy or diseased, they must be washed together with the backing paper, with careful attention. Some people use a loquat pit hammer to soak and boil the dirty areas, but after washing, they must be rinsed with deacidified water, otherwise stains are unavoidable.

Peeling off the mounting is not easy; peeling silk is still possible, but peeling paper is really difficult. If the paper is thin and the paste is heavy, or if white orpiment is used as paste, one must be cautious. If the calligraphy or painting is damaged, it must be repaired with the original silk. When repairing, the thickness of the paper and the fineness of the silk must be matched to be as identical as possible; even the paper grain and silk threads cannot be overlooked. The items to be peeled and mounted must have a "flying lining," which means leaving a two- or three-fen gap around the edges when lining, now called "leaving the seat," so that the original painting is not damaged when cutting and mounting with paste. When old calligraphy and painting have defects, old ink can be used to add a few strokes, which is called "completing," but it must be done by someone with high artistic skill to make it seamless.

There are many types of mounting. The most common ones nowadays are silk mounting, paper mounting, and sequential mounting. The style includes full brocade, half brocade, and edged brocade. The same applies to silk brocade, which can be inlaid, embedded, or hollowed out. The value depends on the cost of labor and materials. In the past, scrolls were mostly mounted with paper shells filled with sand to give them weight and make them hang down, but they were easily broken, so they are rarely used now, and wooden rods are used instead. The best ones are made of heavy and substantial wood, sandalwood being the best, followed by old fir. Fir is used for its dryness, and sandalwood can repel insects.

Scrolls with flat ends are called flat scrolls. Those mounted with scroll ends have mahogany scroll ends and horn scroll ends. Ivory and sandalwood are also often used. Occasionally, magnetic scroll ends are used, but they are brittle and easily broken. White bamboo carved scroll ends are more elegant and desirable. Jade scroll ends are mostly used for handscrolls, and the mounting is also flat, with ivory clasps attached to the beginning of the scroll, which is an old style.

The format of the mounting must be beautiful. The dimensions of the upper and lower inlays, and the width of the left and right borders, must be properly arranged, whether they are narrow and long or wide and broad, to match the calligraphy and painting itself, or to suit the location where they are hung. This cannot be generalized. However, it is forbidden to use a "poetry hall." Those who are knowledgeable about mounting never use a "poetry hall," even for small pieces. Using it makes it vulgar, and vulgarity is incurable. Nowadays, many people like "poetry halls," which is incomprehensible!

Educational News

Jiangsu Education Fund Office Sends Letter to the Finance Department Requesting That Provincial Education Funds Still Be Stored Separately in the Treasury

Niu Yongjian, Director of the Jiangsu Education Fund Management Office, recently sent a letter to Zhao, the Director of the Finance Department, requesting that provincial education funds still be stored separately in the Provincial Education Treasury. An excerpt from the original letter is as follows: "Upon investigation, the provincial education funds collected from the land tax of various counties have been directly transferred by the treasury to the commission for special fund storage for a long time, without any obstruction. Since the establishment of county treasuries last year, the accounting directors of Wu County, Changshu, Songjiang, Nanhui, Baoshan, and other counties have, under the pretext of unifying the county treasury system, refused to allow direct transfer by the treasury. They have instead submitted the provincial education funds collected from the land tax to the county treasury for storage, and then re-allocated them separately, just like local funds to be disbursed. Baoshan County even delayed the transfer of special funds collected in July of last year until recently. The other central counties also do not have a fixed schedule for allocation after the funds are deposited. According to the current new accounting system regulations in our province, the method for affiliated institutions and various collection offices to submit funds clearly stipulates that provincial funds should be fully submitted to the provincial treasury and stored in a separate account under the name of special funds. The county treasury is only responsible for the receipt and disbursement of county funds and does not extend to provincial taxes. Furthermore, Article 7 of the Interim Regulations for County Treasuries stipulates that county taxes, county education taxes, county construction taxes, county grain reserve taxes, and temporary taxes are all county taxes. If special accounts need to be added, the county magistrate should submit a request to the Finance Department for approval. Their accounting subjects do not allow for the existence of provincial education funds. This shows that their management scope is limited to the storage and disbursement of county funds. Why must the accounting directors of these counties overstep their authority and prevent direct allocation by the treasury, instead insisting on storing the funds in the county treasury? In the future, the reporting and transfer of provincial education funds will require the county government to sign checks and extract them from the county tax items, causing unnecessary trouble. Moreover, the boundaries are blurred. If the county government experiences financial difficulties, it will inevitably挪移 accumulate arrears. It seems that the establishment of the new accounting system is specifically to protect other provincial and county funds, while the provincial education funds, which have been divided independently for several years and have been managed effectively, are now losing their protection due to the establishment of the new system. This seems to be a misunderstanding. Therefore, I hereby request Director Zhao to investigate and instruct all counties and accounting directors to follow the various regulations and systems and continue to handle the allocation and transfer of provincial education funds according to the old methods, without any changes. If there are still any doubts, please refer to Article 5 of the Provincial Special Fund Custody and Disbursement Regulations, which states, 'The collected special funds should be fully submitted to the treasury by the second morning,' and submit the collected provincial education funds to the commission for separate storage by the second morning to maintain the needs of the provincial education funds. I also hope to receive a reply for the sake of convenience."

Chunhui Middle School Will Be Closed Down

Chunhui Middle School in Shangyu, Zhejiang Province, was founded by the late gentry Chen Chunlan, who invested 200,000 gold to create a school for the youth of the county. It has been established for thirteen years, nurturing talent. Recently, it was heard that a portion of the school board members have proposed to donate the school to the provincial government and transfer the funds to Datong Hospital. The Zhejiang Education Department sent Inspector Zhu to the school to investigate the matter. The teachers and students were in an uproar and organized a school protection association to seek help from all parties. It is learned that Yao Zantang, Yin Youlan, Chen Bangyan, Zhu Ziming, and other natives of the county living in Shanghai believe that the proposal of some Chunhui school board members goes against the original intention of the late Mr. Chen in founding the school. They have sent an urgent letter to the school board, requesting that it continue to operate, in order to benefit future generations.

Declaration of School Protection by Alumni: All Chunhui alumni, due to the recent proposal by the school board to挪移 funds and close the school, have organized a school protection association and issued a declaration stating: "Our school, Chunhui, was founded by Mr. Chen Chunlan and cannot be destroyed by others. The designated fund of 145,000 yuan cannot be embezzled by others. The school buildings belong to Chunhui, the facilities belong to Chunhui, and every plant and tree in the school belongs to Chunhui. Chunhui is the Chunhui of our alumni. All those who teach at Chunhui and study at Chunhui love and protect Chunhui. Since we love and protect it, we must preserve it. Now that some school board members are plotting to挪移 school funds and eliminate Chunhui, we, the alumni, vow to come out and oppose it with all our strength, and we will not stop until we achieve our goal. We hope that the education community and local people will be aware of this." Chunhui Middle School School Protection Association.

Shaoxing Student Circles Express: Since hearing the news of the closure of Chunhui, students from Shaoxing Private Jishan Middle School, Chengtian Middle School, Yuecai Middle School, and Junde Girls' Middle School have expressed dissatisfaction due to the matter concerning the future of students' education, and public opinion has been divided. Yesterday, the student self-government associations of the various schools held a joint meeting to discuss the course of action, telegraphed the Zhejiang Provincial Education Department, and telegraphed the Chunhui school board members.

It is also heard that the Shanghai, Hangzhou, and Ningbo areas are also responding. Chunhui alumni in Shaoxing organized the Chunhui Shaoxing Alumni School Protection Association on the 10th of this month. Yuan Shunda and others initiated the effort, and they sent letters to alumni in other locations and telegraphed the Provincial Education Department. The telegram to the Education Department stated: "To Xu Junjian, Director of the Zhejiang Provincial Education Department, Chunhui Middle School in Shangyu has a fund of 145,000 yuan. Some people are proposing to transfer and use the funds, destroying the school. Please immediately order a stop to this. Education is fortunate. Shun Da, He Minxing, Yao Xuanqing, Lu Zixiang, Ding Gongliang, Chen Hongda and others knock."

Jiang Baili Publishes His Thoughts on the "Ten Declarations," Continued

Mr. Tao Xisheng, in his "Wandering Fire Research," pointed out two different groups, which made me extremely happy. This is a major discovery in history.

And I believe that this point is the fatal wound of the national decline for three thousand years. After the failure of Xiang Yu's "gentlemen's society" and the deaths of Han Xin, the humiliation and escape of Zhang Liang, and Xiao He, an endless covert struggle between activists and intellectuals (莽换之's alterations and the literary inquisitions of past dynasties) has ensued. Within the intellectual class, there has also been constant infighting (the party strife of past dynasties). The most important cells of a nation have always been in a state of internal strife. Therefore, this has fostered two incurable maladies within the intellectual class: 1. Irresponsibility (The ideal for a scholar is to be a prime minister, not an emperor). 2. Detachment from reality (The transformation from the six arts of rites, music, archery, chariot driving, writing, and arithmetic to the six classics of poetry, books, rites, music, Yi, and Spring and Autumn Annals was a major turning point). For example, if the enzyme for brewing wine is bad, just like an explosion, if the electrical tube is wet, all the good laws, good intentions, and excellent products in the world must pass through this corrupt and dark door before they can enter Chinese society. The general cause of the ineffectiveness of all medicines is not here.

History has also seen a few painful cries, such as Gu Tinglin's advocacy of practical learning in the early Qing Dynasty, which was a resistance to detachment from reality. However, this movement, due to the covert struggle between activists and intellectuals, resulted in the ultimate failure of the factualist Yan Yuan Li Gangzhu, and it transformed into textual research. The spirit of textual research was indeed scientific, but in reality, it was still just a few dead words. During the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom era, Hu Wenzhong's monopolization and Zeng Wenzheng's "Upholding the Classics First Chapter" were both resistances to irresponsibility, but they only achieved partial success. And Li Hongzhang, who rose from the covert struggle, was still defeated by the great tide of irresponsibility and detachment from reality, leading to the heartbreaking diplomatic situation of today. The character of activists is fundamentally the opposite of intellectuals. Their strength is their willingness to take responsibility, but the result is often arbitrary. They are able to stay grounded in reality, but the result is often opportunism. Arbitrariness prevents them from gathering the strengths of the masses, and opportunism prevents them from establishing long-term plans. Both of these things are unsuitable for the development of a modern nation. After the Qin and Han dynasties, political power, military force, and knowledge were divided.

(Previously concentrated in the aristocratic class) Therefore, there was constant competition in politics, and the Chinese people gradually declined. However, under this oppression, our Chinese people (struggling for three thousand years) have done an amazing thing, that is, the work on things (I also have a special chapter entitled "The Chinese People and Material"). In terms of the spirit of struggle, it is no less important than the invention of the steam engine. From papermaking, printing, ceramics, lacquer, architecture, sculpture, to water wheels and weaving machines, there are unique inventions in every aspect. However, they are despised by the intellectual class, so there is no written record, and the accumulation of academic knowledge cannot be promoted. In the last fifty years, society has undergone great changes due to the influence of the environment, but its political evolution can be divided into several steps. The first step is the cooperation of knowledge and military force ((1) Intellectuals join the military, (2) Soldiers go to school to acquire knowledge, (3) Cooperation between intellectuals and activists in society). The gatherings, separations, successes, and failures in between have been proven by facts and do not need to be detailed. The second step, of course, is the unity of political power, military force, and knowledge. But what should be paid close attention to is that intellectuals still cannot effectively control material, so there is a fundamental problem in the life of the nation. And the reason why they cannot control material is still due to the two major weaknesses of irresponsibility and detachment from reality.

From Gu Yan's spirit of practical learning and Zeng Hu's responsible attitude, perhaps new life can be added to the enzyme detonator. But the new society has another element called "organization." The meaning of the word "organization" is that one thing is not the responsibility of one person or one institution, but each smallest unit (individual) takes its own special responsibility, and a kind of mutual assistance success is achieved in the application. This is the key point of the new economy and the element of national defense. We can now say that there are strong soldiers but the country is not rich, but there has never been a rich country with weak soldiers.

To say a complaining word, if students in shops and apprentices of craftsmen can read for an hour at night (that is, people who live in practical things and can acquire knowledge), I am afraid that they can bear the responsibility of reviving the nation. And those who take carpools every day and attend six hours of gong ke in primary and secondary schools are still just an appendage. And the scientists in books can only allow the overseas Chinese who are bound by etiquette and controlled by the agricultural patriarchal spirit to remit money back every year to support them in their old age.

Finally, Mr. Jiang spoke the following words with extremely rich emotion. He said that the declarations of you gentlemen are like the echo of a bell in an ancient temple in the deep mountains, which represents the feeling of loneliness and desolation at this time. I hope that they will be the pioneers of dawn. The conversation did not end until late at night. (The end)

Letter from Jinan University, Published as Is

The letter from Jinan University reads: "Dear Editor, I read the educational news in your newspaper on March 22nd, which contained a message about an academic lecture by the Vocational Education Society, in which it was mentioned that Zhang Yiping is the director of the Literature Department of Jinan University (according to the manuscript submitted by the China Vocational Education Society). It was also stated that Mr. Zhang is the secretary and professor of Jinan University. After investigation, our school has separate Chinese Language and Literature Departments and Foreign Language and Literature Departments. Mr. Long Muxun is the director of the Chinese Language and Literature Department, and Mr. Chen Linrui is the director of the Foreign Language and Literature Department. I am sending this letter to request a correction. Thank you very much. Sincerely, the Chinese Language and Literature Department and the Foreign Language and Literature Department of National Jinan University, March 24th."

Financial Markets: Foreign Banks Surge, Gold Price Plummets to $15.60, Foreign Banks' Rise Unabated, Gold Market Dominated by Buyers, Future Unpredictable

The gold market experienced a sudden and surprising surge in overseas silver markets, causing panic. Yesterday's market decline was particularly severe. Banks and Sassoon maintained their positions, while other Chinese merchants were particularly cautious. The Indian silver market reported another sharp rise. Initially, overseas silver markets in England and America rose sharply in unison. It was also said that the United States would accept purchases at $0.0625 above the closing price. Forward silver prices also rose by more than one cent, and exchange rates all increased. London raw gold fell by 5.5 pence. Reports circulated that London was rife with rumors of a Sino-British loan of £10 million, further dampening sentiment. As a result, pre-market trading opened and immediately retreated within the $60 range. Major players emerged, short sellers gained momentum, and the situation appeared weak, with prices fluctuating downward. The Central Bank's benchmark price was announced, with both British and American currencies rising, and the Customs Gold Unit falling by 1.7%. The standard gold price was reduced to $897.80, leading to further declines after the opening. Banks took advantage of the cheap prices to buy aggressively, and the foreign exchange market tightened. Major players actively bought, gradually pushing prices up, briefly breaking through the $60 mark. Foreign banks took advantage of slight gains and then reported a decline. At this point, because banks had offsetting positions, the market briefly stagnated, appearing stable for quite some time. Later, Dayun Company and others continued to sell, banks became sluggish, the foreign exchange market hardened, and Sassoon also sold. The market was inherently bearish, and the decline became more pronounced, with many parties liquidating positions, briefly approaching the $50 mark. Later, banks took advantage of the cheap prices to maintain their positions, floating short positions took profits, and major players also came to buy, gradually improving the situation. Sassoon then came back to cover positions. Rumors of favorable news suddenly caused prices to rebound. The market appeared stable at noon. The market opened slightly lower in the afternoon, but unexpectedly, Sassoon aggressively bought significant amounts of US dollars and shillings, causing panic. Yesterday, US cotton opened with an increase of 2 to 7 points. Subsequently, with good news from Liverpool, Japanese merchants and economic merchants bought in, and prices continued to rise strongly. Midway through, due to selling by local and New Orleans traders and a sluggish stock market, the market appeared slightly weak. Then spot traders bought in near-month contracts, triggering short covering, which caused prices to rebound again. There was not much speculation, and traders were watching. In the afternoon, due to limit-price buying, short covering, and Japanese merchant purchases, there was another upward trend. Near the close, local players took profits, resulting in a slight weakening. The cotton exchange estimates that global US cotton consumption in February was 958,000 bales, a decrease of 158,000 bales compared to the same period last year. The close was firm. Spot prices rose by 20 points, and futures prices rose by 12 to 20 points. British cotton spot prices fell by one point, and futures prices rose by 3 to 4 points. Indian cotton fell due to selling by futures traders and profit-taking by bulls. Plain cotton fell by 3 rupees, and Oomra fell by 0.75 rupees. White Rawxi fell by 2 rupees.
