Dried Goods: Quanzhou Dried Longan New Seedlings Show Signs of Shortage

Recently, not many Quanzhou dried longans have arrived. Upon investigation, only 400-odd boxes were imported on the Fudong Wheel the day before yesterday. Due to outside groups purchasing from the local source, the Quanzhou price has increased by 2-3 yuan. According to letters from freight customers, prices must be increased, and it is also rumored that the current longan seedlings are only 10-20% of last year's crop, so sentiments are quite high. However, as the sales here have not been strong, dealers are not greedy and their appetite is not great, the trend shows a reverse soft trend, resulting in no deals.

Oil Market: Asphalt Prices Fluctuate

The spring season is extremely important for the asphalt market because candle makers begin to prepare for summer production, and they must use the highest quality goods. Even soap factories, which use low-quality goods, also purchase at this time, so the spring sales are stronger than the winter season. In recent years, soap factories have mostly switched to using imported goods such as tallow and coconut oil for making soap. The domestic asphalt, the raw material for making soap, has been abandoned. The reason is that the price of asphalt is high, and soap factories naturally choose cheaper materials. Therefore, the only people who rely on asphalt are candle makers. Unexpectedly, since last winter, the price of tallow and coconut oil has also risen to over 20 yuan per dan, about the same as asphalt. Therefore, since last winter, soap factories have also been buying asphalt. As a result, the price of asphalt this spring is about 6-7 yuan higher per dan compared to last spring. However, the reason for the increase is not entirely due to strong soap demand. The large crop failures in various asphalt-producing regions last year also had a significant impact. With both the crop failure and strong demand, price increases should be expected. However, due to widespread droughts in Zhejiang province, the demand for candle-making has been greatly reduced. The drought in Zhejiang has had a greater impact than the crop failure. Therefore, although the market has risen, the supply still exceeds the demand. Last week, Machang oil in Hankou suddenly rose by one or two, while Zhejiang oil was still sold at the original price. If Zhejiang oil had not been selling to Jiangsu province, the stockpiles would have been extremely crowded. Recently, Hankou Machang oil has fallen back from 15 liang to 14 liang 4 qian. The brief price increase was temporary. Local dealers have no intention of following the Jing Gong agreement of 24 yuan per dan, but rather are selling based on habit.

Piece Goods: Yellow Twill Sales Very Strong

Yesterday, the wool trade was still strong, and the sales of yellow twill were very strong. Tianxiang Desheng pattern yellow twill was sold at 5 jiao 4 fen per yard, Yongle brand at 5 jiao 6 fen, Rongkang 55 brand at 5 jiao 1 fen, Hua Ji at 3 jiao 8 fen, and domestic Dafeng yellow twill sold at 4 jiao 6 fen.

Hardware: Hard Lead Wire in Extreme Short Supply

Hard lead wire, numbers 12 to 20, is a popular product for thermos bottle factories and the Ningbo group. Therefore, whenever they arrive, these groups must rush to purchase them. Although the actual sales volume is not large, it is a type of goods that plays a role in the market. Recently, although there has been a constant stream of arriving goods, the demand has been so strong that there is still not enough in the market to meet the sales volume, resulting in a shortage of circulating goods and high prices. It is quoted at 7 yuan 7 jiao 5 fen to 8 yuan 5 jiao per dan. However, due to the shortage of goods, dealers have very high expectations, and some are even asking for about 9 yuan. It is said that there are more than 260 loads for sale. Upon investigation, the goods expected to arrive in the next one or two weeks have already been sold, and the quoted price is said to be in the range of 8 yuan 1-2 jiao.

Silk and Tea: Domestic Zhenmei Tea Sells Slowly at Low Prices

European merchants have been allowing Chinese tea merchants to lower prices to sell. Although telegrams have been sent, Morocco has not requested to buy much. Free Talk

"Remnants of Elegance"

— Bai Zhu

Lin Zhengda (Jingzhi) of the Song dynasty wrote a volume of "Remnants of Elegance". It was a Qing dynasty carved edition that I bought from an old bookstore last year. It doesn't seem to have been included in the Qiangcun Series. This is a very unique collection of lyrics, all of which are paraphrased from ancient poems, fu, and essays. In the preface, the author says: "The world often takes Tao Jingjie's 'Returning Home', Du Gongbu's 'Song of Drunkenness', Li Taibai's 'Bring the Wine', Su Changgong's 'Red Cliff Fu', Ouyang Gong's 'Record of the Old Drunkard', and a dozen or so similar works, and sets them to music... But in the heat of drinking, the singer and the listener often become tired. Therefore, predecessors paraphrased them, slightly adapting them to the musical rhythm, such as 'Returning Home' becoming 'Shaobian', 'Listening to Ying Shiqin' becoming 'Shuidiao Ge', 'Record of the Old Drunkard' becoming 'Rui He Xian', capturing the meaning of the words, simplifying the complex, making them easier to sing and recite. Not only can they be used for entertainment, but they can also be used to imagine the high ideals of the ancient sages. I love them very much, and I often imitate them, forgetting my own ugliness..." and so on.

This collection paraphrases many works by ancient poets and writers, such as Du Fu, Han Yu, Li Bai, Ouyang Xiu, and Fan Zhongyan, totaling more than thirty pieces. Let's take a look at one of them. This is a paraphrase of "Preface to the Poems Composed at the Orchid Pavilion," set to the tune of "He Xin Lang":

"The events of the Orchid Pavilion on that day. There were high mountains, lush forests, and tall bamboos, where all the wise men gathered. The turbulent currents reflected each other, leading to flowing cups of wine along the winding stream. They only spoke freely of their secluded feelings. Singing and drinking, it was truly a joy, tired of the sounds of pipes and strings. It was late spring, and they performed the purification ritual together. The gentle breeze was pleasant, and the weather was new. They spread their high aspirations, looking up at the universe, and observing the species below. Between looking up and looking down, they entrusted their feelings, releasing themselves from the constraints of their bodies. They did not know that old age was approaching. They lamented that the old travels had become relics, thinking about how many joys there were in life. Looking back from the future, it will be the same as the past."

The technique is indeed quite good, but besides seeing the author "skillfully" express the original work in another form, what else do we get? Wang Xizhi's emotions are definitely not his emotions. Wang Xizhi's personal social environment and the natural environment of the Orchid Pavilion purification ceremony are also completely unrelated to him. He simply moved the "paper" original to another "piece of paper." He neither resonates with the original author from the heart nor infuses the original work with new life. The purpose is only to "set it to music." This is like silk flowers in a vase, artificial fountains in a fountain pool, all fake.

However, the "originator" was not Lin Zhengda. In the past, Su Shi's "Shaobian" was a well-known example. Huang Tingjian paraphrased Ouyang Xiu's "Record of the Old Drunkard" as "Around Chuzhou are all mountains. They look verdant and beautiful. They are Langya Mountains..." That "Rui He Xian" is also very famous. In addition, Jiang Jie of the Southern Song dynasty also had a "He Xin Lang" in his "Zhushan Lyrics" that paraphrased Du Fu's poem, starting with: "A reclusive hermit alone. Hiding her beautiful figure in a deep place, watching the clouds and valleys. She herself said that she was from a good family in Guanzhong, and has fallen to living among the grass and trees..." It still did not escape the shackles of the predecessors. Liu Shangyou, a surviving citizen who came south, also had a "Qinyuan Chun" in his "Yangwu Zhai Lyrics" that paraphrased the "Former Red Cliff Fu," with the opening line: "In the autumn of Renxu, on the fifteenth day of the seventh month, Su Zi sailed a boat..." This trend became more and more widespread as time went on.

People have mixed opinions about this method of paraphrasing. As far as I know, Shen Xiong's "Liutang Lyrics" says: "Scholars in Tokyo paraphrased Su Shi's 'Dongxian Ge' as 'Yulou Chun' to record the events of the Moha Pool, as seen in Zhang Zhongsu's 'Ben Shi Ji'. Lu Zhi paraphrased Zi Tong's 'Fisherman's Song' as 'Zhegu Tian' to record the scenery in front of Xisai Mountain, as seen in 'Shangu Lyrics'. It is truly simple and elegant." But there were also many who opposed it. For example, He Chang's "Zhou Shui Xuan Lyrics" said: "Su Shi's paraphrase of 'Returning Home' and Huang Tingjian's paraphrase of 'Record of the Old Drunkard' both fell into evil tendencies. There are many things in the world that are ruined by famous people." Liu Tiren also said in his "Qi Song Tang Lyrics": "The paraphrase style is not feasible. Not only is 'Drunkard's Pavilion' like chewing wax, but even if Zizhan changes the words 'qin' and 'pipa' in his 'Listening to the Qin' poem, it is still a dream from beginning to end." This can explain the opinions of some people. In fact, this genre is the most difficult to use. If you cannot infuse the original work with new life, it is even easier to "fall into evil tendencies" than couplets and rhyming. I don't object to borrowing existing materials to re-express, just don't be "confined to the old ways," without any innovation, because if that's the case, we already have the original work.

Such "Remnants of Elegance" were just the idle entertainment of scholars and officials at that time.

Traveling to Minhang (1)

— Leng Mo

The biting cold that people thought might come, finally did not arrive. The breath of March makes people abandon the foolish question of whether it is already spring. The name of this solar term, Awakening of Insects, is very wonderful. It is not only appropriate for hibernating insects, but humans, as animals, probably cannot escape the scope of this awakening. Of course, people usually don't pay attention to the Awakening of Insects, but they do celebrate the Spring Purification Festival, and they have changed the Spring Purification Festival to March 3rd on the Gregorian calendar, which is even closer in time. This solar term is very worthy of promotion because it is a season when people can travel. This year, that day happened to be a Sunday, and the weather was so good. Without even noticing that it was a holiday, people would want to go out for a walk. So I went to Minhang that day.

Although I have traveled to many places, I am unusually unfamiliar with the neighborhood of Shanghai, where I have lived for ten years. Minhang is one place I have never been to. Perhaps this is not surprising. In Jiangwan, there are elderly people in their decades who have never even been to Shanghai. So, there must be even more Shanghai residents who have never been to the unremarkable Minhang. There was no particular reason for my choosing to go to Minhang, probably only because it is located on the Huangpu River, and I could see the scenery on both sides of the upper reaches of the Huangpu River by taking a boat. The fun of traveling is probably more on the journey than at the destination. Traveling on water is even better than traveling on land. When I stay in one place for too long, I often take a short ferry ride to get a little taste of travel. The ferries between Hong Kong's Sham Shui Po and Hankou's Xujiazha have both been places I have lingered. I have also traveled between Shanghai and Gaoqiao in this way. There are probably many passengers on that ferry who purely regard it as a sightseeing trip. I often fantasize that if there were a floating hotel that would sail away from the bustling city every night, sail a suitable distance, and then return to the city the next morning, many people would be willing to make this hotel their home. There are probably people in Shanghai who live in Minhang and commute by boat every day.

During that sweltering summer last year, when the Shanghai Ferry Company was operating the tour boats on the Huangpu River, there were also special boats going to Minhang. I didn't pay attention at the time whether they were operated by the same organization, but later I mistakenly remembered that they were together. Before going to Minhang this time, I first went to the Tongren Pier to ask about the sailing time. The person at the pier told me to go to Dongjiadu. At Dongjiadu, I only saw the Shangnan Ferry. When I asked again, they said to go to the Kaiqiao Pier. When I wanted to ask more, that person said impatiently, "You'll know when you get there. The boat is about to leave, hurry up." I didn't have time to call a taxi to take me there, but the Pinghu bus to Minhang was also about to leave in about fifteen minutes, so I decided to take that one. At the time, I still thought there was another ferry. It wasn't until later, when I arrived in Minhang, that I realized I had been mistaken before.

Stepping onto the boat, the vendors, who are always present on inland river boats, immediately made me feel like I was on a journey. The boat didn't leave on time, but I can't blame the boat company. The passengers probably just like to take things slow. Even if they were willing to arrive at the pier on time, they would still argue about the taxi fare, take care of their luggage, take out money from their innermost pockets to buy tickets, and politely decline the farewell of their senders. Then they would slowly stroll onto the boat. How could the boat not wait? There didn't seem to be many people in the same cabin as me who were just going for fun, and everyone's attitude was even more leisurely than mine, probably because they were more culturally Chinese. The most distinctive were a few passengers or boatmen in the back cabin. As soon as the boat left, they immediately dragged out a table and started playing mahjong. As their mahjong game began, the seats in our cabin gradually became more spacious because some people who had been lying down gave up their seats and sacrificed their legs to stand and watch the game.

Long Road

— Zigang

What I love most is traveling.

Perhaps it is precisely because of the scarcity of travel opportunities that I love it even more. People always yearn in their hearts for things they have not experienced or have experienced very little; "freshness" attracts people's hearts.

But what I love is not necessarily green hills and clear waters and exotic scenery; what makes me even happier is the means of transportation for long journeys: things like boats and cars.

When stepping onto the carriage or the gangway, I can feel my heart jumping, so even if it is not spring, a spring smile will appear on my face.

For the past month, I have had to jump on the tram three days a week in the evening for a round trip of nearly twenty li. The tram has similarities to the train, with its long carriages, the steps and handrails for getting on and off, the only difference being that the driver's bell replaces the long whistle of the steam engine.

But this - also has its own charm.

When the rumbling of the wheels vibrates in my ears, and my eyes gaze at the city streets about to be enveloped in darkness, a waking dream begins. It feels like I am huddled in a corner of a long-distance train carriage, and with the rolling of the wheels, I am speeding through desolate mountains and fields, unable to see a single light, enveloped in darkness, touching only darkness. This brings a series of conjectures.

Imagining that unknown land and unfamiliar people. If it's not all for fun, a new hope grows even more in my heart: to cast off the old and start a new journey.

In the tram, I indulge even more in guessing.

This long-distance tram is particularly cheap. From Xuanwumen to Chongwenmen, there are many people, needless to say, but if you don't get on at a busy stop along the way, it's still not so crowded that there's no place to sit.

Because I catch the tram according to the time, I also happen to meet some frequent riders: office workers and students who get off work and school according to the time. Everyone nods familiarly, but doesn't want to exchange words.

Each time there are so many unfamiliar faces: soldiers and policemen in uniform, women carrying bags and bundles, old men leisurely twirling walnuts in the tram, delivery apprentices, and even third-rate actors going to catch a late-night opera...

Listen with your ears:

Today, they received a few dollars in salary, and at what time a robbery occurred in a certain city gate (and then they describe the process of catching the thief, which attracts the people sitting next to them to interject). When women meet women, they become eloquent, asking "Where are you going?" asking about their children and grandchildren, and maybe even saying a flattering sentence with a smile:

"Good fortune! Good fortune!"

That person then wiggles their pursed lips and smiles.

The leisurely old men twirling walnuts in their palms will ask the apprentice merchants about the market conditions, and when they hear that prices are rising again, they stroke their beards:

"This is terrible, people are going to lose their lives!"

First-class actors at least have a monthly chartered car; those who are mixed in here are mostly young actors who sing the first two or three acts. From the corners of their eyes and eyebrows and the expression in their speech, you can determine who sings the female role and who sings the painted face... "I have to rush to 'Zhonghe' tomorrow night!"

"What's scheduled for you?"

"The Mulberry Garden Meeting. You're the Caogiao Pass tonight, right?"

Having gotten used to playing female roles, even their daily speech and demeanor have a touch of femininity.

The butcher shop owner, covered in oil stains, dozes leaning against the window sill, drool seeping from the corner of his mouth; this is his rest. Children giggle at him, and some adults smile at the robust children in Boy Scout uniforms. The children still can't be quiet in the car, walking back and forth, bumping into people. Old women look at their thin, short clothes with trepidation:

"Aren't you cold, good children?"

At each stop, a few travelers get on and off. Newspaper vendors shout outside the tram window, selling small newspapers or evening papers for a large copper coin each. They are very lucky to receive the copper coin that is reached out from the tram.

The tram keeps going to the end, and people get off to go to their own destinations. The ticket seller gets off and waves to colleagues at the station.

The driver turns the tram around again.

The Task of a Writer of the Times

— Mei Junyi

Someone in the Chinese literary world once said: It's all as lonely as a desolate desert: there is no fragrance of lilacs or slenderness of lilies here. There is no melodious song of cuckoos or mournful chirping of cicadas. However, some have also said: The Chinese literary world is like a noisy market: there are all kinds of different playthings. There are "new era" "avant-garde" and "old bones" "enthusiasts." In short, it's dazzling, like a colorful market, each with its own goods, techniques, and means of deceiving customers.

All of this is true. From the perspective of quality: the "products" of the Chinese literary world, whose materials are "durable," "beautiful," and make people "look good" on, are simply as rare as phoenix feathers and unicorn horns. In terms of quantity, although there are not few "goods," and they are displayed in a dazzling array, they are all "counterfeit goods," "inferior goods," "old goods," and "untimely leftovers." There is very little that can truly suit the taste of the masses. Therefore, one only sees diversity without refinement.

Perhaps this is a reflection of a certain Chinese social phenomenon. Under deformed phenomena, deformed things will inevitably be produced.

However, as a writer of the times. He must see these phenomena clearly. See his own work and task clearly, and see the requirements, tastes, and needs of the reading public clearly.

In the barren and cluttered literary world, as a writer of the times, he should put in hard work, remove weeds, sweep away garbage, and use his heart to cultivate beautiful and robust flowers and fruits. This is the task of the gardener. Therefore, heroic struggle is necessary. Humble learning is essential. Diligent work is appropriate. The creation of a writer of an era's literature and art should and can "reflect the era," "inspire the era," and "advance the era," powerfully express the true meaning of life, and powerfully create new forms of life.

Miscellaneous Notes on War (12)

— Translation by Ye Yin from the work of Tokunaga Sunao

Brother Xiong was an extreme denier of war. The sparse beard that remained at that time was a souvenir of Brother Xiong's time in the military. He was a brave man who had served in both the Sino-Japanese War and the Russo-Japanese War, and the wounds on one hand and foot were received during the Battle of Shou Shan Fort.

The blue bronze leaf medal and more than one hundred yuan in bonuses became the price of a wife who lived together for a long time and one hand; Brother Xiong, who had few relatives, became a disabled person without a wife or children.

The taciturn Brother Xiong once told his father a story like this.

It was four or five days before the Battle of Shou Shan Fort. It was when they were marching all night to rescue the soldiers of the Third Company, which belonged to the same regiment on the front line. Just as everyone was advancing along the railway, passing through the sorghum fields, they heard incessant gunfire from afar.

Upon hearing the increasingly intense gunfire, everyone's brains, which had been as tired as cotton from the forced march of four or five days and insufficient food, felt a sense of tension as if being tightened, and they naturally felt as if the sound of their own footsteps was echoing on their eardrums.

"Halt!"

The company commander said in a sharp voice. Just as everyone was feeling baffled and stopped, on the distant front line, the "wah" cries that seemed to be from a charge suddenly covered up the gunfire and other sounds.

The company commander seemed to ponder for a while: but, after sending out five scouts, he immediately ordered the whole team to "step forward."

It was unknown whether those charging were the enemy or comrades: but the situation did seem to have reached a conclusion, and the gunfire gradually subsided.

After stepping over the sorghum fields in one breath, there was a slightly wider plain that was very uneven: on the right, you could see the rails shining lonely, and on the opposite side of the dark depression, sorghum fields were still undulating.

At this time, the shouts of many people, a kind of "wah wah" sound, came from more than three hundred meters ahead.

"Lie down!"

The company commander immediately shouted such a command; everyone prepared to lie down, waiting for the second order.

"Wah wah..."

However, this kind of sound, as it approached, made people feel really strange. The company commander was thinking like this: needless to say, this was not a charge; but, if it were the Japanese army, then there would naturally be no need to shout when retreating. At this time, two scouts ran back to report to him:

"The front line has been occupied by the enemy. The × and × companies seem to have been completely wiped out..."

The company commander looked into the distance at the approaching dark shadows of about one company of people, and seemed to have made up his mind, shouting the command to "lie down and prepare to fire"; he himself also held his bayonet tightly and lay down.

Gradually approaching from three hundred meters away, and walked to two hundred meters away... but, he did not issue a second order... What was laughable was that kind of shouting. It was not like that when the distance was far; but, once they got close, it was really... an energetic shout.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Russian Youth Gang Commits Crimes for Fun

— Xiaomin

According to a Reuters dispatch from Moscow on the 23rd, there is a gang of young people in Russia who specialize in committing crimes, and have even set up a general association to train children in the art of theft. The three leaders, all between the ages of eighteen and twenty, have all been discovered and executed. During the interrogation, according to the confessions of the individuals, they were not stealing because of poverty, but specifically to "have fun." Recently, the authorities have launched a large-scale crackdown on bandits throughout the country. In Leningrad alone, 4,000 bandits and 2,000 petty thieves have been arrested. Judging from this, there are indeed quite a few petty thieves and bandits in Russia.

Soviet Russia is a communist country. They have communal wives, communal property, communal care, and communal education. The social economy is completely centralized, and individuals have no savings whatsoever. There is absolutely no problem with food, clothing, shelter, and transportation. There are public places for games and entertainment. The people of other countries are clamoring about unemployment. According to the boasts of the Soviets, their workers are in a situation where demand exceeds supply. Therefore, being a Soviet Russian person is very much like working at sunrise and resting at sunset, not picking up things lost on the road, and not closing doors at night. Are they the people of the Wuhuai clan, or the people of the Getian clan? Although I have never been to Russia, my heart yearns for it.

Now, looking at the news reported above, it is completely beyond my expectations. The "fun" of young people generally consists of watching dramas and movies, playing ball, gambling, chasing the opposite sex, etc. I have never heard of using "theft" as a tool for "fun." Although our country is a communist country, its people do not have three heads and six arms, or different internal organs. I am afraid that they are the same as ordinary Eurasian people. Why is their "fun" so unique? When Mo Di saw the King of Chu, he asked the king, "Suppose there is someone who abandons their decorated carriage, and a neighbor has a dilapidated carriage that they want to steal; they abandon their brocade silk, and a neighbor has coarse clothing that they want to steal. What kind of person is this?" The king said, "This person must have a 'stealing disease.'" This is just a fable of Mozi's, but now I unexpectedly find that there are such people, which is really strange.

It can be seen that the Russian youth theft gang is definitely not "stealing" for "fun." It is either because of economic oppression or because of the unbearable pressure of political power. There is nothing to say, nothing that can be said, so they can only say that it is for "fun." This is the reality of communist people being forced to be unbearable by the communist government, which can already be generally seen. Moreover, in Leningrad alone, there are as many as 6,000 bandits and petty thieves, so the total number of bandits and petty thieves in the country can also be imagined.

Not only are the people of Russia like this, but even their government uses thieving methods. Since September 18th, Russia has taken advantage of...

Before the Abyss

— Chen Liang

The empty, gray-white garden path stretches windingly across the withered grassy beach, like the arm of an anemic woman thrown upon a dark yellow velvet blanket, making it appear even more haggard and pitiful. The low, dark green junipers are perpetually imprisoned within coarse, long black iron chains; whenever a branch grows particularly long or extends beyond the iron chains, it is savagely lopped off by a sharp blade. They grow forever under stern constraint, losing their ability to develop freely. Though they stand in neat rows, they are ultimately cripples, decorative objects grown solely to adorn the garden. Yet, in this winter when all vegetation has withered and died, only the junipers can withstand the ravages of the seasonal winds, revealing a verdant and thriving color.

"Plants of endurance!" Having walked the length of the junipers and their parallel line of black iron chains, I quietly breathed a sigh of empathy from my brooding chest. The sky was overcast, threatening rain, and large masses of gray-white clouds drifted swiftly by. Alas, is not my own state of mind like this overcast sky, constantly crowded with layers of melancholy clouds, with depression and gloom entrenched in my inspiration, misty and difficult to dispel? I stood blankly beneath the Chinese juniper at the edge of the garden path, when three or four children, laughing and hopping, ran past me, so lively, like white doves fluttering in the breeze. This momentary image pierced my throat like a juniper branch, causing a sharp pain. Thinking of my own vanished childhood, a quiet surge of sorrow for the passage of time welled up.

Moving with languid steps, I crossed the grassy ground that resembled a dark yellow velvet blanket and arrived at the edge of the stream. The stream water flowed past indifferently under my melancholic gaze—

Time! Time flows like the stream water, time is like the shadows of wisps of clouds on the water surface, comprehending the rise and fall of so many things, those stars, seasons, bodies, loves, careers, green herbs, and roses! Awakening to all the occasional fleeting moments of existence. Should the youth of the end of the century be in a period of hibernation? Otherwise, unable to bear the melancholy and loneliness, they will degenerate into a dissolute and unrestrained life. Very well, the water must always flow, stagnant water will breed foul odors and mosquitoes. Young people; junipers, in this cold atmosphere, only the young can endure the pressures of the environment. I looked at the stream, I looked at my own reflection in the stream, and said, "Endure!"

Endure, endure in adversity! Every moment of silence is but an opportunity for a fruit to ripen, and unexpected encounters will always come. A breeze, a white dove, a lightly leaning young woman, all the slightest of tremors will give the afflicted a sense of effortless joy.

In a moment of confusion, I felt vaguely that I was lying before an abyss, dreaming a lukewarm and dry dream – this dream was vague, like duckweed floating in a dark abyss, seemingly drifting with the tide every hour, east or west? Completely losing my own will. However, this was certainly not a dream, but a real situation, this world, this life, an abyss, a dream. I hesitated before the stream. I felt that the steady flow of water was too meaningless. I wanted to pick up a stone and throw it into the surface of the water to splash some water, but the brave and upright park guard kept watching me. "Perhaps this would violate some regulation!" So, I lost this courage, and finally dragged my slow steps, still along the row of junipers and black iron chains, and limped out of the park gate. "Plants of endurance!" I still breathed a sigh quietly from my brooding chest.

Rapeseed Flowers Yellow

— Mu

Mid-February is the most leisurely time for farmers. The beans and wheat in the fields, and the boundless rapeseed flowers, surge like gold with a gust of gentle wind. In this kind of warm and sunny weather, most farmers, after eating lunch, go to the teahouse to chat. Even the few who cut green grass by the mountains to feed livestock rest from time to time, casually singing love songs of "Sister, my love." The goat herding girls also sing along without any embarrassment. The singing seems to never stop from morning to night.

Near the mountains is Yan Village, which is actually named after Yan Mountain; it is said to be a mountain, but it is only a slightly larger earth mound. Green grass is everywhere, and a dozen or so goats wander under the sun. The goat herding girl lies in the shade of the mountain, messing around with the grass-cutting man, and laughter and songs are sent to every corner by the spring breeze.

At the foot of the mountain, a clear stream surrounds half of Yan Village. Near the place where the village is about to exit, is the home of Old Lady Wang. Her daughter-in-law, wearing a serge jacket and pants, squats by the river washing diapers, as if too lazy, and several diapers have not been finished for half a day. Suddenly, her name is called from inside the house. She knows that it is time for the child to wake up and eat milk. She abandons the work in her hands and runs home nimbly. Her mother-in-law, Old Lady Wang, with an unnatural expression on her face, hands the child to her, muttering and goes into the room to chant Buddhist scriptures. She coaxes the child to drink milk, and her eyes involuntarily look along the stream: that place is where she and her husband pledged their love. She is the goat herding girl from the opposite village. Because the green grass of Yan Mountain is abundant, she comes here every day from the opposite village. In this way, she met a young man, and this pile of earth mounds became closely related to her.

It was during the season when the rapeseed flowers turned yellow last year that they got married. The wedding was exceptionally lively. Relatives and neighbors from both villages rudely made a ruckus in the bridal chamber until midnight, making all kinds of gestures they had made while flirting on Yan Mountain to win her coquettish smiles. The situation seemed to extend for four or five days.

In less than three months, she was pregnant. During the busy farming season, her husband always secretly came back once or twice to visit. When neighbors met them, they spread the news throughout the village as a joke. On the one hand, she felt ashamed, and on the other hand, she had an unspeakable joy.

Spring unknowingly passed away, and her happy days also disappeared like a flash in the pan. The cruel summer

Page 18

day took away her husband. The former relatives and friends have all become enemies, and even her mother-in-law, who loved her so much, often cursed her on the street, calling her a jinx. A wife who has lost her husband is considered an unlucky person in the countryside.

From then on, she was squeezed into hell. She did not dare to leave the bedroom a step. She feared countless snake-tongue-like gazes. But endless, untrue gossip still poured into her ears every day. Sometimes her mother-in-law deliberately talked loudly to people, and the sound of the jinx was so harsh, even saying that she did not keep her chastity. Therefore, her only hope was the piece of flesh in her belly. She swallowed her tears and gave birth to a boy.

The countryside naturally values ​​boys over girls. Having given birth to a boy, she was given importance. But this was not her hope. She hoped that the child would grow up, and she poured all the love she had for her husband into the child...

But the second rapeseed flower season came. The songs of Yan Mountain are sent every day. She saw pairs of butterflies fluttering among the rapeseed flowers. The child in her arms only knew how to drink milk and sleep. She often stood still and shed tears in private. This distant hope cannot fill the loneliness before her. The lonely years of a widow!

Ascending North Peak

— Baishan

Having come out of the Yue Wang Temple, we had lunch at a small restaurant next to the Bixue Danxin stone archway. This is all that the lake tour guide told us, and the half-day tour ends here.

With a full stomach, I really wanted to pluck up the courage to run up to Lingyin, but I was afraid that, as the guide said, I would not be able to ascend North Peak. Tourists pouring out of the restaurant were all on the same trip as us. When the bus stopped in front of the Yue Wang Temple, they scrambled to stuff the bus until it could hardly breathe. The straps for hanging on to in the bus were not enough to be distributed, but there was no need to worry, even if the bus turned and swayed, everyone was already like a sandwiched board, and there was absolutely no danger of not being able to stand firm.

The bus traveled for about ten minutes and arrived at Lingyin Temple. The crowd entered the temple through many stalls, passing through a long stone pedestrian path, on both sides of which were also stalls selling miscellaneous items such as prayer beads and sachets. Dear husbands always buy prayer beads for their wives to hang on their chests. This kind of disharmonious image, as long as you go for a walk on Bai Causeway at sunset, is full of modern women with yellow bags for pilgrimage. Even our group of three, in that kind of military training uniform, are not people who can be found in temples at ordinary times. Therefore, the villas with red tiles and Western-style decorations are built on the shores of the lightly powdered eyebrow West Lake, and everyone thinks it is a necessary embellishment.

Our purpose was to climb the mountain, so we also bought three climbing sticks. Entering the grand and majestic Great Hero Hall, the incense smoke there almost made people fall into a dense fog. Entering the Arhat Hall also made us shed tears: although one of our companions asked about the well where Ji Gong raised wood to build the temple, everyone hurriedly went to Taoguang on the left side.

Moving forward along the stone steps, there are tens of thousands of bamboos on both sides, and the sound of gurgling water can be heard. Upon closer inspection, it is the mountain spring that has trickled down from the split bamboo. Near Taoguang Temple, countless bamboo branches were found with words such as ×× releasing life engraved on them. This thing is still a mystery to this day. If we had asked the old ladies with yellow bags at that time, they would definitely have told us a long history; but none of us wanted to do this. When we rested in front of Taoguang Temple, everyone used this as conversation material, and the result was naturally still equal to zero. However, I secretly thought that if there was a chance to revisit in the future, this unanswered guess could still stir our interest: moreover, knowing a little less is not necessarily the happiness of being a human being. I personally think so.

On the way up North Peak, we met many devout Maoshan Taoists. They all sat cross-legged on the corner of the road, without looking askance, and tapped the wooden fish rhythmically. The bamboo basket in front of them was filled with double-cent copper coins given by pilgrims, which was quite considerable. Becoming a monk is indeed a supreme way to relieve unemployment. Along the way, there are many sugarcane stalls, and the prices are very expensive, but they have climbed so many stone steps to seek high profits. Compared with the Maoshan Taoists who gain without labor, I always feel that these people are too pitiful. However, many of the ladies who take mountain sedan chairs to cultivate good fortune haggle with those vendors, and the scene is very much like the situation of weighing catty by catty in a small vegetable market in Shanghai.

Arriving at North Peak, the area near Hangzhou can be seen at a glance; that green jade belt with fishing sails coming and going in between, is the Qiantang River. Confronting it is South Peak. It is a pity that I did not bring the guide book, otherwise, if someone pointed out something, there might be more excitement. After a while, the red sun set in the west, and the Qiantang River was reflected in golden splendor, as if hundreds of thousands of small golden snakes were surging from the bottom of the water. If we could stay here overnight and watch the sunrise, there would be an even more wonderful sight.

Before leaving, everyone drew a lottery stick. Mine was the best of the best, and the Bodhisattva told me that I had a long way to go and to take good care of myself!

Scattered Strings of the Lion River

— Ding Weinan

My own life has been one of constant destitution, going east one moment, west the next, like drifting clouds in the sky. For the sake of friends, relatives, and even family, I was urgently pressed time and again to quickly set off and return to this place, our true hometown. Although it is thirty or forty *li* away from the land where I was born, it is still my hometown!

A leaping automobile carried me back to my Lion River. Several years had passed since I last saw it. Though it had been seven or eight years, familiar outlines were still deeply etched in my mind and could be recognized, even if some forms had changed. Back when I was a child, this place was known as a hub connecting eight provinces. Even seven or eight years ago, before life threw me into destitution, there were still many newly rich upstarts. The narrow streets overflowed with crowds of people. But now, it has transformed into a different scene, like a consumptive patient supporting itself with its own bones.

Refugees unable to return home wander the streets, eyes blank, waiting for good news.

Business is extremely slow. In cloth shops, very few people step inside during the course of a long day. The shop assistants are bored to death. But since the shop is open, there must be business. Everyone has to rest their hands on the counter, watching the passersby on the street with eager eyes. Many shops have changed owners, naturally after several vicissitudes. Several old established shops, relying on the capital earned in previous years, painfully persevere to this day, luckily avoiding closure, but their vitality is greatly diminished. Though they have large storefronts, the pain of carrying the ashes of disaster can only be understood by a mute who has tasted *huanglian* (bitter root).

It's truly strange, yet not at all surprising. A place that used to be known for its rice is now expensive, over ten *yuan* per *shi*. The poor cry out in misery. Many farmers cannot return to farming, leaving fertile land to fall into desolation. My own erratic movements and the transgressions of recent years have hastened the collapse of the countryside!

The boats on the river also have little business. The masts that once stood in a forest along the riverbank are now so sparse. I heard that many boatmen have changed professions because roads have reached into the interior. The reeds still stand on Monk Island, while the houses of families across the river reveal a scene of disarray and disintegration! The broad river water rolls down the beach in a vast expanse, and the gray-white sky seems unable to contain the desolation here.

Amateur Mailbox

How to Find Amusement in Leisure Time!

To the Editor:

We have a question of utmost importance to personal life, a serious issue concerning the lives of ordinary people, and we seek your advice, hoping you can provide us with clear guidance.

We all work at a bank, and we are off on Saturday afternoons and Sundays. After a week of intense work, we naturally want to seek entertainment during this time of respite. However, we see our colleagues spending their time off watching movies, playing cards, or even dancing until late at night before returning home. This kind of life is simply unacceptable. Although some are better, very few can find proper entertainment to spend their days off.

We feel that after working to the point of extreme fatigue, we need entertainment to regulate our monotonous lives. However, we certainly don't want to do what others do, like watching plays, dog racing, or engaging in reckless card games. At the same time, we find it difficult to find what we consider suitable entertainment, so we end up staying at home on our days off, reading books, and feeling utterly bored and frustrated all day long.

Sir, we believe that there must be many people in our situation today. We feel that many young people are going down the path of depravity because they can't find proper entertainment, and this is very dangerous!

For our own sake and for the sake of others, we are writing this letter to you, hoping that you can guide us on how to find proper pastimes to recover from the fatigue of work. Respectfully,

Wen Yangqiu

Lu Dianchen (same as above)

Cheng Long

Editor's Note: The question about leisure entertainment raised by the three gentlemen, Wen, Lu, and Cheng, is indeed a serious one of utmost importance to the lives of ordinary people.

The purpose of entertainment is to provide us with a means to soothe our minds and spirits and to soothe our moods after we have become mentally and physically fatigued. Because a person is busy from morning to night, leading to both mental and physical fatigue and lack of energy, entertainment can invigorate our spirits, promote our physical health, and help us forget the fatigue of work. At the same time, proper entertainment can prevent the erosion of ambition, prevent depravity, and increase work efficiency to achieve career advancement.

Since the meaning and effect of entertainment are so great, what kind of entertainment can be considered proper? We can see that Shanghai is so extravagant and the environment is so terrible, but what ordinary people consider to be entertainment is playing cards, horse racing, dog racing, smoking, drinking, whoring, and so on. Is this our proper entertainment? No! These things only waste our time, wear out our spirits, and waste our money. This kind of entertainment is luring us down the path of depravity. In the past and at present, countless young people have been seduced by it and have fallen.

There are many kinds of proper entertainment. Here are a few easy to implement, for general reference.

(1) Exercise—Exercise can make the body strong, energetic, and refreshed. But we are not limited to large sports venues to exercise. In the morning, we can do morning exercises in a place with fresh air, or after work, take a walk in a quieter place, or find a place to play ball. These are all exercises.

(2) Music—It has great magic. It can make people feel happy and relaxed, and it can cultivate one's character. Music is indeed the best tool for regulating the spirit. In one's spare time after work, fiddling with it at will is truly full of infinite interest.

(3) Travel—Travel is an even more amazing form of entertainment. During the journey, we admire the beautiful scenery of nature, and we can gain a lot of knowledge that books don't provide. Although long-term travel is not possible, it is a good thing to be able to invite a few friends to run around in the nearby countryside during breaks.

(4) Watching plays—Some people say that watching plays is not proper entertainment. I cannot agree with this statement. I believe that plays with corrupt content or improper content are not worth seeing, but it is okay to watch plays with beautiful performances, edifying abilities, and correct themes. Because it can cultivate the mind and body, regulate the spirit, and give you a lot of experience and knowledge.

In addition, reading newspapers and books, photography, chess, hunting, etc. are all very interesting and proper entertainments, but due to space constraints, I cannot read them in detail.

Finally, we hope that this group of people can reform their past bad habits, avoid past boring behaviors, and choose one or two proper entertainments in pursuit of a perfect life. As for which type of entertainment your economic environment allows you to do, you must decide for yourself.

Opening "Spring Sorrow Tune"

The slanting sun enters the courtyard, piercing cold rises. In the empty, silent embroidered chamber, the treasure censer is warm. Reluctant to part, longing for spring, spring has grown old. Gradually, dream shadows are enough to dissipate the soul. Listless and ill, too lazy to put on makeup. Head drooping from wine, unable to bear being thin. Thinking of last night, when the lamp wick had just brought good news. But the joyous occasion is shallow and vague. How lovely the parrot, earnest, reciting poetry haltingly. But the swallow, sincere, telling of its sorrow again and again. Already the twenty-four seasonal flowers send messages. Only catkins and willow floss block the gauze window. I remember being carefree, the library quiet behind the curtain. I sent the sound of chess pieces being placed. I remember picking at the thirteen-stringed zither. The sound is as smooth as jade and as round as pearls. I remember peering with drunken eyes from behind the screen. The jade-like person awakes, the phoenix hairpin lying horizontal. That day, I hurriedly covered my sleeves on the Yangguan Road. The horse slipped, the fog dense, under the moon. Now I wish to send the luxuriant grass on the riverbank. To carry my sorrow straight to the short and long pavilions. I am only left with tailors like bees and butterflies, idle and listless. Stealing rouge to embrace the falling blossoms. Gazing until my eyes can no longer see the green of the smoke and water by the bridge. This year in the hall north of Botang, I tread on the remnants of spring. Resenting the Eastern Emperor for being so wasteful.

Supplement to the *Shen Bao* Local Edition, Film Special

Ushers in Theaters Also Have Hope of Becoming Movie Stars

— Yiji

We commonly call them "seat watchers" or "usher," but every time we mention these "seat watchers," especially the ushers in major Shanghai theaters, we can't help but feel a bit of a headache, because their methods of extorting small favors are endless. What with melon seeds, fruit, handkerchiefs, they simply take more than the ticket price. And these people are so deeply entrenched that there is no way to eradicate them. But what we are going to talk about now is not this kind of person with thick eyebrows and large eyes, hands on hips, waiting fiercely for you to take out your wallet, smiling broadly as soon as their dark eyes see the colorful bills. We want to talk about the young men who shave their beards cleanly, wear neat uniforms, hold flashlights, and politely lead you to your seat after taking your ticket at the entrance of the movie theater. We want to distinguish them from the old-style ushers used in theaters, so we call them "ushers."

These ushers are also theater staff or workers. They earn their living with wages and do not need to extort or blackmail, so although they cannot be said to be respected, they are not annoying. Douglas Fairbanks used to be one of them. The late Rudolph Valentino was also one of them. George Raft used to be one of them. These three popular and handsome young men, unexpectedly, all came from movie theater ushers. There are also many other male and female stars, so of course this is worth mentioning.

Before Ramon Novarro was discovered by the great director Rex Ingram and filmed "The Prisoner of Zenda," he was an usher at the Grauman's Broadstreet Theatre in Los Angeles. But who knew him then? He led hundreds or thousands of viewers to their seats every day, for many weeks and months. But who knew that this dark-skinned Mexican youth would one day shine brighter than the flashlight in his hand and become a star in the film firmament?

At that time, Rudolph Valentino was already extremely popular. His star had risen to an unprecedented height. He was the idol worshipped by millions of women. Thousands of theaters were vying for his works. His fame surpassed the speed of the Four Horsemen and spread throughout the world. Many anecdotes arose from this, some of which were true and some of which were unfounded. But in the end, two things are certain. One is that he used to be a bus driver. One is that he used to be a movie theater usher.

In the history of every career, there are many romances that can be talked about after tea and wine. However, the fact that these two great stars, Valentino and Ramon Novarro, both came from the same movie theater usher is also one of the talking points in film history. But the strangeness of the matter does not stop there.

On the eve of the filming of the great director Ingram's "The Prisoner of Zenda," Ingram suddenly quarreled with Valentino. Valentino was originally a person promoted by Ingram himself. Ingram was so angry with him that he vowed to create another male star of the same caliber. And because Valentino was just an ordinary usher in a theater, he suddenly remembered Ramon Novarro, an usher at the Grauman's Broadstreet Theatre who had a strong desire for film but was unable to find a way. He immediately called Ramon and resolutely decided to cast him as the protagonist of "The Prisoner of Zenda." His anger towards Valentino made him even more hopeful for Ramon Novarro. Sure enough, Ingram had magical skills and created a shining new star in no time.

Ramon Novarro's speed of ascent even followed in the footsteps of his predecessor. Within a few months, he became Valentino's rival. They were competing to be the biggest lover on the screen. In this way, a Mexican man caused women all over the United States to be in a state of infatuation and unease, and the entire film industry was filled with an atmosphere of Latin romance, which also made the average men follow suit.

How did they have this ability to win over women? How could they deeply understand women's psychology? It turns out that it was because they had been movie theater ushers. When they were ushers, they first came into contact with the audience and learned what kind of men they liked to see on the screen. In the halls and aisles, they heard the general public's criticism of men more clearly than others. Day after day, watching and listening, they were influenced by what they saw and heard, and over time, the movements of male stars on the screen that could win the public's favor were imprinted in their minds, so that they could perform with extraordinary skill.

This is not empty talk. Let's take another handsome young man as proof. George Raft is one of them. He is not Mexican, nor is he Italian, but he looks just like Valentino, so his style also followed the past Italian lover. But he used to be an usher at the Capitol Theater in New York. Isn't his "The Trumpet Blows" the same flavor as Valentino's "Blood and Sand"? In this way, the theater is actually a vocational school for creating movie stars. Therefore, I advise the average usher not to underestimate their position. They can say this... Shun was also a man, and I am also a man, so why should I fear him?

Audience Opinions

Impressions After Watching "Escape"

— Mao Di

"Escape" is an excellent work with a sound consciousness that strives to expose reality. Needless to say, the playwright's purpose is to oppose imperialism and resist Japan, while at the same time reflecting the painful situation of these refugees escaping in hardship under the oppression of imperialism.

On the vast desert, many refugees who were both frozen and starved, with no home to return to, were wandering. They had nowhere to go in front and no way back behind. The miserable situation of their颠沛 and hardship would make anyone who saw them feel sad, angry, and tearful!

Other things, such as the depiction of opportunistic philanthropists who only lightly moved a few beads on the abacus with the relief money they raised, and then safely pocketed it; the wanton enjoyment of playboys and the trampling of women; and the fact that refugees could not get thin porridge but were beaten instead, all made people feel indignant and aroused their passionate blood, wishing to take those scoundrels one by one and "stab them with white knives and pull them out with red knives."

But in the end, Wang Yin's慷慨激昂 speech and the refugees taking up hoes and spades to go to the front line to reclaim lost land became an unimportant ending.

The director's method is very skillful, and half of it must also be attributed to the authenticity of the background, such as the big fire and the escape, and a few small places where comparisons are made are also quite touching.

The skillful acting skills of several actors naturally helped the progress of the plot and made it even more colorful: however, the two songs seemed to be forcibly inserted.

We can say this: "Escape" has the flavor of "The Highway," but the former stimulates people more deeply than the latter.

Reflections After Seeing "Escape"

— Dai

I admit that the script of "Escape" is realistic. Especially at a time when the entire nation is numb and insensitive to pain, completely forgetting the loss of thousands of miles of Northeast territory in the September 18th Incident and the destruction of Zhabei in the January 28th Incident, this script is particularly needed.

"Escape" begins by unfolding a picture of the nomadic life of farmers beyond the Great Wall, making us feel that this life is much purer than the noise of urban life. Unconsciously, we are filled with envy and a desire to experience this kind of life. However, this picture is eventually torn to pieces by the enemy's planes and artillery, and the farmers who lived and worked in peace are transformed into homeless refugees. Who has inflicted this pain upon us?

The men and women in the countryside show such filial piety in serving the elderly. Even in the midst of escape, they struggle desperately to protect their elderly fathers. The love between siblings and the righteousness among neighbors all make urban audiences feel inferior!

"Escape" also depicts how, in the midst of their flight, some villains with no regard for human life exploit the refugees' homelessness to abduct and seduce respectable young women, just as there were traitors who worked for the enemy during the Battle of Zhabei. Such inhumane behavior is so hateful!

While charities cannot be entirely dismissed, at least some of them use charity as a pretext to enrich themselves and abuse their power. "Escape" ruthlessly exposes the ugly face of these fake philanthropists.

Finally, "Escape" clearly reveals to us that the enemy is advancing step by step, and our only response is to flee and rely on charities. This is not our way out. Our only way out is to fearlessly reclaim our lost territories.

Undoubtedly, "Escape" still has many unsatisfactory aspects in terms of directing and acting. However, we believe that the scriptwriting is conscious, and it cannot be compared with those film scripts that are indifferent to pain and unable to address China's problems.

Reflections on "Escape"

— Hengguang

Today, when imperialists are rampant and brutally seizing our country's territory with planes and artillery, the presentation of "Escape" is indeed a work that exposes reality.

The impression "Escape" gives to the audience is hatred for the ferocity of imperialism and disgust for the cruelty of war. The fact that it arouses anti-imperialist and anti-war sentiments is the success of "Escape." But unfortunately, at a time when the rural economy is bankrupt, there are tens of thousands of unemployed people escaping, and many disaster victims wandering. This widespread reality of escape is a fact that the screenwriter of "Escape" has not paid attention to.

As for the editing of the "Escape" theme, the appropriateness of the exposure, the round and passionate acting, and the rare outdoor scenes, these are all worth noting and praising. Furthermore, the exposure of Hui Shan's false mask, the ease with which girl scouts raise donations, the refugees' destruction of Dong's mansion showing the greatness of the power of the masses, and the misery of the refugees' lives are all cleverly and appropriately exposed.

The Story of Carole Lombard's "Heart Laugh" in "The Runaway Bride"

— Guocheng

Now, "The Runaway Bride," starring Carole Lombard, is showing in Nanjing, and what is recorded below is a story about Lombard's personal "laugh."

This incident happened in 1924. It was a terrible car accident in which the car was wrecked, and Lombard was sitting in the car. As a result, she suffered very serious injuries. Her face and neck were bleeding a lot, and her life was in great danger. At that time, the doctors were also worried about her, fearing that even if she did not die, she would become a person with a facial disfigurement for the rest of her life.

She lived alone in the hospital and felt very painful mentally, especially when someone came into her room and saw her strange appearance with many bandages wrapped around her head, face, and neck. She knew that they would leave and talk about her behind her back. She was determined to restore her original appearance. So she didn't care about anything and spent her days thinking about many happy and interesting things in her heart; but she couldn't laugh out loud, because if she laughed, it would cause her facial muscles to move, and this muscle movement would be detrimental to her wounds, or it would cause her skin to crack.

There was only one way, that is, when her friends told her some funny things, she would try to learn a so-called "heart laugh," without moving the expression on her face. She spent eight months like this, and her friends simply couldn't figure out her temperament.

Later, she recovered from her injuries and came out of the hospital! Can you know what the first thing she did was? That is: she used all her strength to laugh heartily. Because it had been so long since she had laughed out loud with her face and mouth!

Movie Novel

India's National Humiliation (Clive Of India) (11)

— Maode

While Clive was talking to Governor Pigot, he suddenly heard an Indian woman selling mangoes outside, wailing. He was suddenly touched and hurried out. The governor followed behind. Clive went outside and asked Captain Clark what the ragged old woman wanted. Clark said, "She has been here all afternoon and refuses to leave. She keeps saying that the mangoes on the other side of the river are better than the ones here, and I don't know what she means." Clive listened and suddenly had an idea. He smiled and glanced at the governor, then led the woman to the front of his tent. The governor and Edmund followed.

When the woman arrived in front of the tent, she respectfully offered Clive a basket of mangoes. Edmund shouted from the side, "Robert, don't touch it, it might be poisonous!" But Clive spoke in fluent Hindustani and talked to the old woman. The old woman then walked back to Clive's side and took out a pair of slippers from under the basket of mangoes and placed them in Clive's hands. Clive took the slippers and told Clark to give her more money and send her away.

Clive held the slippers in his hand and felt around them, then took out a small knife and cut open the sole of one of the shoes, pulling out a piece of paper from inside. He winked at the governor and Edmund, and they all went into the tent. Clive opened the piece of paper and saw that it was a secret letter from Mir Jafar, which read: "Cross the river quickly. If possible, I will join you with 30,000 men. I haven't dared to move yet. Cross the river quickly. Issue the attack order. When possible, I will come and join you."

"If possible... Wait until it's possible..." Clive muttered to himself. Governor Pigot suddenly shouted, "No doubt! It must be a trick! The monsoon is about to start. Once the monsoon starts, the tide will rise, and you will have a strong enemy in front of you and a flood behind you. At that time, you will be caught in a trap!" Clive also muttered to himself, "That's right, that's right." The governor then waved his hand and told Edmund to retreat immediately. He also instructed Clive, "Colonel Clive, you must not cross the river! If Mir Jafar does not come to join you, you will have 60,000 infantry and 20,000 cavalry to fight against you. You only have 800 British troops and 2,000 native troops. You must not risk the lives of all of us on a single gamble... Besides, your wife is also among them!"

Clive said blankly, "Do you think I don't know that? I ask you, have I ever been defeated?" The governor hesitated and did not answer immediately. The monsoon may not come for two days... The opportunity is not completely lost... He then said, "First send a letter to Mir Jafar, telling him to bring his troops to meet here before the heavy rain. Otherwise, the treaty will be cancelled. This is my final order!" As he spoke, he frowned and said to Clive, "I'm going back now. Do you have anything to say or any letter to take to your wife?" Clive said, "I don't have time to write a letter. Please tell her that I have reached a crossroads. She will understand when she hears it... I really want to see her." The governor said, "I will deliver this message in person." As he said this, he said goodnight to Clive and walked out.

After the governor left, Edmund came in. Clive sighed and said, "Edmund, it seems like everyone in the world is against me. I ask you... you tell me..." As he spoke, he sighed again, because Edmund hesitated and didn't speak, but his meaning was clearly expressed. Clive then walked alone to the front of the tent and stared blankly at the vast river in front of him. (To be continued)
